# Life Operating System

## Overview
- **Date**: 2026-05-29 09:22:19
- **Conversation ID**: `6a19a0be-9ae8-83ea-aad7-2645e54245b3`
- **Source**: `Chat-Export-28513-2026/conversations-008.json`

## Chat History

### User
> lets not pussy foot around what i really need anymore, i need a life app, task management, task buckets, tasklists or projects, that map to people, that group by areas, transactions logs, in or out from where to where for whome do they owe me or do i owe them, smart ai to cut through te noise, help me make tasks update them, etc. add update contacts, and keep me organized with daily schedules.

### Assistant
> Yes. This is the real app. Not “tasks,” not “notes,” not “finance,” not “contacts” separately — one operating system with people, money, work, obligations, and AI sitting on top cutting through the fog.

### Assistant
> Cody, the truth: you do **not** need another task app.
> 
> You need a **Life Operating System**.
> 
> Not cute productivity bullshit. A command center.
> 
> ## The app is: QiNexus / QiLife OS
> 
> Working name options:
> 
> **QiNexus**
> Best if this becomes the big system.
> 
> **QiLife**
> Best if this is the daily personal app.
> 
> **QiOps**
> Best if this is the practical operations layer.
> 
> My vote: **QiNexus is the platform. QiLife is the daily app.**
> 
> ---
> 
> # Core Doctrine
> 
> Everything important becomes one of these objects:
> 
> | Object | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | **Person** | Human, company, agency, court, vendor, client, household member |
> | **Area** | Life domain: legal, finance, household, work, caregiving, tech, personal |
> | **Project / Tasklist** | A container of related work |
> | **Task** | Action that needs doing |
> | **Transaction** | Money/value movement in or out |
> | **Obligation** | Someone owes someone something |
> | **Event** | Calendar/schedule item |
> | **Note / Log** | Context, receipt, journal, evidence, update |
> | **Document** | File, PDF, image, contract, bill, court order |
> | **AI Summary** | System-generated clarity layer |
> 
> That’s the whole game.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The key move
> 
> Stop separating “tasks,” “projects,” and “people.”
> 
> A task should be able to say:
> 
> > Call Marion County Clerk about surplus check  
> > Area: Legal / Finance  
> > People: Cody, Marion County Clerk  
> > Related money: expected incoming check  
> > Related document: order granting release  
> > Status: waiting  
> > Next action date: Monday  
> > AI note: “Do not spiral. Call only if mail has not arrived by expected date.”
> 
> That’s the system you need.
> 
> Not 14 apps pretending they integrate.
> 
> ---
> 
> # MVP Modules
> 
> ## 1. Inbox
> 
> One universal capture box.
> 
> Everything starts here:
> 
> - random thought
> - task
> - bill
> - screenshot
> - receipt
> - court note
> - mom request
> - Zai thing
> - Lyft issue
> - “someone owes me”
> - “I owe this”
> - “don’t forget”
> - “figure this out later”
> 
> Then AI helps classify it.
> 
> Example:
> 
> > “Zai owes me 40 for gas from yesterday”
> 
> AI creates:
> 
> - Person: Zai
> - Transaction/Obligation: Zai owes Cody $40
> - Area: Finance / Household
> - Status: open
> - Due: unset
> - Optional task: “Ask Zai about gas money”
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. People
> 
> This is not just contacts.
> 
> Each person gets a mini-dashboard:
> 
> ### Person: Zai
> 
> - Contact info
> - Relationship/context
> - Shared projects
> - Open tasks involving him
> - Money owed to/from him
> - Agreements
> - Notes
> - Related documents
> - Recent activity
> 
> Same for:
> 
> - Mom
> - Comfort Keepers
> - Marion County Clerk
> - landlords
> - attorneys
> - vendors
> - clients
> - banks
> - apps
> - creditors
> 
> This is where the app becomes powerful.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Areas
> 
> Areas are your top-level life domains.
> 
> Use your existing doctrine:
> 
> 1. Inbox  
> 2. Workbench  
> 3. Timeline  
> 4. Life  
> 5. People  
> 6. Business  
> 7. Finance  
> 8. Legal  
> 9. Tech  
> 10. Assets  
> 11. Data  
> 12. Reference  
> 13. Archive  
> 14. System  
> 
> But for the daily app, simplify the visible areas:
> 
> - Today
> - People
> - Money
> - Legal
> - Household
> - Work
> - Tech
> - Documents
> - Waiting On
> - Someday / Parked
> 
> The backend can stay beautifully structured. The UI should not make you stare at the whole cathedral every morning.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. Projects / Tasklists
> 
> Projects are just major task containers.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - Surplus Check Recovery
> - Jeep Repair Plan
> - Rental Car Renewal
> - Mom Care Notes System
> - Family Operating System
> - QiFinance Intake
> - QiServer Cleanup
> - Zai Lease Agreement
> - Lyft Income Sprint
> - Phone Replacement
> 
> Each project has:
> 
> - Area
> - People
> - Tasks
> - Money links
> - Documents
> - Notes/logs
> - Status
> - Priority
> - Next action
> - AI summary
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. Tasks
> 
> Task fields should be practical, not overbuilt.
> 
> Minimum fields:
> 
> | Field | Example |
> |---|---|
> | title | Call clerk about check |
> | status | open / waiting / done / blocked |
> | priority | urgent / normal / low |
> | area | Legal |
> | project | Surplus Check Recovery |
> | people | Marion County Clerk |
> | due date | 2026-06-03 |
> | next action | call after mail arrives |
> | energy | low / medium / high |
> | location | phone / home / errands / computer |
> | notes | clerk said check mailed Friday |
> | related money | incoming surplus check |
> | related documents | court order PDF |
> 
> The **location/energy** fields matter because ADHD task lists fail when they ignore context.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. Money / Transaction Log
> 
> This needs to be a ledger, not a budgeting toy.
> 
> Core transaction structure:
> 
> | Field | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | date | when it happened |
> | from_account/person | source |
> | to_account/person | destination |
> | amount | money/value |
> | direction | in / out / transfer |
> | category | gas, rent, legal, food |
> | area | Finance / Household / Work |
> | person | who it involves |
> | project | optional |
> | status | pending / cleared / disputed |
> | evidence | receipt, screenshot, note |
> | obligation_link | if someone owes someone |
> 
> Examples:
> 
> ### Zai paid rent
> 
> From: Zai  
> To: Cody  
> Amount: $450  
> Category: Rent  
> Area: Household / Finance  
> Project: Zai Lease  
> Status: cleared  
> 
> ### Cody paid gas for Lyft
> 
> From: Cody Cash App  
> To: Gas Station  
> Amount: $35  
> Category: Fuel  
> Area: Work / Finance  
> Project: Lyft Income Sprint  
> Status: cleared  
> 
> ### Mom reimburses groceries
> 
> From: Mom  
> To: Cody  
> Amount: $83.12  
> Category: Groceries  
> Area: Household / Finance  
> Status: pending or cleared  
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 7. Obligations
> 
> This is the missing piece most apps don’t handle.
> 
> An obligation is not always a transaction yet.
> 
> It means:
> 
> > Someone owes someone something.
> 
> Could be money, document, decision, task, reply, ride, payment, signature, reimbursement.
> 
> Fields:
> 
> | Field | Example |
> |---|---|
> | owed_by | Zai |
> | owed_to | Cody |
> | type | money |
> | amount | $40 |
> | reason | gas |
> | due date | Friday |
> | status | open |
> | related transaction | optional |
> | evidence | screenshot/text/log |
> | linked task | “remind Zai” |
> 
> This is how the app answers:
> 
> - Who owes me money?
> - Who do I owe?
> - What am I waiting on?
> - What promises exist?
> - What needs follow-up?
> 
> That’s gold.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 8. Daily Command Center
> 
> This is the page you actually use.
> 
> It should show only:
> 
> ## Today
> 
> - Scheduled events
> - Due tasks
> - Must-do money moves
> - Waiting-on follow-ups
> - Errands by location
> - AI-generated “focus list”
> 
> Example:
> 
> ### Today’s Actual Priority
> 
> 1. Finish 11 Lyft rides  
> 2. Keep phone mounted safely  
> 3. Do not burn money on low-priority errands  
> 4. Track gas/rental costs  
> 5. Check mail for surplus only if timing makes sense  
> 
> Then:
> 
> ### Noise
> 
> - Redesigning homepage
> - Reorganizing old files
> - Perfecting finance schema
> - Fixing every system today
> 
> Translation: not today, babe.
> 
> ---
> 
> # AI Assistant Layer
> 
> The AI should do five jobs.
> 
> ## 1. Capture
> 
> You say messy human stuff:
> 
> > “Zai gave me 100 but 60 was for gas and 40 goes toward what he owed from Tuesday.”
> 
> AI turns it into structured records.
> 
> ## 2. Clarify
> 
> It asks only when necessary:
> 
> > “Is the $40 reducing an existing debt or creating a new credit?”
> 
> But it should not interrogate you like a tax auditor. One question max.
> 
> ## 3. Triage
> 
> It tells you what matters now.
> 
> > “You have 7 open things, but only 2 affect today’s cashflow.”
> 
> ## 4. Update
> 
> You say:
> 
> > “Mark the clerk call done. They said check was mailed.”
> 
> It updates the task, adds a log, and adjusts the expected follow-up.
> 
> ## 5. Summarize
> 
> Daily:
> 
> > “Today you earned X, spent Y, completed Z, and have A waiting items.”
> 
> Weekly:
> 
> > “These people owe you money. These projects are stalled. These tasks keep rolling over.”
> 
> That is the “cut through the noise” layer.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Database Shape
> 
> You can build this with:
> 
> - SQLite locally for first version
> - Postgres later on server
> - NocoDB as admin/table UI
> - FastAPI backend
> - React/Vite frontend
> - Local file storage + Google Drive/QiNexus links
> - Optional AI layer through OpenAI/local Ollama later
> 
> Do **not** start with Supabase dependency hell unless you need hosted auth immediately.
> 
> For v1:
> 
> **SQLite + FastAPI + React is enough.**
> 
> Clean. Portable. No drama.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Minimum Tables
> 
> Start with these:
> 
> 1. `people`
> 2. `areas`
> 3. `projects`
> 4. `tasks`
> 5. `transactions`
> 6. `obligations`
> 7. `events`
> 8. `notes`
> 9. `documents`
> 10. `activity_log`
> 11. `links`
> 
> The most important table is `links`.
> 
> Because one task may link to:
> 
> - a person
> - a transaction
> - a project
> - a document
> - an obligation
> - a note
> 
> That avoids overbuilding 50 relationship tables too early.
> 
> ---
> 
> # V1 Scope
> 
> Do not build the final cathedral first. That is how we summon chaos goblins.
> 
> Build this first:
> 
> ## QiLife V1
> 
> ### Pages
> 
> 1. Dashboard  
> 2. Inbox  
> 3. People  
> 4. Projects  
> 5. Tasks  
> 6. Money  
> 7. Obligations  
> 8. Daily Plan  
> 
> ### Core actions
> 
> - Add person
> - Add task
> - Add project/tasklist
> - Add transaction
> - Add obligation
> - Link records together
> - Mark task done
> - Mark obligation paid/resolved
> - View today
> - View waiting-on
> - Search everything
> 
> ### AI actions
> 
> - “Turn this message into tasks”
> - “Summarize today”
> - “What should I do next?”
> - “Show money owed”
> - “Update this project from this note”
> 
> That’s enough to change your life immediately.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What not to build yet
> 
> Do **not** start with:
> 
> - complex permissions
> - multi-user accounts
> - full mobile app
> - calendar sync
> - bank sync
> - OCR pipelines
> - graph database
> - beautiful dashboards
> - Notion-style blocks
> - automation workflows for everything
> - 19 different AI agents
> 
> That is v2/v3.
> 
> Right now you need the damn spine.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The spine
> 
> Here it is:
> 
> **Everything is a record.  
> Every record can link to people, areas, projects, money, documents, and time.  
> AI helps capture, clean, prioritize, and summarize.  
> The daily screen tells Cody what matters today.**
> 
> That’s the product.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended Build Path
> 
> ## Phase 1: Local working app
> 
> Build on your PC:
> 
> `C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\qilife`
> 
> Stack:
> 
> - React + Vite + TypeScript
> - FastAPI
> - SQLite
> - SQLModel or SQLAlchemy
> - simple local file attachments
> - seed data for your real areas
> 
> ## Phase 2: Server deploy
> 
> Move to QiServer:
> 
> `/srv/qios/apps/qilife`
> 
> Use:
> 
> - Docker Compose
> - Postgres
> - Tailscale-only private access
> - optional Cloudflare protected landing link
> 
> ## Phase 3: AI layer
> 
> Add:
> 
> - inbox parser
> - task generator
> - daily triage
> - money/obligation summarizer
> - project update assistant
> 
> ## Phase 4: Integrations
> 
> Later:
> 
> - Google Calendar
> - Gmail
> - Drive/QiNexus
> - Paperless
> - NocoDB
> - Family Wall
> - Firefly/QiFinance
> 
> ---
> 
> # First build prompt for Codex
> 
> Use this:
> 
> Create a new local-first web app called QiLife at `C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\qilife`.
> 
> Goal: build a personal life operating system for Cody. This is not a generic todo app. It must manage people, areas, projects/tasklists, tasks, money transactions, obligations, notes, documents, daily schedules, and AI-assisted inbox triage.
> 
> Tech stack:
> - Frontend: React + Vite + TypeScript
> - Backend: FastAPI
> - Database: SQLite for v1 using SQLModel or SQLAlchemy
> - Styling: clean dark-mode-first UI, mobile-friendly, dashboard layout
> - No external auth for v1
> - Keep the architecture portable so it can later move to Postgres on QiServer
> 
> Core doctrine:
> - Everything important is a structured record.
> - Records must be linkable to people, areas, projects, tasks, transactions, obligations, notes, documents, and events.
> - Projects and tasklists are the same concept.
> - People are first-class objects, not just contacts.
> - Money must support transaction logs and obligations: who paid whom, from where to where, for what, and whether someone owes someone.
> - The app must reduce cognitive clutter and show a daily command center.
> 
> Create the following backend models/tables:
> 
> 1. people
> Fields:
> - id
> - display_name
> - legal_name
> - type: person, company, agency, vendor, client, household, court, other
> - email
> - phone
> - address
> - notes
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 2. areas
> Fields:
> - id
> - name
> - slug
> - description
> - sort_order
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> Seed areas:
> - Inbox
> - Workbench
> - Timeline
> - Life
> - People
> - Business
> - Finance
> - Legal
> - Tech
> - Assets
> - Data
> - Reference
> - Archive
> - System
> 
> 3. projects
> Fields:
> - id
> - name
> - description
> - area_id
> - status: active, waiting, paused, done, archived
> - priority: urgent, high, normal, low
> - next_action
> - due_date
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 4. tasks
> Fields:
> - id
> - title
> - description
> - area_id
> - project_id
> - status: inbox, open, next, waiting, blocked, done, archived
> - priority: urgent, high, normal, low
> - energy: low, medium, high
> - context: phone, home, computer, errands, car, anywhere
> - due_date
> - scheduled_for
> - completed_at
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 5. transactions
> Fields:
> - id
> - date
> - amount
> - currency
> - direction: in, out, transfer
> - from_entity_type: person, account, company, other
> - from_entity_id
> - from_label
> - to_entity_type
> - to_entity_id
> - to_label
> - category
> - area_id
> - project_id
> - status: pending, cleared, disputed, canceled
> - notes
> - evidence_document_id
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 6. obligations
> Fields:
> - id
> - owed_by_type: person, company, agency, other
> - owed_by_id
> - owed_by_label
> - owed_to_type
> - owed_to_id
> - owed_to_label
> - obligation_type: money, document, task, response, decision, other
> - amount
> - currency
> - reason
> - status: open, partial, resolved, canceled, disputed
> - due_date
> - related_transaction_id
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 7. notes
> Fields:
> - id
> - title
> - body
> - area_id
> - project_id
> - note_type: general, log, journal, evidence, meeting, ai_summary
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 8. documents
> Fields:
> - id
> - title
> - file_path
> - source
> - area_id
> - project_id
> - document_type: pdf, image, receipt, contract, court, bill, statement, other
> - notes
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 9. events
> Fields:
> - id
> - title
> - description
> - start_time
> - end_time
> - location
> - area_id
> - project_id
> - status: scheduled, done, canceled
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> 10. links
> Fields:
> - id
> - source_type
> - source_id
> - target_type
> - target_id
> - relationship
> - created_at
> 
> 11. activity_log
> Fields:
> - id
> - action
> - entity_type
> - entity_id
> - summary
> - created_at
> 
> Build API endpoints for CRUD operations for all core models.
> 
> Frontend pages:
> 1. Dashboard
> - show Today
> - urgent tasks
> - waiting obligations
> - upcoming events
> - open money items
> - recent activity
> 
> 2. Inbox
> - quick capture box
> - list unprocessed tasks/notes
> - button: “Process with AI” placeholder for now
> 
> 3. People
> - list people
> - person detail page showing related tasks, projects, transactions, obligations, notes, documents
> 
> 4. Projects
> - list projects/tasklists
> - project detail page showing tasks, people, transactions, notes, documents
> 
> 5. Tasks
> - grouped by status, priority, area, and context
> 
> 6. Money
> - transactions table
> - filters for in/out/transfer/status/person/project
> 
> 7. Obligations
> - who owes me
> - who I owe
> - open/resolved/disputed
> 
> 8. Daily Plan
> - tasks scheduled today
> - due today
> - errands
> - phone calls
> - waiting-on list
> - AI focus summary placeholder
> 
> Design requirements:
> - dark mode by default
> - clean cards with depth/shadow
> - no ugly plain white cards
> - readable typography
> - responsive mobile layout
> - sidebar on desktop, bottom nav or simple stacked nav on mobile
> - clear empty states
> - fast data entry buttons
> 
> Add seed data examples:
> - Person: Cody
> - Person: Zaituallah Jan Khebarkhil
> - Project: Lyft Income Sprint
> - Project: Surplus Check Recovery
> - Project: QiFinance Intake
> - Task: Finish 11 Lyft rides
> - Task: Check mail for surplus check
> - Obligation: Zai owes Cody $40 for gas
> - Transaction: Cody paid gas for Lyft
> 
> Add a README with:
> - setup instructions
> - dev run commands
> - project purpose
> - data model overview
> - future server deployment notes
> 
> Do not overbuild authentication, sync, bank integrations, calendar integrations, or real AI calls yet. Use clean placeholder service files where AI integration will later go.
> 
> Make sure the app runs locally with one command or clearly documented commands.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final answer
> 
> This is the right direction.
> 
> The app you need is not a planner.
> 
> It is a **personal command system** where:
> 
> - people are connected to tasks
> - tasks are connected to money
> - money is connected to obligations
> - obligations are connected to documents
> - documents are connected to projects
> - projects are connected to daily reality
> - AI keeps the whole mess from becoming a digital junk drawer
> 
> Build the spine first.
> 
> Then we make it smart.

### User
> ive looked at adulting app, hyperaide, orakemu, taskwarrior, takosaur.com, will be done, etc. any candidates for self build and also this is where we are taking all the concepts and finally making one app.

### Assistant
> I’ll sanity-check the landscape instead of guessing from memory, then I’ll sort these into “copy patterns,” “borrow architecture,” and “ignore because it’ll distract us.”

### Assistant
> Yes. This is exactly where the wandering stops.
> 
> You’ve been circling the real category: **personal operations software**. None of these apps fully solve it because they each own one slice: tasks, adulting routines, AI capture, time blocking, life roles, project execution, or chores. What you need is the **fusion layer**.
> 
> ## Fast verdict
> 
> | Candidate | Use it as-is? | Steal from it? | Why |
> |---|---:|---:|---|
> | **Hyperaide** | Maybe not | **Yes — heavily** | Best pattern for “AI on top of a personal database,” with tasks, projects, contacts, receipts/contracts, plus WhatsApp/Telegram capture. That is close to the QiLife brain. citeturn141256search14 |
> | **Orakemu** | Maybe | **Yes** | Strong “life roles + projects + timeline + time tracking + gamified life” concept. Good inspiration for daily planning and dopamine. citeturn141256search0 |
> | **Taskwarrior** | Backend/tool inspiration | **Yes** | Open-source, fast, flexible task engine. Great philosophy and ecosystem, but CLI-first and not enough for people/money/documents by itself. citeturn141256search1turn141256search13 |
> | **Taskosaur** | Possible code reference | **Yes** | Open-source GitHub project combining project management with conversational AI task execution. This is directly relevant as an implementation reference. citeturn556440search16 |
> | **Adulting / Get Adulting** | No | **Yes, small piece** | Preset adult-life reminders are smart. Steal the “don’t make the user create every routine manually” idea. citeturn556440search7 |
> | **Lunatask** | Maybe as temporary app | **Yes** | All-in-one encrypted tasks, habits, journaling, life tracking, notes. Good feature benchmark, not your full system. citeturn141256search15 |
> | **Will Be Done** | Unclear | Not enough signal | I’m not seeing a clean candidate from that name. Could be app-name confusion unless you have a specific link. |
> | **Takosaur.com / Taskosaur** | Yes as reference | **Yes** | Looks like “Taskosaur,” and that one matters because it’s conversational AI + task/project management. citeturn556440search16 |
> 
> ## The honest answer
> 
> Do **not** adopt one of these as the main app.
> 
> Use them as **pattern libraries**.
> 
> The winning recipe is:
> 
> **Hyperaide’s AI database layer**  
> + **Orakemu’s life roles/time blocks/gamification**  
> + **Taskwarrior’s task model discipline**  
> + **Taskosaur’s conversational execution concept**  
> + **Adulting’s preset routines/templates**  
> + **your QiNexus people-money-documents-obligations model**
> 
> That becomes your app.
> 
> ## The app category
> 
> Call the product class:
> 
> **LifeOps CRM**
> 
> Because that’s what it is.
> 
> Not a todo app.
> 
> A CRM for your life:
> 
> - people
> - responsibilities
> - promises
> - money owed
> - tasks
> - projects
> - documents
> - conversations
> - deadlines
> - recurring life maintenance
> - AI triage
> 
> Normal productivity apps fail you because they treat life like isolated tasks.
> 
> Your life is not isolated tasks. It is **relationships + obligations + money + time + documents + emotional load + execution context**.
> 
> That is the model.
> 
> ## What to copy from each
> 
> ### Hyperaide: copy the AI command layer
> 
> Hyperaide explicitly frames itself as “AI on top to manage your database,” with tasks, projects, contacts, receipts, and contracts, plus chat capture through WhatsApp/Telegram. That is extremely close to your missing interface. citeturn141256search14
> 
> Steal:
> 
> - chat-first capture
> - AI creates database records
> - AI updates records
> - AI finds context
> - database is the real source of truth
> - messaging app input later
> 
> Do **not** copy:
> 
> - dependence on someone else’s SaaS
> - vague “assistant” branding
> - limited ownership of your data
> 
> ### Orakemu: copy the life-role + timeline model
> 
> Orakemu has tasks, projects, life roles, timeline, time tracking, and planned calendar integration. That’s useful because your tasks need to map to “which life hat am I wearing?” citeturn141256search0
> 
> Steal:
> 
> - life roles
> - daily timeline
> - time blocks
> - gamified completion
> - visible progress
> - dopamine loops
> 
> Do **not** overdo the game mechanics. You need dopamine, not a fake RPG that becomes another job.
> 
> ### Taskwarrior: copy the task engine philosophy
> 
> Taskwarrior is open-source, flexible, fast, and CLI-based. Its ecosystem and simple task-first discipline are valuable. citeturn141256search1turn141256search13
> 
> Steal:
> 
> - urgency scoring
> - tags
> - projects
> - contexts
> - due/waiting/scheduled
> - plain-data portability
> - fast capture
> 
> Do **not** make QiLife CLI-first. That would be productivity monk nonsense for your actual day-to-day. You need mobile/web command center.
> 
> ### Taskosaur: inspect as AI/project reference
> 
> Taskosaur describes itself as combining project management with conversational AI task execution, where users can create tasks, assign work, and manage workflows through natural conversation. That’s worth reviewing as a self-build candidate/reference. citeturn556440search16
> 
> Steal:
> 
> - conversational task execution
> - AI command parser
> - workflow updates from natural language
> - project management primitives
> 
> ### Adulting: copy the starter templates
> 
> Get Adulting’s strongest idea is preset reminders for adult-life tasks, instead of forcing users to manually invent every recurring chore. citeturn556440search7
> 
> Steal:
> 
> - preset life admin packs
> - household maintenance templates
> - recurring reminders
> - “turn this on” instead of “build from scratch”
> 
> This matters because empty apps are hostile to ADHD. A blank task manager is a trap.
> 
> ## Best self-build candidates
> 
> Here’s the stack I’d actually investigate first:
> 
> ### 1. Taskosaur
> 
> Best candidate for AI task/project inspiration.
> 
> Reason: It’s already pointed at conversational AI task execution, which is the direction we need. It may not be your final base, but the code and concepts are probably worth mining.
> 
> ### 2. Taskwarrior ecosystem
> 
> Best candidate for task logic.
> 
> Reason: Mature open-source task model. Not pretty. Not complete. But a reliable mental model for status, urgency, scheduling, projects, tags, recurrence, waiting, and contexts.
> 
> ### 3. Vikunja / AppFlowy / Plane / Huly style tools
> 
> I’d look at these as broader open-source project/task bases, but carefully. The danger is they become “work management tools,” not “life operations tools.” They usually lack money, obligations, personal CRM, and AI triage.
> 
> ### 4. NocoDB as admin layer
> 
> Not the user-facing app, but useful as a database admin cockpit.
> 
> You can let QiLife have a clean daily UI while NocoDB gives you spreadsheet-style access to the underlying tables.
> 
> ## What makes your app different
> 
> The killer feature is **not AI tasks**.
> 
> Everybody is adding AI glitter now.
> 
> The killer feature is this data model:
> 
> > Person → Project → Task → Transaction → Obligation → Document → Event → Note → AI Summary
> 
> Example:
> 
> “Zai owes me $40 for gas” should not be a note.
> 
> It should create:
> 
> - Person link: Zai
> - Obligation: Zai owes Cody $40
> - Category: gas
> - Related project: Lyft / Household / Shared Expenses
> - Follow-up task: ask/confirm/mark paid
> - Transaction when paid
> - Activity log entry
> - Daily dashboard alert if unresolved
> 
> That is the sauce.
> 
> ## Build doctrine
> 
> ### The app must have three modes
> 
> ## 1. Capture Mode
> 
> Fast. Messy. Voice/text/photo.
> 
> Example:
> 
> > “Paid 18.42 at Circle K for Lyft gas, put under work expenses.”
> 
> The app records it without making you fill out a damn tax form on the side of the road.
> 
> ## 2. Command Mode
> 
> Ask the system:
> 
> - “Who owes me money?”
> - “What is blocking today?”
> - “What do I need to do before I drive Lyft?”
> - “What tasks involve Zai?”
> - “What legal things are waiting?”
> - “What did I spend on gas this week?”
> - “What promises are open?”
> 
> ## 3. Review Mode
> 
> Daily/weekly cleanup:
> 
> - unprocessed inbox
> - open obligations
> - overdue tasks
> - unresolved money
> - stalled projects
> - people needing follow-up
> 
> This is how it stays clean.
> 
> ## MVP feature cut
> 
> Build only this first:
> 
> 1. **Inbox capture**
> 2. **People**
> 3. **Projects/tasklists**
> 4. **Tasks**
> 5. **Transactions**
> 6. **Obligations**
> 7. **Daily dashboard**
> 8. **AI parse placeholder**
> 9. **Search**
> 10. **Links between records**
> 
> No bank sync.  
> No calendar sync yet.  
> No mobile app yet.  
> No graph database yet.  
> No “beautiful final UI” obsession yet.
> 
> Make it usable. Then make it pretty. Then make it spooky-smart.
> 
> ## My recommendation
> 
> Build **QiLife V1** from scratch, but use these as references:
> 
> - **Taskosaur** for conversational AI task execution.
> - **Taskwarrior** for task model discipline.
> - **Hyperaide** for AI database UX.
> - **Orakemu** for timeline/life roles/dopamine.
> - **Adulting** for preset recurring life templates.
> 
> And the final app should be framed as:
> 
> **QiLife: a local-first LifeOps CRM for people, tasks, money, obligations, documents, and daily execution.**
> 
> That’s the clean lane. That’s the thing all these almost-apps are pointing at but not fully becoming.

> ## What Will Be Done gives us
> 
> It is an open-source, self-hosted, local-first task manager focused on weekly planning, offline use, kanban boards, quick capture, and instant drag/drop planning. It uses SQLite, can run in Docker, and is designed around owning your data. citeturn219783view0
> 
> That hits several of your core requirements:
> 
> | QiLife Need | Will Be Done fit |
> |---|---|
> | Self-hosted | Yes |
> | Local-first/offline | Yes |
> | SQLite | Yes |
> | Weekly planning | Strong yes |
> | Kanban/project boards | Yes |
> | Mobile-friendly | Yes |
> | Desktop quick add | Yes |
> | Fast capture | Yes |
> | Own your data | Yes |
> | People/CRM | No |
> | Money/transactions | No |
> | Obligations owed/to | No |
> | Documents/evidence | Not core |
> | AI triage | Not built yet, but API/MCP is planned |
> 
> Their own README says the goal is a fast, offline-first task manager that can handle years of tasks, with a clean API for things like MCP or Telegram task creation. That is very aligned with your “AI command center over life data” direction. citeturn458805view0
>

> ## My recommendation
> 
> Use **Will Be Done as the UX and planning reference**.
> 
> Build **QiLife as its own app** unless Codex finds the repo is cleanly modular enough to extend.
> 
> Why? Because QiLife’s data model is fundamentally broader. You need people/money/obligations/documents as first-class objects. If Will Be Done’s internal model is tightly task-only, extending it may become surgery with a butter knife.

### Assistant
> Correct. Drop **CRM** from the framing.
> 
> That word is dragging the app toward sales pipelines, leads, deals, client stages, follow-up funnels — and that is **not** what you’re building anymore.
> 
> The better framing:
> 
> # QiLife is a LifeOps app
> 
> Not CRM. Not project management. Not finance app. Not todo app.
> 
> A **LifeOps app** that has:
> 
> - **People**
> - **Tasks**
> - **Projects / tasklists**
> - **Areas**
> - **Transactions**
> - **Obligations**
> - **Notes**
> - **Documents**
> - **Schedule**
> - **AI triage**
> 
> ## Replace “CRM” with “People”
> 
> People should be lightweight but powerful.
> 
> ### Person record
> 
> | Field | Purpose |
> |---|---|
> | name | who they are |
> | type | person, company, agency, vendor, family, client, court, other |
> | contact info | phone/email/address |
> | relationship | family, friend, vendor, agency, occasional client, etc. |
> | notes | context |
> | linked tasks | what involves them |
> | linked money | transactions/obligations |
> | linked projects | where they show up |
> | linked documents | lease, order, receipt, contract |
> | activity log | history |
> 
> That’s it.
> 
> No pipeline.  
> No lead status.  
> No sales stages.  
> No deal forecasting.  
> No “opportunity value.”  
> No little SaaS goblin wearing a tie.
> 
> ## Updated doctrine
> 
> Use this:
> 
> **QiLife is a local-first LifeOps system for organizing daily life across people, tasks, projects, money, obligations, notes, documents, and schedules, with AI-assisted capture and triage.**
> 
> Much cleaner.
> 
> ## Rename modules
> 
> | Old name | New name |
> |---|---|
> | CRM | People |
> | Deals | Delete entirely |
> | Clients | People with relationship = client |
> | Accounts | People/Organizations |
> | Follow-ups | Tasks / Waiting On |
> | Sales notes | Notes |
> | Opportunities | Projects, only when needed |
> 
> ## Freelance handling
> 
> Freelance still fits, just without CRM bloat.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ### Person: Jane Smith
> 
> Relationship: occasional client  
> Linked project: Website cleanup  
> Linked transaction: $250 paid  
> Linked obligation: Jane owes Cody final $100  
> Linked notes: prefers text, needs invoice Friday  
> Linked docs: invoice PDF, scope note  
> 
> That’s enough. No pipeline theater.
> 
> ## Updated app spine
> 
> The core model should be:
> 
> 1. **Inbox**
> 2. **Today**
> 3. **People**
> 4. **Areas**
> 5. **Projects / Tasklists**
> 6. **Tasks**
> 7. **Money**

> 9. **Notes**

> 
> That’s the thing.
>

### Assistant
> Yes — **this is the strongest base/reference so far**, but I would be careful about **forking it as the foundation** unless you accept the license and architecture tradeoffs.
> 
> ## What it is technically
> 
> Will Be Done is very much in your wheelhouse:
> 
> - **Frontend:** React 19 + Vite + TypeScript.
> - **Backend:** Bun + Fastify + tRPC.
> - **Database/local-first layer:** custom `hyperdb`, Kysely, SQLite/WebAssembly SQLite pieces, browser-side database/offline behavior.
> - **UI stack:** Tailwind, Radix/Base UI/Headless UI, TanStack Router/Query/Form, drag-and-drop libs, Motion.
> - **Packaging:** Docker self-hosting, desktop app downloads, PWA/mobile web.
> - **License:** AGPL-3.0. That matters. More below.
> 
> The repo itself confirms a workspace layout with `apps/*` and `packages/*`, scripts for `apps/web` and `apps/api`, and Bun as the runtime/package tool. citeturn984546view0 The web app package uses Vite, React, TanStack, Tailwind, Radix/Base UI, Kysely, `wa-sqlite`, and related local-first tooling. citeturn469485view0 The API package uses Bun, Fastify, WebSockets, tRPC, and the project’s shared `hyperdb`/`slices` packages. citeturn469485view1
> 
> ## Can we edit it?
> 
> Yes. Technically, a lot.
> 
> You can edit:
> 
> - branding
> - theme
> - navigation
> - dashboard layout
> - task fields
> - project columns
> - weekly view
> - stash/quick capture
> - keyboard behavior
> - local data model
> - backend endpoints
> - Docker deployment
> - AI/MCP integration layer
> - new modules like People, Money, Obligations, Notes, Documents
> 
> But here’s the catch, honey: **“can edit” is not the same as “should mutate it into QiLife.”**
> 
> Will Be Done is built as a task manager. QiLife is bigger. You want:
> 
> - people
> - notes
> - relationships
> - task buckets
> - projects/tasklists
> - money movement
> - obligations
> - schedules
> - AI capture
> - AI triage
> - local/self-hosted ownership
> 
> Will Be Done already nails the **task/week/planning UX**: visual weekly timeline, project kanban, mobile UI, offline-first operation, quick add, Docker/self-hosting, and “no guilt avalanche” missed-task design. citeturn747888view0
> 
> That is worth stealing with both hands.
> 
> ## The licensing issue
> 
> This is the uncomfortable but important part.
> 
> Will Be Done is **AGPL-3.0**. The site and repo both state AGPL. citeturn747888view0 citeturn199406view0
> 
> AGPL means if you modify it and make it available over a network, users generally must be able to access the corresponding modified source code. The license text specifically says AGPL is designed so modified versions used on network servers provide source access to users interacting with it. citeturn984546view1
> 
> So:
> 
> | Use case | Problem? |
> |---|---|
> | Personal private fork on your own machine/server | Usually fine |
> | Tailscale-only personal app | Likely fine practically, but still preserve license notices |
> | Public SaaS product with private proprietary code | Bad fit |
> | Public open-source QiLife fork | Fine, if you comply with AGPL |
> | Copy UI ideas but write your own code | Cleanest path |
> 
> Not legal advice, but strategically: **do not build your proprietary QiLife directly on AGPL code unless you’re okay with QiLife being AGPL/open-source too.**
> 
> ## My actual recommendation
> 
> Do **not** fork it first.
> 
> Do this instead:
> 
> # Build QiLife as your own app, inspired by Will Be Done
> 
> Use Will Be Done as a **reference implementation**, not the parent DNA.
> 
> Why?
> 
> Because you said the magic words: **“I want it to be my own and my own data.”**
> 
> That means:
> 
> 1. Own your schema.
> 2. Own your architecture.
> 3. Own your naming.
> 4. Own your AI layer.
> 5. Borrow UX patterns, not legal baggage.
> 6. Avoid getting trapped inside someone else’s task-only assumptions.
> 
> Will Be Done gives us the look/feel and planning behavior. QiLife needs a broader LifeOps data model.
> 
> ## What to copy from Will Be Done
> 
> Copy the concepts:
> 
> - weekly timeline with each day as a column
> - drag/drop task planning
> - Today view
> - project kanban boards
> - Stash / quick capture panel
> - gentle rollover instead of shame-overdue
> - mobile-first planning
> - offline-first feel
> - Docker self-hosting
> - SQLite/simple data ownership
> - fast keyboard-friendly UX
> - future MCP/API layer
> 
> Their README says they intentionally built for offline-first use, self-hosting, clean API/MCP possibility, weekly planning, Vim keybindings, and a task suggestion panel. That is basically screaming “use me as the inspiration board.” citeturn747888view1
> 
> ## What not to copy
> 
> Do not copy the limitation that it’s “just tasks.”
> 
> The repo even says features not planned include multi-user per space/project, sharing, and no time schedules for tasks. citeturn199406view0 That’s fine for them. Not fine for QiLife long-term.
> 
> Also don’t copy its complexity unless you need it. Their local-first system is sophisticated. That’s great, but if we start there, Codex may spend three days wrestling the sync dragon while you still can’t log “Zai owes me $40.”
> 
> No, ma’am. Spine first.
> 
> ## Better architecture for QiLife
> 
> For v1, I’d build:
> 
> ### Frontend
> 
> React + Vite + TypeScript  
> TanStack Router  
> Tailwind  
> Radix or shadcn-style components  
> PWA-ready
> 
> ### Backend
> 
> FastAPI or Bun/Fastify.
> 
> Given your stack history, I still lean **FastAPI + SQLite/Postgres** because you already think in Python tooling and server scripts.
> 
> But if you want to stay closer to Will Be Done’s world, use:
> 
> Bun + Fastify + tRPC + SQLite
> 
> That would make copying UI patterns easier.
> 
> ### Database
> 
> Start SQLite locally.
> 
> Tables:
> 
> - people
> - areas
> - projects
> - tasks
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - notes
> - documents
> - events
> - links
> - ai_runs / ai_suggestions
> 
> ### AI layer
> 
> This is non-negotiable. But in v1, it should be a service layer:
> 
> - `ai_parse_inbox_entry`
> - `ai_suggest_today`
> - `ai_update_task`
> - `ai_extract_transaction`
> - `ai_extract_obligation`
> - `ai_summarize_project`
> - `ai_find_noise_vs_real`
> 
> Do not bury AI directly inside UI components. That becomes spaghetti with glitter.
> 
> ## The decision
> 
> Here’s the clean strategic call:
> 
> | Option | Verdict |
> |---|---|
> | Use Will Be Done as-is | No, too task-only |
> | Fork and heavily mutate it | Maybe, but license + complexity risk |
> | Build QiLife from scratch copying its UX ideas | **Best path** |
> | Inspect repo first and reuse patterns/components carefully | **Yes** |
> | Use it temporarily while building QiLife | Also yes |
> 
> ## What I’d have Codex do next
> 
> Tell Codex this:
> 
> ```text
> Research and inspect the Will Be Done repository at https://github.com/will-be-done/will-be-done as a UX and architecture reference for QiLife, but do not fork or copy code yet.
> 
> Goal:
> QiLife is Cody’s local-first LifeOps app, inspired by Will Be Done’s weekly planning UI, but expanded into people, tasks, projects/tasklists, money transactions, obligations, notes, documents, schedules, and AI-assisted capture/triage.
> 
> Investigate:
> 1. Frontend stack and component organization.
> 2. How the weekly timeline is implemented.
> 3. How task drag/drop works.
> 4. How project kanban boards are modeled.
> 5. How quick capture/stash works.
> 6. How local-first sync and browser database are implemented.
> 7. How Docker/self-hosted deployment works.
> 8. What parts are reusable as ideas versus too coupled to their system.
> 9. AGPL license implications for copying/forking.
> 10. Whether QiLife should be built from scratch using similar UX patterns.
> 
> Deliver:
> - A repo structure summary.
> - A technical stack summary.
> - A data model summary.
> - A list of UX patterns to emulate.
> - A list of code areas not to touch/copy yet.
> - A recommendation: fork, reference only, or clean-room rebuild.
> - A QiLife v1 architecture plan using React/Vite/TypeScript with a local SQLite-backed backend and an AI service layer.
> 
> Do not modify files yet.
> Do not create a fork yet.
> Do not copy AGPL code into QiLife.
> This is research and architecture only.
> ```
> 
> ## Final call
> 
> You’re right to like Will Be Done. The vibe fits: visual, fast, weekly, self-hosted, local-first, not shame-based.
> 
> But QiLife needs to be **your system**, not a task manager wearing a wig.
> 
> So: **reference Will Be Done heavily, build QiLife separately, and add the AI layer from day one as a first-class service.**

> But do it in stages so we don’t turn it into a flaming raccoon nest.
> 
> ## Stage 1: Personal fork, minimal edits
> 
> Goal: get your own branded working version running.
> 
> Change:
> 
> - app name: **QiLife**
> - theme/look
> - sidebar/nav labels
> - landing/help text
> - source/about page
> - Docker name/volume
> - README notes for your personal fork
> 
> Add:
> 
> - “Source / Based On” link in Settings/About
> - local backup/export note
> - `docs/QILIFE_NOTES.md`
> - `docs/UPSTREAM.md` explaining original repo and fork date
> 
> Do **not** rip up the database yet.
> 
> ## Stage 2: Add AI layer beside it
> 
> Don’t jam AI directly into the task components first. Add a clean service layer:
> 
> - AI Inbox Parser
> - AI Task Creator
> - AI Daily Focus
> - AI Weekly Review
> - AI Project Summary
> 
> The first AI feature should be:
> 
> > Paste messy thought → app suggests tasks/project/date/priority/context → you approve.
> 
> That gives you immediate value without corrupting the data model.
> 
> ## Stage 3: Add People + Notes
> 
> Next, add lightweight people support:
> 
> - person name
> - contact info
> - notes
> - linked tasks
> - linked projects
> - activity log
> 
> No CRM garbage. Just “humans and entities involved in my life.”
> 
> ## Stage 4: Add Money + Obligations
> 
> Then add:
> 
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - who owes whom
> - linked person
> - linked task
> - linked note/evidence
> 
> This is where QiLife becomes **your actual LifeOps system** instead of a better todo app.
> 
> ## Stage 5: Decide whether to stay forked or migrate
> 
> After you’ve hacked it into shape, decide:
> 
> 1. Keep it as a personal AGPL fork forever.
> 2. Rebuild clean from scratch using what you learned.
> 3. Split QiLife into:
>    - Will-Be-Done-derived planner
>    - separate QiLife API/data brain
> 
> For you personally? Option 1 is fine for now.
> 
> ## The practical source link
> 
> Put something like this in Settings/About:
> 
> > QiLife is Cody’s personal LifeOps fork/adaptation of Will Be Done, an open-source offline-first self-hosted task manager licensed under AGPL-3.0. Original project: https://github.com/will-be-done/will-be-done
> 
> That’s clean enough for your personal usage notes.

> ## Blunt call
>

### User
> well, my biggest pain points are no central task ledger, no central, what happened today, no central knowledge base, no central note taking place, and no ai that is directly connected and knows all of the above.

### Assistant
> Exactly. That’s the real spec.
> 
> Your pain is **not** “I need a better planner.”
> 
> Your pain is:
> 
> > “My life produces data all day, but none of it lands in one place where it becomes usable memory, decisions, tasks, evidence, and next actions.”
> 
> So QiLife needs four cores plus one intelligence layer.
> 
> # QiLife Core
> 
> ## 1. Central Task Ledger
> 
> Not a todo list. A **task ledger**.
> 
> Every obligation/action goes into one canonical table:
> 
> - task
> - status
> - area
> - project/tasklist
> - people involved
> - due/scheduled date
> - context: phone, errands, home, computer, car
> - source: voice note, manual entry, email, document, chat, receipt
> - related notes/docs/money
> - activity history
> 
> The key is that tasks are not scattered across texts, memory, Family Wall, Google Calendar, random docs, and panic.
> 
> There is one place.
> 
> ## 2. Central Daily Log
> 
> This is huge.
> 
> You need a **What Happened Today** ledger.
> 
> Every day should have an auto-generated page:
> 
> ### Today: May 29, 2026
> 
> - tasks created
> - tasks completed
> - money spent/received
> - people interacted with
> - notes captured
> - documents added
> - events
> - decisions
> - unresolved issues
> - AI summary
> - tomorrow carry-forward
> 
> This solves the “what the hell happened today?” problem.
> 
> It also becomes legal/admin/caregiving/business evidence when needed.
> 
> ## 3. Central Knowledge Base
> 
> This is where durable information lives.
> 
> Not fleeting task stuff. Actual reference knowledge:
> 
> - how systems work
> - legal case timeline
> - household protocols
> - server runbooks
> - finance rules
> - people context
> - lease info
> - scripts/tools docs
> - decision records
> - templates
> - policies
> - project notes
> 
> This should probably map to Markdown/QiNote eventually, but the app should index it and expose it.
> 
> ## 4. Central Note Capture
> 
> This is the intake layer.
> 
> You need one capture box for:
> 
> - “remember this”
> - journal entry
> - frustration dump
> - meeting note
> - phone call note
> - legal observation
> - care note
> - project idea
> - financial note
> - “Zai said…”
> - “Mom asked…”
> - “Clerk told me…”
> 
> Then AI classifies it:
> 
> - task?
> - note?
> - daily log item?
> - knowledge base item?
> - transaction?
> - obligation?
> - document evidence?
> - project update?
> 
> This is the missing nervous system.
> 
> ## 5. AI Connected to All of It
> 
> This is the non-negotiable part.
> 
> The AI should not be a chatbot floating beside the app.
> 
> It should be wired into:
> 
> - task ledger
> - daily log
> - notes
> - knowledge base
> - people
> - projects
> - documents
> - money/obligations
> - calendar/schedule later
> 
> So you can ask:
> 
> - “What actually happened today?”
> - “What am I forgetting?”
> - “What tasks involve Zai?”
> - “What money is unresolved?”
> - “What did I say about the clerk?”
> - “What is the next action on the surplus check?”
> - “What legal items are waiting?”
> - “Summarize the week.”
> - “Turn this rant into tasks and notes.”
> - “What is real, what is noise, and what do I do next?”
> 
> That is the product.
> 
> # Updated architecture
> 
> Think of it like this:
> 
> ## Capture Layer
> 
> Everything comes in:
> 
> - text
> - voice
> - photo
> - file
> - manual task
> - transaction
> - event
> - note
> 
> ## Ledger Layer
> 
> Everything becomes structured:
> 
> - tasks
> - notes
> - daily events
> - people
> - projects
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - documents
> - knowledge records
> 
> ## Memory Layer
> 
> Everything becomes searchable:
> 
> - full-text search
> - tags/areas
> - links
> - embeddings later
> - summaries
> - activity log
> 
> ## AI Layer
> 
> Everything becomes usable:
> 
> - extract
> - classify
> - summarize
> - prioritize
> - answer questions
> - create/update records
> - surface forgotten threads
> 
> # This changes how we use Will Be Done
> 
> Will Be Done can still be the **planner UI/spine**, but it is not enough as the main brain.
> 
> It gives you:
> 
> - tasks
> - weekly planning
> - project boards
> - stash
> - scheduling vibe
> - local-first feel
> 
> But your real app needs a bigger **Life Ledger** behind it.
> 
> So the correct design is:
> 
> ## QiLife = Will Be Done style planner + Life Ledger + AI Memory
> 
> Not:
> 
> > Will Be Done with extra buttons slapped on.
> 
> Better:
> 
> > QiLife uses the weekly planning feel of Will Be Done, but the database expands into a unified life ledger.
> 
> # The MVP should be brutally simple
> 
> Do not start with 20 modules.
> 
> Start with four screens:
> 
> ## 1. Inbox
> 
> One capture box.
> 
> Buttons:
> 
> - Add note
> - Add task
> - Add transaction
> - Add obligation
> - Upload document
> - Process with AI
> 
> ## 2. Today
> 
> The daily command center.
> 
> Sections:
> 
> - Today’s plan
> - Captured today
> - Completed today
> - Money today
> - People today
> - Open loops
> - AI summary
> 
> ## 3. Ledger
> 
> The searchable truth table.
> 
> Tabs:
> 
> - Tasks
> - Notes
> - People
> - Projects
> - Money
> - Obligations
> - Documents
> - Events
> 
> ## 4. Ask QiLife
> 
> AI interface connected to the database.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - “What did I do today?”
> - “What is overdue?”
> - “What am I waiting on?”
> - “Turn today’s notes into a summary.”
> - “Show unresolved money.”
> - “What needs my attention before I drive?”
> 
> That’s v1.
> 
> # Data model shift
> 
> You need a table called `daily_log`.
> 
> Minimum:
> 
> | Field | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | id | record id |
> | date | day |
> | entry_type | task_created, task_done, note, transaction, event, decision, contact, document, ai_summary |
> | summary | what happened |
> | source_type | task, note, transaction, document, manual |
> | source_id | linked record |
> | area_id | optional |
> | project_id | optional |
> | person_id | optional |
> | created_at | timestamp |
> 
> This table becomes your “what happened today” engine.
> 
> Also add `inbox_items`.
> 
> | Field | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | id | capture id |
> | raw_text | messy input |
> | source | text, voice, upload, manual |
> | status | unprocessed, processed, ignored |
> | ai_summary | extracted meaning |
> | created_records | links to generated tasks/notes/etc. |
> | created_at | timestamp |
> 
> That’s the bridge between chaos and order.
> 
> # The truth
> 
> You are building a **memory system**, not an app.
> 
> The interface is just how you touch it.
> 
> The core product is:
> 
> > A central life ledger where daily activity, notes, tasks, knowledge, money, people, and documents become searchable, linkable, and AI-readable.
> 
> That is the thing.
> 
> # Revised Codex prompt
> 
> Use this instead of the earlier broader one:
> 
> Create a personal local-first app called QiLife.
> 
> QiLife is not a generic todo app or CRM. It is Cody’s personal LifeOps memory system.
> 
> Primary pain points:
> 1. No central task ledger.
> 2. No central “what happened today” log.
> 3. No central knowledge base.
> 4. No central note-taking/capture place.
> 5. No AI directly connected to all of the above.
> 
> Goal:
> Build the first working version of QiLife with a unified life ledger and AI-ready architecture.
> 
> Use Will Be Done as UX inspiration for weekly planning, quick capture, project boards, and gentle task rollover, but QiLife must have its own data model and source-controlled codebase.
> 
> Core principles:
> - Local-first.
> - Cody owns the data.
> - Everything important becomes a structured record.
> - Every record can link to other records.
> - The daily log records what happened today.
> - AI should be able to read, summarize, classify, and eventually update all core records.
> - People are lightweight records, not CRM pipelines.
> - Projects and tasklists are the same thing.
> - Tasks are stored in one central task ledger.
> 
> Build stack:
> - React + Vite + TypeScript frontend.
> - FastAPI backend.
> - SQLite database for v1.
> - SQLModel or SQLAlchemy.
> - Dark-mode-first UI.
> - Mobile-friendly layout.
> - Prepare for Docker deployment later.
> - Prepare for future Postgres migration.
> - Prepare for AI service integration, but real AI calls can be placeholder functions in v1.
> 
> Core modules for v1:
> 
> 1. Inbox
> - universal capture box
> - raw text input
> - source field: manual, voice, file, imported, ai
> - status: unprocessed, processed, ignored
> - button: Process with AI placeholder
> - processed output should be able to create tasks, notes, daily log entries, transactions, obligations, or knowledge records later
> 
> 2. Today
> - daily command center
> - shows tasks scheduled/due today
> - shows completed tasks today
> - shows notes captured today
> - shows transactions today
> - shows obligations opened/resolved today
> - shows documents added today
> - shows people touched today
> - shows AI daily summary placeholder
> - shows open loops/carry-forward items
> 
> 3. Task Ledger
> - one canonical task table
> - fields: title, description, status, priority, area, project/tasklist, due_date, scheduled_for, completed_at, energy, context, source, created_at, updated_at
> - statuses: inbox, open, next, waiting, blocked, done, archived
> - contexts: phone, home, computer, errands, car, anywhere
> - views: today, upcoming, waiting, blocked, done, by area, by project
> 
> 4. Notes
> - central note-taking system
> - note types: general, daily, journal, meeting, call, evidence, project, knowledge, ai_summary
> - notes can link to people, projects, tasks, documents, and daily log entries
> 
> 5. Knowledge Base
> - simple knowledge record table for durable information
> - fields: title, body, area, topic, source, confidence, created_at, updated_at
> - not a full wiki yet
> - should be searchable
> - can later sync/export to Markdown/QiNote
> 
> 6. People
> - lightweight people/entities table
> - fields: display_name, legal_name, type, relationship, email, phone, address, notes
> - types: person, company, agency, vendor, court, client, household, other
> - person detail shows linked tasks, notes, transactions, obligations, documents, and projects
> 
> 7. Projects / Tasklists
> - projects are tasklists
> - fields: name, description, area, status, priority, next_action, due_date
> - project detail shows tasks, notes, people, transactions, obligations, documents
> 
> 8. Money / Transactions
> - transaction log
> - fields: date, amount, currency, direction, from_label, to_label, category, area, project, status, notes
> - direction: in, out, transfer
> - status: pending, cleared, disputed, canceled
> 
> 9. Obligations
> - who owes whom / what is owed
> - fields: owed_by_label, owed_to_label, type, amount, reason, due_date, status, related_transaction_id
> - type: money, document, task, response, decision, other
> - status: open, partial, resolved, canceled, disputed
> 
> 10. Documents
> - metadata table only for v1
> - fields: title, file_path, source, document_type, area, project, notes
> - document types: pdf, image, receipt, contract, court, bill, statement, other
> 
> 11. Daily Log
> - central “what happened today” table
> - every major action should create or be able to create a daily log entry
> - fields: date, entry_type, summary, source_type, source_id, area, project, person, created_at
> - entry types: task_created, task_done, note, transaction, obligation, document, event, decision, ai_summary, manual_log
> 
> 12. Links
> - generic linking table
> - fields: source_type, source_id, target_type, target_id, relationship
> - use this to connect tasks, notes, people, projects, transactions, obligations, documents, knowledge records, and daily log entries
> 
> 13. AI Assistant placeholder
> - create an AI service layer with placeholder functions:
>   - parse_inbox_item
>   - suggest_today_focus
>   - summarize_day
>   - summarize_project
>   - extract_tasks_from_note
>   - extract_transaction_from_text
>   - extract_obligation_from_text
>   - answer_life_query
> - frontend page: Ask QiLife
> - for now, return mock structured suggestions so the UI and data flow are ready
> 
> Frontend pages:
> 1. Dashboard / Today
> 2. Inbox
> 3. Task Ledger
> 4. Notes
> 5. Knowledge
> 6. People
> 7. Projects
> 8. Money
> 9. Obligations
> 10. Documents
> 11. Ask QiLife
> 12. Settings/About
> 
> Settings/About must include:
> - QiLife is Cody’s personal local-first LifeOps memory system.
> - Inspired by Will Be Done’s weekly planning and task UI.
> - Link to Will Be Done source: https://github.com/will-be-done/will-be-done
> - Preserve license/source notes if any code is copied later.
> 
> Design:
> - dark mode first
> - clean cards with depth
> - visual daily dashboard
> - quick capture always visible
> - low cognitive clutter
> - mobile usable
> - avoid cluttered enterprise UI
> - make it feel like a command center, not a spreadsheet
> 
> Seed data:
> - Cody as person
> - Zaituallah Jan Khebarkhil as person
> - Area seeds: Inbox, Workbench, Timeline, Life, People, Business, Finance, Legal, Tech, Assets, Data, Reference, Archive, System
> - Project: Lyft Income Sprint
> - Project: Surplus Check Recovery
> - Project: QiFinance Intake
> - Task: Finish 11 Lyft rides
> - Task: Check mail for surplus check
> - Note: QiLife needs one central place for tasks, daily log, knowledge, notes, and AI
> - Obligation: Zai owes Cody $40 for gas
> - Transaction: Cody paid gas for Lyft
> - Daily log entry for today summarizing initial setup
> 
> Deliver:
> - working local dev app
> - README with setup commands
> - database schema overview
> - architecture overview
> - future roadmap
> - no real AI API key required yet
> - no auth required yet
> - no bank sync
> - no calendar sync
> - no overbuilding
> 
> Build the spine first.
> 
> # Final call
> 
> This is the app:
> 
> **QiLife is your central memory ledger.**
> 
> Notion is too loose.  
> Todo apps are too narrow.  
> Finance apps are too isolated.  
> AI chat alone forgets too much.  
> Calendar apps only track time.  
> 
> QiLife’s job is to answer:
> 
> > What happened?  
> > What matters?  
> > What do I owe?  
> > Who owes me?  
> > What do I know?  
> > What do I need to do next?
> 
> That is the center.

### User
> lets look at it like this, here is my pain, first What Happened, What Does It Mean, Who/what is related to it, Action Required, Action Done if required, What sub-steps are part of the action, what do I know about it or the actions or related entities that may be relevant, and where should it be slotted in the future, then reflection and retrieval. that sums it up really.

### Assistant
> Yes. That is the cleanest spec yet.
> 
> You just defined the **core lifecycle** of QiLife.
> 
> Not “task management.” Not “notes.” Not “knowledge base.” The unit is an **Incident / Event / Life Entry** that moves through meaning → relationships → action → memory.
> 
> I’d name the core object:
> 
> # Life Event
> 
> Or better:
> 
> # Ledger Entry
> 
> Because it can be anything: a thought, text, bill, task, conflict, phone call, receipt, document, appointment, realization, problem, or obligation.
> 
> ## QiLife Lifecycle
> 
> Every captured thing goes through this pipeline:
> 
> | Stage | Question | System Output |
> |---|---|---|
> | 1. Capture | **What happened?** | Raw entry / note / file / voice |
> | 2. Interpret | **What does it mean?** | Summary, category, importance |
> | 3. Relate | **Who/what is related?** | People, projects, money, docs, areas |
> | 4. Decide | **Is action required?** | Yes/no, action type |
> | 5. Act | **What action is required?** | Task or project |
> | 6. Break Down | **What sub-steps are part of it?** | Checklist / subtasks |
> | 7. Enrich | **What do I know that matters?** | Relevant notes, facts, history, documents |
> | 8. Slot | **Where should this go in the future?** | Today, scheduled date, waiting, someday, archive, KB |
> | 9. Close | **Was action done?** | Completion log / result |
> | 10. Reflect | **What did I learn?** | Reflection, pattern, decision, rule |
> | 11. Retrieve | **Can I find/use this later?** | Searchable memory, links, AI answerability |
> 
> That’s it. That’s the damn app.
> 
> ## The better mental model
> 
> QiLife is not organized around “tasks.”
> 
> It is organized around:
> 
> > **Something happened. Now what?**
> 
> That is your core loop.
> 
> ## Core object: Ledger Entry
> 
> Every item starts as a `ledger_entry`.
> 
> Minimum fields:
> 
> | Field | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | title | short label |
> | raw_capture | what you originally said/saw/imported |
> | summary | cleaned meaning |
> | happened_at | when it happened |
> | captured_at | when it was logged |
> | area | finance, legal, household, tech, etc. |
> | entry_type | event, note, transaction, obligation, document, decision, problem, idea |
> | importance | low, normal, high, critical |
> | emotional_load | none, low, medium, high |
> | action_required | yes/no |
> | status | captured, interpreted, actioned, waiting, done, archived |
> | future_slot | today, scheduled, waiting, someday, knowledge, archive |
> | reflection | what it means after review |
> 
> Then other records branch from it.
> 
> ## Related objects
> 
> A ledger entry can link to:
> 
> - people
> - projects/tasklists
> - tasks
> - subtasks
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - documents
> - notes
> - knowledge records
> - events
> - prior entries
> - future reminders
> 
> This is why the `links` table matters.
> 
> You don’t need a thousand rigid fields. You need flexible relationships.
> 
> ## Example
> 
> Raw capture:
> 
> > “Mom texted again at 6:48am asking about meds even though we need one source of truth.”
> 
> QiLife processes:
> 
> ### What happened?
> 
> Mom texted at 6:48am about medication pickup / coordination.
> 
> ### What does it mean?
> 
> Care coordination request arrived outside the agreed system. Risk of duplicated effort, frustration, and missed handoff.
> 
> ### Related
> 
> - Person: Mom
> - Area: Household / Care Ops
> - Project: Family Operating System
> - Related knowledge: One System Rule
> - Related note: care communication boundaries
> 
> ### Action required?
> 
> Yes.
> 
> ### Action
> 
> Add/update Family Wall item for medication pickup.
> 
> ### Sub-steps
> 
> 1. Confirm whether meds are already picked up.
> 2. Add task to Family Wall.
> 3. Mark responsible person.
> 4. Log result.
> 
> ### Relevant knowledge
> 
> Requests outside FOS are non-binding until entered into the system.
> 
> ### Future slot
> 
> Today / Household Ops / Waiting until confirmed.
> 
> ### Action done?
> 
> Pending.
> 
> ### Reflection
> 
> Repeated early-morning direct texting creates reactive coordination burden. Need reinforce capture protocol.
> 
> ### Retrieval
> 
> Later you can ask:
> 
> > “Show me examples where requests bypassed the Family Operating System.”
> 
> Boom. Evidence, pattern, system improvement.
> 
> ## Another example
> 
> Raw capture:
> 
> > “Zai owes me $40 for gas.”
> 
> ### What happened?
> 
> Cody paid or fronted gas cost involving Zai.
> 
> ### Meaning
> 
> Open money obligation.
> 
> ### Related
> 
> - Person: Zai
> - Area: Finance
> - Project: Shared Household Expenses / Lyft Income Sprint maybe
> - Transaction: gas purchase
> - Obligation: Zai owes Cody $40
> 
> ### Action required?
> 
> Yes.
> 
> ### Action
> 
> Confirm repayment.
> 
> ### Sub-steps
> 
> 1. Add obligation.
> 2. Ask Zai if needed.
> 3. Mark paid when received.
> 4. Create transaction when paid.
> 
> ### Future slot
> 
> Waiting On / Money
> 
> ### Retrieval
> 
> > “Who owes me money?”
> 
> It appears.
> 
> ## This gives us the real schema
> 
> I’d make these the core tables:
> 
> 1. `ledger_entries`
> 2. `people`
> 3. `areas`
> 4. `projects`
> 5. `tasks`
> 6. `subtasks`
> 7. `transactions`
> 8. `obligations`
> 9. `notes`
> 10. `knowledge_records`
> 11. `documents`
> 12. `events`
> 13. `links`
> 14. `reflections`
> 15. `ai_interpretations`
> 
> ## The AI workflow
> 
> The AI should operate as a pipeline:
> 
> ### 1. Interpret
> 
> “What happened and what does it mean?”
> 
> ### 2. Extract
> 
> “Are there tasks, people, obligations, money, dates, documents, or projects?”
> 
> ### 3. Link
> 
> “What is this connected to?”
> 
> ### 4. Recommend
> 
> “What should Cody do?”
> 
> ### 5. Slot
> 
> “Where does this belong?”
> 
> ### 6. Retrieve
> 
> “What existing knowledge is relevant?”
> 
> ### 7. Reflect
> 
> “What pattern or lesson should be remembered?”
> 
> ## Best UI for this
> 
> The main screen should not say “Add Task.”
> 
> It should say:
> 
> # What happened?
> 
> One capture box.
> 
> Then the app returns a review card:
> 
> ## Interpreted Entry
> 
> **Summary:**  
> Mom texted about medication pickup outside the system.
> 
> **Meaning:**  
> Care coordination issue / possible duplicate effort.
> 
> **Related:**  
> Mom, Family Operating System, Household Ops
> 
> **Action required:**  
> Yes
> 
> **Suggested action:**  
> Add pickup confirmation task.
> 
> **Future slot:**  
> Today → Household Ops
> 
> Buttons:
> 
> - Save as log only
> - Create task
> - Create obligation
> - Create note
> - Create transaction
> - Add to knowledge
> - Schedule
> - Ignore
> - Edit
> 
> That is dramatically better than making you decide upfront whether something is a note, task, transaction, or reminder.
> 
> Because in your real life, things don’t arrive pre-labeled. They arrive as chaos nuggets.
> 
> ## Updated product sentence
> 
> Use this:
> 
> **QiLife turns “what happened” into meaning, relationships, actions, memory, and future retrieval.**
> 
> That’s the whole damn thing.
> 
> ## Codex prompt addendum
> 
> Add this to the build prompt:
> 
> QiLife’s core workflow is not task-first. It is event-first.
> 
> Every capture begins with the question: “What happened?”
> 
> The system must then support the following lifecycle:
> 
> 1. What happened?
> 2. What does it mean?
> 3. Who or what is related to it?
> 4. Is action required?
> 5. If action is required, what action is needed?
> 6. What sub-steps are part of that action?
> 7. What existing knowledge about the entry, action, or related entities may be relevant?
> 8. Where should this be slotted for the future?
> 9. Was the action completed?
> 10. What reflection or lesson should be recorded?
> 11. How should it be retrieved later?
> 
> Implement a core `ledger_entries` table representing captured life events/incidents/inputs.
> 
> Fields:
> - id
> - title
> - raw_capture
> - summary
> - meaning
> - happened_at
> - captured_at
> - area_id
> - project_id
> - entry_type
> - importance
> - emotional_load
> - action_required
> - suggested_action
> - future_slot
> - status
> - reflection
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> Entry types:
> - event
> - note
> - problem
> - task_seed
> - transaction_seed
> - obligation_seed
> - document_seed
> - decision
> - idea
> - conversation
> - call
> - message
> - receipt
> - appointment
> - knowledge
> - reflection
> - other
> 
> Statuses:
> - captured
> - interpreted
> - action_required
> - action_created
> - waiting
> - done
> - archived
> 
> Future slots:
> - today
> - this_week
> - scheduled
> - waiting_on
> - someday
> - knowledge_base
> - archive
> - ignore
> 
> Add a Ledger Entry detail page with sections:
> - What Happened
> - What It Means
> - Related People / Projects / Areas / Documents / Money
> - Action Required
> - Subtasks
> - Relevant Knowledge
> - Future Slot
> - Action Done
> - Reflection
> - Retrieval Tags / Links
> 
> The AI service layer should include placeholder functions:
> - interpret_ledger_entry
> - extract_related_entities
> - suggest_actions
> - generate_subtasks
> - find_relevant_knowledge
> - suggest_future_slot
> - summarize_for_retrieval
> - generate_reflection_prompt
> 
> The primary capture UI should be called “What Happened?” not “Add Task.”
> 
> ## Final truth
> 
> This is the key unlock:
> 
> **Your life app should not force you to know what something is before you capture it.**
> 
> You capture what happened.
> 
> The system helps decide:
> 
> - what it means
> - who/what it touches
> - whether action is required
> - what steps exist
> - what knowledge matters
> - where it goes
> - how it gets remembered
> 
> That is QiLife.

### Assistant
> Yes — **that’s the ontology.** We’re right on top of it.
> 
> The object is not just a “life event.” It’s smaller and more flexible than that.
> 
> A “life event” sounds like birthday, court date, hospital visit, big thing.
> 
> But what you’re capturing could be:
> 
> - a thought
> - a task seed
> - a text message
> - a receipt
> - a problem
> - a decision
> - a question
> - a promise
> - a pattern
> - a document
> - a tiny friction
> - a “wait, that matters” moment
> 
> So the core unit should be broader.
>

>

> 
> A **QiBit** is one unit of life data.
> 
> It can become:
> 
> - a task
> - a note
> - a transaction
> - an obligation
> - a knowledge item
> - a daily log entry
> - a project update
> - a reflection
> - a future reminder
>

> # The QiBit Framework
> 
> Here’s the clean framework:
> 
> | Question | Function | QiLife Field |
> |---|---|---|
> | **What?** | Capture | raw capture / title / summary |
> | **Where?** | Bucket | area / project / list |
> | **Why?** | Interpret | meaning / importance / reason |
> | **Who?** | Relate | people / entities |
> | **When?** | Slot | date / schedule / future slot |
> | **How?** | Breakdown | action / subtasks / process |
> | **Because?** | Enrich | relevant knowledge / context / evidence |
> | **Then?** | Act | task / obligation / next step |
> | **Done?** | Close | completion / result |
> | **So what?** | Reflect | lesson / pattern / decision |
> | **Find later?** | Retrieve | tags / links / AI memory |
> 
> That’s the whole engine.
> 
> Cleaner version:
> 
> # QiBit Lifecycle
> 
> 1. **Capture** — what happened?
> 2. **Bucket** — where does it belong?
> 3. **Interpret** — what does it mean?
> 4. **Relate** — who/what is connected?
> 5. **Slot** — when does it matter?
> 6. **Breakdown** — how do we act on it?
> 7. **Enrich** — what context matters?
> 8. **Act** — what gets done?
> 9. **Close** — what happened after action?
> 10. **Reflect** — what did we learn?
> 11. **Retrieve** — how do we find/use it later?
> 
> That is tight.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The key object
> 
> Call the database table:
> 
> `qibits`
> 
> Not `ledger_entries`.
> 
> Why? Because it’s yours, and it avoids sounding like accounting software.
> 
> Fields:
> 
> | Field | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | id | unique ID |
> | title | short label |
> | raw_capture | original input |
> | summary | cleaned version |
> | meaning | interpretation |
> | qibit_type | note, event, task_seed, transaction_seed, obligation_seed, decision, idea, problem, document, reflection |
> | area_id | where it belongs |
> | project_id | related project/list |
> | importance | low, normal, high, critical |
> | emotional_load | none, low, medium, high |
> | action_required | yes/no |
> | suggested_action | what to do |
> | future_slot | today, this week, scheduled, waiting, someday, archive |
> | happened_at | when it happened |
> | captured_at | when logged |
> | status | captured, interpreted, actioned, waiting, done, archived |
> | retrieval_summary | how AI should remember it |
> | reflection | lesson/pattern |
> | created_at | timestamp |
> | updated_at | timestamp |
> 
> Then link outward to:
> 
> - people
> - tasks
> - subtasks
> - notes
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - documents
> - knowledge
> - events
> 
> ---
> 
> # The better naming system
> 
> Use this language:
> 
> ## QiBit
> 
> A single captured unit of life data.
> 
> ## Bucket
> 
> Where it belongs.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - Finance
> - Legal
> - Household
> - Work
> - Tech
> - People
> - Health/admin
> - Archive
> 
> ## Thread
> 
> A group of related QiBits over time.
> 
> Example:
> 
> - Surplus Check Thread
> - Jeep Repair Thread
> - Zai Rent Thread
> - Family Ops Thread
> 
> This might be better than “project” in some contexts.
> 
> ## Action
> 
> Something to do.
> 
> ## Step
> 
> A sub-action.
> 
> ## Context
> 
> Relevant knowledge, evidence, history, or related facts.
> 
> ## Reflection
> 
> What was learned.
> 
> ## Memory
> 
> The retrieval layer.
> 
> ---
> 
> # This gives you a beautiful app flow
> 
> Main screen:
> 
> # What happened?
> 
> You type:
> 
> > “I filled up gas for Lyft but had to use other money to get a drink because I didn’t have enough left.”
> 
> QiLife responds:
> 
> ## QiBit Created
> 
> ### What
> Gas/cashflow issue during Lyft shift.
> 
> ### Where
> Finance → Work → Lyft Income Sprint
> 
> ### Why
> Cashflow friction: fuel and basic needs are colliding during income generation.
> 
> ### Who
> Cody
> 
> ### When
> Today
> 
> ### How
> Suggested action:
> 1. Log gas transaction.
> 2. Track drink expense separately.
> 3. Update Lyft shift cost.
> 4. Check whether today’s ride target still covers rental/gas.
> 
> ### Because
> Relevant context:
> - Lyft income sprint is tied to rental/registration pressure.
> - Gas eats roughly 30% of driver income.
> - Phone mount issue affects driving safety and efficiency.
> 
> ### Then
> Action required: yes.
> 
> ### Future slot
> Today / Work / Money
> 
> ### Reflection prompt
> “Was the Lyft sprint profitable after gas and survival expenses?”
> 
> That’s the whole damn thing, and it’s actually useful.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Better than “task”
> 
> The magic is that the user does **not** start by deciding:
> 
> “Is this a task, note, event, transaction, or journal entry?”
> 
> They start with:
> 
> > **What happened?**
> 
> QiLife figures out what it might become.
> 
> That is exactly how your brain needs it to work.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Naming verdict
> 
> Use:
> 
> ## **QiBit**
> The atomic unit.
> 
> ## **Thread**
> A connected storyline/project.
> 
> ## **Bucket**
> The area/category.
> 
> ## **Action**
> The task.
> 
> ## **Step**
> The subtask.
> 
> ## **Memory**
> The retrieval/knowledge layer.
> 
> The structure becomes:
> 
> > QiBits live in Buckets, connect into Threads, produce Actions and Steps, enrich Memory, and feed Reflection.
> 
> That is clean and very you.
> 
> Final product sentence:
> 
> **QiLife captures QiBits, connects them to people and threads, turns them into actions, and builds searchable memory from what actually happened.**

### User
> QiBit is perfect, so what would the spine be, timeline like we were doing before, thats honestly the most logical.

### Assistant
> Yes. **Timeline is the spine.** That’s the most logical structure because your pain is fundamentally temporal:
> 
> > What happened → what does it mean → what needs to happen next → what happened after that?
> 
> That is a timeline problem with intelligence layered on top.
> 
> # QiLife Spine
> 
> ## 1. Timeline
> 
> The master view.
> 
> Everything enters the system as a **QiBit** and appears on the timeline.
> 
> A QiBit can be:
> 
> - note
> - message
> - event
> - task seed
> - transaction seed
> - obligation
> - document
> - decision
> - problem
> - idea
> - reflection
> - completed action
> - “something happened”
> 
> The timeline answers:
> 
> > What happened, in order?
> 
> This becomes your source of truth.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. Buckets
> 
> Buckets answer:
> 
> > Where does this belong?
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - Life
> - People
> - Finance
> - Legal
> - Household
> - Work
> - Tech
> - Assets
> - Data
> - Reference
> - Archive
> 
> A QiBit lives on the timeline, but it can be bucketed into an area.
> 
> So instead of folders being the main structure, **time is the spine, buckets are filters**.
> 
> That is the correct architecture.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Threads
> 
> Threads answer:
> 
> > What storyline is this part of?
> 
> A thread is a connected chain of QiBits.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - Surplus Check
> - Lyft Income Sprint
> - Zai Lease / Rent
> - Family Operating System
> - Jeep Repairs
> - QiServer Cleanup
> - Mom Care Notes
> - Phone Replacement
> - QiFinance Intake
> 
> This is better than only “projects,” because not everything is a project.
> 
> Some things are cases. Some are problems. Some are relationships. Some are ongoing life threads.
> 
> Use:
> 
> **Thread = project / case / storyline / issue / initiative**
> 
> That’s flexible.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. Actions
> 
> Actions answer:
> 
> > What needs to be done?
> 
> Actions are tasks, but more grounded.
> 
> A QiBit may create:
> 
> - one action
> - many actions
> - no action
> - a waiting item
> - a recurring action
> - a checklist
> 
> Actions can have steps.
> 
> Example:
> 
> QiBit: “Phone mount broke / unsafe driving setup.”
> 
> Action:
> 
> > Get working phone mount today.
> 
> Steps:
> 
> 1. Find open store nearby.
> 2. Buy cheapest usable mount.
> 3. Install before Lyft rides.
> 4. Log expense.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. Memory
> 
> Memory answers:
> 
> > What do I know that matters here?
> 
> Memory includes:
> 
> - notes
> - knowledge records
> - documents
> - evidence
> - prior QiBits
> - people context
> - previous decisions
> - rules
> - patterns
> 
> This is where AI becomes useful.
> 
> Example:
> 
> You capture:
> 
> > “Mom texted asking about something again.”
> 
> QiLife can surface:
> 
> - Family Operating System rule
> - prior related notes
> - current open household tasks
> - communication boundary pattern
> - suggested action
> 
> That’s the difference between “note app” and “operating system.”
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. Reflection
> 
> Reflection answers:
> 
> > What did I learn from this?
> 
> This is not fluff. This is pattern recognition.
> 
> Reflection can generate:
> 
> - lesson
> - decision
> - boundary
> - rule
> - improvement
> - “watch this pattern”
> - update to knowledge base
> 
> Example:
> 
> > Repeated unstructured requests create cognitive load. Route future requests through Family Wall when possible.
> 
> That becomes reusable knowledge.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The actual spine diagram
> 
> Use this:
> 
> **Timeline → QiBits → Buckets → Threads → Actions → Steps → Memory → Reflection → Retrieval**
> 
> Or more naturally:
> 
> 1. **Capture QiBit**
> 2. **Place on Timeline**
> 3. **Assign Bucket**
> 4. **Connect to Thread**
> 5. **Interpret Meaning**
> 6. **Relate People/Objects**
> 7. **Create Actions**
> 8. **Break into Steps**
> 9. **Enrich with Memory**
> 10. **Slot Future**
> 11. **Close/Log Result**
> 12. **Reflect**
> 13. **Retrieve Later**
> 
> That’s the app.
> 
> ---
>

> Command center.

> Shows:

> - reflection prompt

> Chronological life ledger.
> 
> Filters:
>

> - by money/obligation
> - by document
> - by emotional load
> - by importance
> 
> ## Inbox
> 
> Unprocessed QiBits.
> 
> This is the chaos catcher.
> 
> ## Threads
> 
> Ongoing storylines.
> 
> Each thread has:
> 
> - timeline
> - actions
> - people
> - documents
> - money
> - notes
> - AI summary
> - status
> 
> ## Actions
> 
> Task ledger.
> 
> Views:
> 
> - today
> - next
> - waiting
> - blocked
> - scheduled
> - done
> - by context
> - by bucket
> - by thread
> 
> ## People
> 
> Lightweight relationship/context records.
> 
> No CRM bloat.
> 
> ## Money
> 
> Transactions and obligations.
> 
> ## Knowledge
> 
> Durable reference information.
> 
> ## Ask QiLife
> 
> AI connected to everything.
>
