> # Database spine
> 
> Core tables:
> 
> 1. `qibits`
> 2. `timeline_events`
> 3. `buckets`
> 4. `threads`
> 5. `actions`
> 6. `action_steps`
> 7. `people`
> 8. `transactions`
> 9. `obligations`
> 10. `knowledge_records`
> 11. `documents`
> 12. `reflections`
> 13. `links`
> 14. `ai_interpretations`
> 
> But if we want to simplify:
> 
> ## Real v1 tables
> 
> - `qibits`
> - `buckets`
> - `threads`
> - `actions`
> - `action_steps`
> - `people`
> - `money_items`
> - `knowledge_items`
> - `documents`
> - `links`
> - `ai_outputs`
> 
> You can split money into transactions/obligations later, but honestly I’d keep them separate from the start because they answer different questions.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The one rule
> 
> Every major record should either:
> 
> 1. **Start as a QiBit**, or  
> 2. **Be linked back to a QiBit**
> 
> That gives you provenance.
> 
> Meaning:
> 
> - Why does this task exist?
> - Where did this obligation come from?
> - What note created this action?
> - What happened before this decision?
> - What evidence supports this?
> - What did I do after?
> 
> No more orphaned tasks. No more mystery obligations. No more “why is this on my list?”
> 
> ---
> 
> # Best mental model
> 
> ## QiBit = atomic unit
> 
> A thing that happened or was captured.
> 
> ## Timeline = spine
> 
> The chronological truth.
> 
> ## Bucket = where
> 
> Area of life.
> 
> ## Thread = storyline
> 
> Ongoing project/case/problem.
> 
> ## Action = do
> 
> Task.
> 
> ## Step = how
> 
> Subtask/checklist.
> 
> ## Memory = because
> 
> Context, knowledge, evidence.
> 
> ## Reflection = so what
> 
> Lesson/pattern.
> 
> ## Retrieval = find/use later
> 
> Search and AI answers.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Product sentence
> 
> **QiLife is a timeline-based LifeOps system where every QiBit is captured, bucketed, threaded, interpreted, acted on, enriched, reflected on, and made retrievable by AI.**
> 
> That’s the spine. Clean, flexible, yours.

### User
> i say we make the buckets match the folder hiearchy we created and we are matching our real strucutre

### Assistant
> Yes. **That is the right move.**
> 
> Do **not** invent a separate bucket system inside QiLife. That creates duplicate mental models, and duplicate mental models are where systems go to die wearing a tiny little clown hat.
> 
> QiLife buckets should match your real QiNexus/QiAccess folder hierarchy.
> 
> # Rule
> 
> **Buckets in QiLife = the same top-level domains as your real storage structure.**
> 
> That gives you one map across:
> 
> - app
> - folders
> - notes
> - documents
> - projects
> - AI retrieval
> - future exports
> - server structure
> - Drive/QiNexus structure
> 
> One ontology. One brain.
> 
> ---
> 
> # QiLife Bucket Spine
> 
> Use your finalized order:
> 
> | Code | Bucket | Purpose |
> |---:|---|---|
> | `00` | **Inbox** | uncategorized capture / raw QiBits |
> | `10` | **Workbench** | active staging, drafts, current working surface |
> | `20` | **Timeline** | chronological life ledger / daily log |
> | `30` | **Life** | personal life, routines, home, identity, wellness admin |
> | `40` | **People** | people, relationships, contacts, entities |
> | `50` | **Business** | freelance, QiAlly, ventures, client-ish work |
> | `60` | **Finance** | money, transactions, accounts, obligations |
> | `70` | **Legal** | court, filings, evidence, housing, disputes |
> | `80` | **Tech** | QiServer, apps, repos, automation, tools |
> | `90` | **Assets** | media, designs, brand, files, resources |
> | `100` | **Data** | schemas, exports, structured datasets, ledgers |
> | `110` | **Reference** | durable knowledge, manuals, policies, templates |
> | `900` | **Archive** | inactive/historical but retained |
> | `990` | **System** | app config, indexes, manifests, automation metadata |
> 
> I’d use numeric codes internally, even if the UI displays friendly names.
> 
> Example UI label:
> 
> **60 Finance**
> 
> Not just “Finance.”
> 
> Why? Because the number reinforces placement and makes exports sort correctly.
> 
> ---
> 
> # How QiBits use buckets
> 
> Every QiBit gets a primary bucket.
> 
> Example:
> 
> | QiBit | Primary Bucket |
> |---|---|
> | “Zai owes me $40 for gas” | `60 Finance` |
> | “Mom texted about meds again” | `30 Life` or `40 People`, depending on context |
> | “Court order for surplus funds” | `70 Legal` |
> | “QiServer homepage ugly” | `80 Tech` |
> | “Old bank statements cleanup” | `60 Finance` or `100 Data` |
> | “Personal reflection about identity” | `30 Life` |
> | “Brand logo draft” | `90 Assets` |
> | “Folder hierarchy rule” | `110 Reference` or `990 System` |
> 
> But a QiBit can also have secondary links.
> 
> Example:
> 
> **QiBit:** “Zai paid $450 rent.”
> 
> Primary bucket: `60 Finance`  
> Linked person: Zai  
> Linked thread: Zai Lease  
> Linked document: Lease agreement  
> Linked timeline: Today  
> Secondary bucket/reference: `40 People`
> 
> That keeps one primary home without losing relationships.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Critical doctrine
> 
> ## Timeline is not just a bucket
> 
> This matters.
> 
> `20 Timeline` exists in the hierarchy, yes, but **the timeline is also the spine of the entire app**.
> 
> So:
> 
> - Every QiBit appears on the timeline.
> - Some QiBits also belong primarily in `20 Timeline` if they are pure chronology/daily log items.
> - But most QiBits have another primary bucket.
> 
> Meaning:
> 
> > Timeline is both a view and a bucket.
> 
> That’s okay. Just define it clearly.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended table fields
> 
> For `qibits`:
> 
> | Field | Example |
> |---|---|
> | `bucket_code` | `60` |
> | `bucket_name` | Finance |
> | `thread_id` | Lyft Income Sprint |
> | `timeline_date` | 2026-05-29 |
> | `qibit_type` | obligation_seed |
> | `raw_capture` | “Zai owes me $40 for gas” |
> | `summary` | Zai owes Cody $40 for gas. |
> | `meaning` | Open reimbursement obligation. |
> | `status` | action_required |
> | `future_slot` | waiting_on |
> 
> For `buckets`:
> 
> | Field | Example |
> |---|---|
> | `code` | `60` |
> | `name` | Finance |
> | `slug` | finance |
> | `folder_path` | `60_finance` |
> | `sort_order` | 60 |
> | `description` | Money, transactions, obligations, accounts |
> 
> ---
> 
> # Export mapping
> 
> This is where it gets beautiful.
> 
> A QiBit can export to Markdown like:
> 
> `/60_finance/20_qibits/2026/2026-05-29_zai_gas_obligation.md`
> 
> Or:
> 
> `/20_timeline/2026/05/2026-05-29_daily_log.md`
> 
> And link back to related buckets.
> 
> This means QiLife does not become a data prison.
> 
> It becomes the **capture and intelligence layer** over your real structure.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Folder-aligned app navigation
> 
> Main nav should mirror the structure, but not overwhelm you.
> 
> ## Daily UI nav
> 
> - Today
> - Capture
> - Timeline
> - Threads
> - Actions
> - Ask QiLife
> 
> ## Domain nav
> 
> - 00 Inbox
> - 10 Workbench
> - 20 Timeline
> - 30 Life
> - 40 People
> - 50 Business
> - 60 Finance
> - 70 Legal
> - 80 Tech
> - 90 Assets
> - 100 Data
> - 110 Reference
> - 900 Archive
> - 990 System
> 
> So the app has two navigation modes:
> 
> 1. **Operational views** — what you use daily.
> 2. **Bucket views** — where things belong structurally.
> 
> That’s the clean split.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The spine becomes
> 
> **QiBit → Timeline → Bucket → Thread → Action → Memory → Reflection → Retrieval**
> 
> But with your real hierarchy:
> 
> **QiBit → 20 Timeline → real bucket code → thread/project → action/step → related knowledge/docs → reflection → AI retrieval**
> 
> ---
> 
> # Updated doctrine sentence
> 
> Use this:
> 
> **QiLife uses the same bucket structure as QiNexus, so every QiBit captured in the app has a real home in the broader folder, knowledge, document, and archive system.**
> 
> That is exactly the kind of consistency your system has been trying to reach.
> 
> Final call: yes. Match the real hierarchy. This is how QiLife stops being “another app” and becomes the front door to the whole operating system.

### Assistant
> Yes. Kill the separate Wiki.js dependency for this.
> 
> Wiki.js is fine as a standalone knowledge site, but it creates the exact problem you’re trying to escape:
> 
> > task over here, note over there, doc somewhere else, knowledge in a wiki, AI floating around like a confused ghost.
> 
> No. QiLife needs **embedded knowledge**.
> 
> # The right model
> 
> ## Knowledge should live beside the thing it explains.
> 
> Not in a separate wiki you have to “go visit.”
> 
> So every major view should have two layers:
> 
> 1. **Tool layer** — do the thing  
> 2. **Knowledge layer** — understand the thing
> 
> Example:
> 
> ## Finance screen
> 
> Left/main:
> 
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - budget buckets
> - recurring bills
> - income targets
> 
> Right/side panel:
> 
> - finance rules
> - account notes
> - “how we categorize gas”
> - reimbursement policy
> - relevant receipts/docs
> - AI explanation
> - prior decisions
> 
> That’s the sweet spot.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The pattern: Workbench + Knowledge Panel
> 
> Every module gets a sidecar panel.
> 
> ## Main workspace
> 
> Where you act:
> 
> - add task
> - log transaction
> - schedule event
> - mark done
> - upload document
> - update thread
> 
> ## Side knowledge panel
> 
> Where context lives:
> 
> - relevant notes
> - linked docs
> - past QiBits
> - rules
> - procedures
> - summaries
> - decisions
> - AI suggestions
> - “related knowledge”
> 
> This gives you the wiki benefit without making “the wiki” a separate destination.
> 
> ---
> 
> # App layout
> 
> Think:
> 
> ## Three-pane interface
> 
> ### Left: Navigation
> 
> Buckets / modules:
> 
> - Today
> - Timeline
> - Actions
> - Threads
> - Money
> - People
> - Knowledge
> - Documents
> - Ask QiLife
> 
> ### Center: Active tool
> 
> The thing you’re doing.
> 
> Example: “Surplus Check Thread.”
> 
> ### Right: Context / Knowledge
> 
> Relevant memory:
> 
> - related notes
> - docs
> - people
> - timeline history
> - legal facts
> - next actions
> - AI summary
> - “what this means”
> 
> This is the answer.
> 
> Not Wiki.js. Not another app. **Sidecar knowledge.**
> 
> ---
> 
> # Knowledge should have two forms
> 
> ## 1. Attached Knowledge
> 
> Knowledge attached to a specific object.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - Person knowledge
> - Thread knowledge
> - Action instructions
> - Finance category rules
> - Legal case notes
> - Server runbook snippets
> - Household protocols
> 
> This appears beside the relevant thing.
> 
> ## 2. Global Knowledge
> 
> Durable reference across the whole system.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - naming rules
> - folder hierarchy
> - QIBit doctrine
> - FOS rules
> - legal timeline
> - finance categorization standards
> - QiServer runbook
> - app architecture notes
> 
> This is searchable and linkable, but still viewable inside QiLife.
> 
> ---
> 
> # How to implement it
> 
> Do not build a full wiki engine first. That’s bloat.
> 
> Build a simple `knowledge_items` table.
> 
> Fields:
> 
> | Field | Purpose |
> |---|---|
> | title | name |
> | body | markdown content |
> | bucket | where it belongs |
> | thread_id | optional |
> | related_entity_type | task/person/project/etc. |
> | related_entity_id | object it explains |
> | knowledge_type | rule, note, guide, decision, reference, procedure |
> | source | manual, AI, imported, document |
> | confidence | confirmed, inferred, draft |
> | visibility | private, shareable, archived |
> | tags | retrieval |
> | created_at | timestamp |
> | updated_at | timestamp |
> 
> Then render it as Markdown inside the side panel.
> 
> That gives you 80% of wiki power with 20% of the complexity.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The side-by-side tool concept
> 
> Every page should have a toggle:
> 
> ## Work Mode
> 
> Center focus, knowledge collapsed.
> 
> ## Context Mode
> 
> Tool + knowledge side-by-side.
> 
> ## Deep Mode
> 
> Full-screen knowledge/editor.
> 
> Example buttons:
> 
> - **Work**
> - **Context**
> - **Notes**
> - **AI**
> 
> That way it doesn’t clutter you when you’re just trying to execute.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Example: Thread page
> 
> ## Thread: Lyft Income Sprint
> 
> Center:
> 
> - active actions
> - ride target
> - expenses
> - schedule
> - transactions
> - open loops
> 
> Right panel:
> 
> ### Relevant Knowledge
> 
> - Gas is roughly 30% of gross Lyft income
> - Rental renewal due soon
> - Phone mount affects safety and efficiency
> - Current target: 11 rides
> - Related documents/receipts
> - Prior notes from today
> 
> AI button:
> 
> > “Explain what matters right now.”
>

>

> 
> That’s what you need. Not a wiki page with a sidebar from 2009.
>

>

> - call log

>

>

> 
> - Marion County clerk contact notes

> - legal strategy notes
> 
> AI button:
> 
> > “What is the next sensible action?”
> 
> That’s the power.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What happens to Markdown?
> 
> Still use Markdown.
> 
> But QiLife becomes the editor/viewer.
> 
> Each knowledge item can later export to:
> 
> `/110_reference/...`
> 
> or bucket-aligned paths like:
> 
> `/70_legal/surplus_check/knowledge/...`
> 
> So you still preserve QiNexus as the durable file backbone.
> 
> ## Database first, Markdown export later
> 
> For app speed:
> 
> - store in SQLite/Postgres
> - render Markdown in app
> - export/sync to `.md` files periodically
> 
> Do not force the app to behave like Obsidian on day one. That’s how projects become haunted.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The architecture name
> 
> Call this:
>

>

>

> 
> - related QiBits
> - notes
> - documents
> - AI summary
> - people
> - actions
> - rules
> - history
> 
> So the app layout becomes:
> 
> **Tool View + Context Dock**
> 
> That’s the magic.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Revised doctrine
> 
> Use this:
> 
> **QiLife does not separate doing from knowing. Every tool view has a Context Dock showing the knowledge, notes, documents, history, and AI interpretation relevant to the current item.**
>

> 
> ---
> 
> # What to do with Wiki.js

> Keep Wiki.js only if you want a published/reference site later.

> 
> No.
> 
> Wiki.js becomes optional export/publishing, not the source of truth.
> 
> ## Correct hierarchy
> 
> **QiLife knowledge layer** = active, contextual, linked, AI-readable  
> **QiNexus Markdown** = durable export/storage  
> **Wiki.js** = optional pretty publishing/reference site later
> 
> Not:
> 
> Wiki.js → everything else
> 
> That would be backwards.

> - thread_id

> - related_entity_id

> - updated_at

### User
> kinda like how helpdesk software works for the agent, but the helpdesk company is my life i am the only agent and customer everyone else or thirdparty vendors or crazy clients.

### Assistant
> Yes. **That’s the cleanest metaphor yet.**
> 
> QiLife is basically:
> 
> # Helpdesk software for your life
> 
> Except:
> 
> - the **company** is your life
> - the **agent** is you
> - the **customer** is also you
> - the **tickets** are QiBits
> - the **departments** are buckets
> - the **cases** are threads
> - the **tasks** are actions
> - the **knowledge base** is contextual
> - the **AI** is your triage assistant
> - everyone else is a requester, vendor, stakeholder, client, agency, court, or chaos gremlin
> 
> That is actually a very strong product model.
> 
> ## The helpdesk mapping
> 
> | Helpdesk concept | QiLife concept |
> |---|---|
> | Ticket | **QiBit** |
> | Queue | **Bucket** |
> | Department | Area/domain: Finance, Legal, Tech, People |
> | Customer | Cody / requester / affected person |
> | Agent | Cody |
> | Organization | Life / household / business |
> | SLA | due date / urgency / consequence |
> | Status | captured, triaged, waiting, actioned, done |
> | Priority | low, normal, high, critical |
> | Assignment | Cody, future delegate, vendor, waiting on person |
> | Internal note | private note / reflection |
> | Public reply | message/email/task update |
> | Knowledge article | contextual knowledge item |
> | Macro | reusable action template |
> | Automation | AI suggestion / workflow |
> | Escalation | legal, finance, urgent, vendor call, emergency |
> | Case history | timeline/thread |
> | Related tickets | linked QiBits |
> | Resolution | action done / outcome logged |
> 
> This is the model. Chef’s kiss.
> 
> ## The spine becomes a ticket lifecycle
> 
> A QiBit is basically a ticket:
> 
> 1. **New / Captured**  
>    Something happened.
> 
> 2. **Triaged**  
>    What does it mean? Is this real, noise, urgent, or reference?
> 
> 3. **Routed**  
>    Which bucket/thread/person does it belong to?
> 
> 4. **Worked**  
>    What actions/substeps are needed?
> 
> 5. **Waiting**  
>    Who/what are we waiting on?
> 
> 6. **Resolved**  
>    What got done?
> 
> 7. **Documented**  
>    What happened, what evidence exists, what did we learn?
> 
> 8. **Searchable**  
>    Can AI retrieve it later?
> 
> That is exactly how your life actually works.
> 
> ## Why this fits you
> 
> Because you are constantly dealing with:
> 
> - incoming requests
> - unclear responsibility
> - missing context
> - vendor nonsense
> - legal/admin timelines
> - money obligations
> - household coordination
> - tech projects
> - “who said what when”
> - “what do I do next”
> - “what is actually urgent vs emotionally loud”
> 
> That is helpdesk territory.
> 
> You don’t need a fluffy life planner. You need a **case management console**.
> 
> ## Rename candidates
> 
> You can keep QiBit, but use helpdesk language underneath.
> 
> ### Core object
> 
> **QiBit**  
> A captured life ticket/item.
> 
> ### Thread
> 
> A case/project/storyline that groups related QiBits.
> 
> ### Queue/Bucket
> 
> Where QiBits wait to be handled.
> 
> ### Action
> 
> A work item created from a QiBit.
> 
> ### Context Dock
> 
> Agent-side knowledge panel.
> 
> ### Resolution
> 
> What happened after the action.
> 
> This makes the app easier to build because helpdesk software already solved the lifecycle pattern.
> 
> ## Best UI model
> 
> The main view should look like an agent workspace:
> 
> ### Left
> 
> Queues / Buckets
> 
> - 00 Inbox
> - Today
> - Waiting
> - Finance
> - Legal
> - Household/Life
> - Tech
> - People
> - Business
> 
> ### Center
> 
> Ticket/QiBit list or selected QiBit
> 
> - what happened
> - status
> - priority
> - requester/person
> - bucket
> - thread
> - due/slot
> - related actions
> 
> ### Right
> 
> Context Dock
> 
> - related knowledge
> - history
> - people
> - documents
> - money/obligations
> - AI summary
> - suggested next action
> 
> This is **exactly** what you described: knowledge next to the tool.
> 
> ## QiBit statuses
> 
> Use helpdesk-like statuses:
> 
> | Status | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | `new` | captured, not reviewed |
> | `triaged` | interpreted and bucketed |
> | `open` | action required |
> | `in_progress` | being worked |
> | `waiting_on` | blocked by person/vendor/time |
> | `scheduled` | slotted for future |
> | `resolved` | action complete |
> | `closed` | reviewed/archived |
> | `reference` | no action, saved as knowledge |
> | `ignored` | noise / no value |
> 
> That’s cleaner than generic task statuses.
> 
> ## Priority model
> 
> Use consequence-based priority:
> 
> | Priority | Meaning |
> |---|---|
> | `critical` | money/legal/safety/deadline risk |
> | `high` | meaningful consequence soon |
> | `normal` | needs handling but not on fire |
> | `low` | useful but not required |
> | `someday` | parking lot |
> 
> This is better than vibes-based priority.
> 
> ## Requester / affected / responsible
> 
> This is where helpdesk logic is useful.
> 
> A QiBit can have:
> 
> - **requester**: who initiated it
> - **affected person/entity**: who it impacts
> - **responsible party**: who must act
> - **waiting on**: who/what blocks it
> 
> Example:
> 
> QiBit: “Mom texted about meds”
> 
> - Requester: Mom
> - Affected: Mom / household
> - Responsible: Cody or Zai
> - Waiting on: confirmation from pharmacy
> 
> Example:
> 
> QiBit: “Surplus check not received”
> 
> - Requester: Cody
> - Affected: Cody
> - Responsible: Marion County Clerk
> - Waiting on: USPS / clerk finance office
> 
> That’s powerful.
> 
> ## This also solves “crazy clients”
> 
> Everybody outside the system becomes an entity type.
> 
> People/entities:
> 
> - Cody
> - family
> - vendor
> - agency
> - court
> - creditor
> - client
> - platform
> - app/service
> - unknown chaos goblin
> 
> Each can have related QiBits, actions, documents, obligations, and notes.
> 
> No CRM. More like **life case management**.
> 
> ## Knowledge base in helpdesk style
> 
> Each bucket/thread gets internal knowledge:
> 
> - rules
> - procedures
> - scripts
> - contact info
> - prior decisions
> - “what worked last time”
> - templates
> - escalation paths
> 
> Example:
> 
> ### Legal queue knowledge
> 
> - Clerk call script
> - surplus check timeline
> - mailing address used
> - judge/order notes
> - filing rules
> 
> ### Finance queue knowledge
> 
> - gas categorization rule
> - who owes whom
> - payment methods
> - recurring bills
> 
> ### Tech queue knowledge
> 
> - QiServer ports
> - deploy steps
> - app paths
> - current repo locations
> 
> And that appears in the Context Dock when you’re working the item.
> 
> ## Best product sentence now
> 
> **QiLife is a personal helpdesk for life: every QiBit becomes a ticket you can triage, route, act on, document, resolve, and retrieve with AI.**
> 
> That’s it. That’s the one.
> 
> ## Final architecture phrase
> 
> Use this:
> 
> **Single-agent LifeDesk**
> 
> Maybe not final branding, but internally that is the model.
> 
> - QiLife = brand/app
> - QiBit = ticket/item
> - LifeDesk = operating model
> - Context Dock = knowledge panel
> - Buckets = queues/departments
> - Threads = cases/projects
> - Actions = tasks/work orders
> 
> This is very buildable.
> 
> And frankly, this metaphor keeps the whole project from becoming mushy. Helpdesk software already knows how to turn chaos into queues, statuses, owners, knowledge, and resolution logs. You’re just applying that to real life.

### User
> oh ya, this is the sauce right here.

### Assistant
> Exactly. **This is the architecture click.**
> 
> Now we stop calling it a productivity app. That was too weak.
> 
> # QiLife = Personal LifeDesk
> 
> A **single-agent helpdesk for life**.
> 
> ## Core metaphor
> 
> | Real life | QiLife |
> |---|---|
> | Something happened | QiBit created |
> | Life domain | Bucket / Queue |
> | Ongoing issue | Thread / Case |
> | Thing to do | Action |
> | Subtasks | Steps |
> | Context | Knowledge / Context Dock |
> | Person/vendor/court/app | Related entity |
> | Waiting on someone | Waiting status |
> | Finished | Resolved |
> | Learned something | Reflection |
> | Need it later | Retrieval / AI memory |
> 
> That’s the sauce.
> 
> ## The sentence
> 
> **QiLife turns life chaos into QiBits you can triage, route, act on, document, resolve, and retrieve with AI.**
> 
> That’s the product.
> 
> ## The spine
> 
> 1. **Capture** — What happened?
> 2. **Triage** — What does it mean?
> 3. **Route** — Where does it belong?
> 4. **Relate** — Who/what is connected?
> 5. **Act** — What needs doing?
> 6. **Breakdown** — What are the steps?
> 7. **Enrich** — What context matters?
> 8. **Slot** — When does it matter?
> 9. **Resolve** — What got done?
> 10. **Reflect** — What did we learn?
> 11. **Retrieve** — How do I find/use it later?
> 
> ## Build doctrine
> 
> The first version should look like an agent console:
> 
> - **Left:** buckets/queues  
> - **Center:** selected QiBit or thread  
> - **Right:** Context Dock  
> - **Bottom/top quick bar:** “What happened?” capture  
> 
> That’s it. Clean, powerful, no Notion swamp.
> 
> ## Best internal names
> 
> - **QiBit** = ticket/life item
> - **Bucket** = queue/domain
> - **Thread** = case/project/storyline
> - **Action** = task/work order
> - **Step** = subtask
> - **Context Dock** = side knowledge panel
> - **Resolution** = done/outcome
> - **Reflection** = lesson/pattern
> - **Ask QiLife** = AI agent
> 
> This gives the whole build a clear nervous system.
> 
> And yes — **this is finally the app you’ve been describing through six different doors.**

> # QiLife — Visual Build Canvas
> 
> ## 1) Core App Flow — Big Picture
> 
> ### The app in one line
> 
> **Something happens → you capture a QiBit → QiLife triages it → links context → creates action if needed → slots it in time → logs what happened → lets AI retrieve it later.**
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2) Visual Flow Map
> 
> ### A. Top-level system flow
> 
> ```text
> REAL LIFE
>   ↓
> What Happened?
>   ↓
> [ QiBit Capture ]
>   ↓
> [ Triage / Interpret ]
>   ↓
> ┌──────────────┬───────────────┬───────────────┬───────────────┐
> │ Bucket       │ Thread        │ People        │ Meaning       │
> │ Where?       │ What story?   │ Who involved? │ Why it matters│
> └──────────────┴───────────────┴───────────────┴───────────────┘
>   ↓
> Action required?
>   ├─ No → Save as Knowledge / Log / Reference
>   └─ Yes
>       ↓
>    [ Action ]
>       ↓
>    [ Steps ]
>       ↓
>    [ Slot in Time ]
>       ↓
>    [ Work / Waiting / Done ]
>       ↓
>    [ Resolution ]
>       ↓
>    [ Reflection ]
>       ↓
>    [ Retrieval via Timeline / Search / AI ]
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### B. Screen-to-screen user flow
> 
> ```text
> Capture
>   ↓
> Inbox / New QiBit
>   ↓
> QiBit Review
>   ↓
> Bucket + Thread + Related People
>   ↓
> ┌─────────────────────┬──────────────────────┐
> │ Needs action        │ No action needed     │
> │ → Create Action     │ → Save as reference  │
> │ → Add steps         │ → Add to knowledge   │
> │ → Slot in time      │ → Keep on timeline   │
> └─────────────────────┴──────────────────────┘
>   ↓
> Today / Timeline / Thread View
>   ↓
> Context Dock + AI
>   ↓
> Resolve / Reflect / Retrieve
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3) Main Mental Model
> 
> ### QiLife is a private single-agent helpdesk for life
> 
> ```text
> QiLife
> ├── QiBits          = tickets / captured life items
> ├── Buckets         = queues / departments
> ├── Threads         = cases / storylines / projects
> ├── Actions         = work to be done
> ├── Steps           = subtasks
> ├── Timeline        = chronological spine
> ├── Context Dock    = side knowledge panel
> ├── Knowledge       = what matters / what is known
> ├── Money           = transactions + obligations
> ├── People          = involved humans/entities
> └── AI              = triage, context, retrieval, summaries
> ```
> 
> ---

> ### Key question answered

> ├── Done

> └── By Context
> ```
> 
> ### Key question answered

> # 7) QiBit Flow — Visual Lifecycle
> 
> ```text
> QiBit
> ├── What?      = Capture
> ├── Where?     = Bucket
> ├── Why?       = Interpret
> ├── Who?       = Relate
> ├── When?      = Slot
> ├── How?       = Breakdown
> ├── Because?   = Enrich
> ├── Then?      = Action
> ├── Done?      = Resolution
> ├── So what?   = Reflection
> └── Find later = Retrieval
> ```
> 
> That’s the heartbeat of the whole app.

> # 9) Dev Blueprint — Build Spine
> 
> ## Phase 1 — Core Spine
> 
> ### Goal
> Get the core nervous system working.
> 
> ### Build
> ```text
> Phase 1
> ├── App shell
> ├── Left nav
> ├── Center workspace
> ├── Context Dock
> ├── QiBit model
> ├── Buckets
> ├── Threads
> ├── Actions
> ├── Timeline
> ├── Inbox
> └── Ask QiLife placeholder
> ```
> 
> ### Deliverable
> You can capture, triage, route, link, act, and retrieve.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phase 2 — Command Layer
> 
> ### Goal
> Make it useful daily.
> 
> ### Build
> ```text
> Phase 2
> ├── Today dashboard
> ├── Calendar / week planning
> ├── Action views
> ├── Waiting / scheduled / done
> ├── Reflection prompts
> └── AI focus summary
> ```
> 
> ### Deliverable
> You can actually run your day from it.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phase 3 — Context Layer
> 
> ### Goal
> Bring in the side-by-side knowledge model.
> 
> ### Build
> ```text
> Phase 3
> ├── Knowledge items
> ├── Linked notes
> ├── Documents metadata
> ├── Person pages
> ├── Thread summaries
> └── Context Dock enrichment
> ```
> 
> ### Deliverable
> You can work and think in the same app.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phase 4 — Money Layer
> 
> ### Goal
> Add life logistics.
> 
> ### Build
> ```text
> Phase 4
> ├── Transactions
> ├── Obligations
> ├── Budget buckets
> ├── Recurring expenses
> ├── Related money on threads
> └── Money side panel context
> ```
> 
> ### Deliverable
> You can track movement, obligations, and reality.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phase 5 — AI Layer
> 
> ### Goal
> Make it smart, not just structured.
> 
> ### Build
> ```text
> Phase 5
> ├── AI triage
> ├── AI summarize
> ├── AI action suggestion
> ├── AI related-entity extraction
> ├── AI retrieval answers
> ├── AI daily brief
> └── AI reflection helper
> ```
> 
> ### Deliverable
> QiLife becomes your working sidekick.
>

> 
> ## App repo tree
> 
> ```text
> qilife/
> ├── README.md
> ├── docs/
> │   ├── 00_overview/
> │   ├── 10_product/
> │   ├── 20_architecture/
> │   ├── 30_data_model/
> │   ├── 40_ui_flows/
> │   ├── 50_ai_layer/
> │   ├── 60_deployment/
> │   └── 90_decisions/
> │
> ├── frontend/
> │   ├── src/
> │   │   ├── app/
> │   │   ├── pages/
> │   │   │   ├── today/
> │   │   │   ├── timeline/
> │   │   │   ├── inbox/
> │   │   │   ├── threads/
> │   │   │   ├── actions/
> │   │   │   ├── calendar/
> │   │   │   ├── people/
> │   │   │   ├── money/
> │   │   │   ├── knowledge/
> │   │   │   ├── documents/
> │   │   │   └── ask_qilife/
> │   │   ├── components/
> │   │   │   ├── shell/
> │   │   │   ├── qibits/
> │   │   │   ├── threads/
> │   │   │   ├── actions/
> │   │   │   ├── context_dock/
> │   │   │   ├── calendar/
> │   │   │   ├── money/
> │   │   │   └── knowledge/
> │   │   ├── features/
> │   │   ├── hooks/
> │   │   ├── services/
> │   │   ├── store/

> │   │   └── utils/

> ├── backend/

> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 11) Data / Domain Tree Blueprint
> 
> ## Core data structure
> 
> ```text
> QiLife Data
> ├── QiBits
> ├── Buckets
> ├── Threads
> ├── Actions
> ├── Action Steps
> ├── People
> ├── Transactions
> ├── Obligations
> ├── Knowledge Items
> ├── Notes
> ├── Documents
> ├── Events
> ├── Reflections
> ├── Links
> └── AI Outputs
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 12) Page Relationship Tree
> 
> ```text
> Today
> ├── pulls from QiBits
> ├── pulls from Actions
> ├── pulls from Calendar
> ├── pulls from Money
> ├── pulls from Threads
> └── shows AI brief
> 
> Timeline
> ├── shows all QiBits
> ├── links to Threads
> ├── links to People
> ├── links to Actions
> └── links to Documents
> 
> Thread Detail
> ├── related QiBits
> ├── related Actions
> ├── related People
> ├── related Money
> ├── related Documents
> └── Context Dock
> 
> Action Detail
> ├── source QiBit
> ├── steps
> ├── schedule
> ├── status
> └── Context Dock
> 
> Person Detail
> ├── QiBits
> ├── Threads
> ├── Actions
> ├── Money
> └── Documents
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 13) UX Rules
> 
> ## Non-negotiables
> 
> ```text
> UX Rules
> ├── Quick capture always visible
> ├── Timeline is the spine
> ├── Knowledge is side-by-side, not separate
> ├── Everything important links back to a QiBit
> ├── Buckets match real hierarchy
> ├── AI assists, does not obscure truth
> ├── Today view stays lean
> ├── Context Dock is collapsible
> └── One-click path from chaos → action
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 14) Build Order — Practical
> 
> ## Immediate sequence
> 
> ```text
> 1. App shell
> 2. Navigation
> 3. QiBit model
> 4. Inbox / Capture
> 5. Timeline view
> 6. Thread model + page
> 7. Action model + page
> 8. Today dashboard
> 9. Context Dock
> 10. Knowledge items
> 11. People
> 12. Money
> 13. Calendar
> 14. AI layer
> ```
> 
> That’s the order I’d use. Clean and sane.
> 
> ---

### User
> umm, i think first you use canvas to write the documents for us to review, another question too, since we want docs next to their module should all modules have docs folders or how do we assosciate articles to entities with tags or something like how it works on a helpdesk while still maintaingin a navigable central kb source like helpdesk does.

### Assistant
> Yes — **first we create review documents**, not code.
> 
> That keeps Codex from wandering off into goblin architecture. We need a **QiLife Product Bible / Dev Blueprint** first.
> 
> And your question about docs is exactly right:
> 
> > Do modules each get docs folders, or do we use tags/relationships like helpdesk knowledge articles?
> 
> Answer: **both — but with one source of truth.**
> 
> # The right model
> 
> QiLife should have a **central Knowledge Base**, but knowledge articles can be **attached to modules, entities, threads, buckets, people, actions, and QiBits**.
> 
> Think helpdesk:
> 
> A helpdesk has a central KB, but articles can also be suggested on a ticket, linked to a customer, tied to a product, or attached to a category.
> 
> QiLife should work the same way.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Knowledge Architecture
> 
> ## 1. Central KB
> 
> This is the navigable library.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> Knowledge
> ├── 00_inbox
> ├── 10_workbench
> ├── 20_timeline
> ├── 30_life
> ├── 40_people
> ├── 50_business
> ├── 60_finance
> ├── 70_legal
> ├── 80_tech
> ├── 90_assets
> ├── 100_data
> ├── 110_reference
> ├── 900_archive
> └── 990_system
> ```
> 
> This matches your real bucket hierarchy.
> 
> ## 2. Module Docs
> 
> Each module should have its own docs folder **inside the repo** for developer/product docs.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> qilife/
> ├── docs/
> │   ├── 00_overview/
> │   ├── 10_product/
> │   ├── 20_architecture/
> │   ├── 30_data_model/
> │   ├── 40_ui_flows/
> │   ├── 50_modules/
> │   │   ├── qibits/
> │   │   ├── timeline/
> │   │   ├── inbox/
> │   │   ├── threads/
> │   │   ├── actions/
> │   │   ├── calendar/
> │   │   ├── people/
> │   │   ├── money/
> │   │   ├── knowledge/
> │   │   ├── documents/
> │   │   └── ask_qilife/
> │   ├── 60_ai_layer/
> │   ├── 70_deployment/
> │   └── 90_decisions/
> ```
> 
> These are **build docs**, not necessarily user-facing knowledge articles.
> 
> ## 3. Entity-Attached Knowledge
> 
> Inside the app, knowledge should be stored as records and linked to entities.
> 
> A knowledge article can attach to:
> 
> - bucket
> - module
> - QiBit
> - thread
> - action
> - person
> - transaction
> - obligation
> - document
> - calendar event
> - system rule
> 
> So the same article can appear in:
> 
> - central KB
> - Context Dock
> - thread detail
> - action detail
> - person page
> - bucket page
> 
> No duplicate copies. Just linked views.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The key distinction
> 
> ## Repo Docs
> 
> For building QiLife.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - How the QiBit lifecycle works
> - Database schema
> - API routes
> - UI flows
> - deployment notes
> - AI service architecture
> 
> ## In-App Knowledge
> 
> For using your life/system.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - “How I categorize Lyft gas”
> - “Marion County Clerk surplus check process”
> - “Family Operating System one-source rule”
> - “QiServer deployment steps”
> - “Zai lease context”
> - “Phone replacement plan”
> - “Monthly budget rules”
> 
> Both can be Markdown, but they serve different jobs.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Best structure
> 
> ## Repo side
> 
> ```text
> qilife/docs/50_modules/money/
> ├── overview.md
> ├── data_model.md
> ├── ui_flow.md
> ├── context_dock.md
> └── ai_behaviors.md
> ```
> 
> ## App side
> 
> ```text
> Knowledge Article
> ├── title: Gas Categorization Rule
> ├── body: ...
> ├── bucket: 60_finance
> ├── module: money
> ├── linked_entities:
> │   ├── thread: Lyft Income Sprint
> │   ├── person: Cody
> │   └── category: fuel
> ├── tags:
> │   ├── gas
> │   ├── lyft
> │   ├── reimbursement
> │   └── tax
> └── visibility: private
> ```
> 
> That gives you both:
> 
> - navigable KB
> - contextual side-panel knowledge
> 
> ---
> 
> # Data model for Knowledge
> 
> Use `knowledge_items` plus `links`.
> 
> ## `knowledge_items`
> 
> ```text
> knowledge_items
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── body_markdown
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── module_key
> ├── knowledge_type
> ├── source
> ├── confidence
> ├── visibility
> ├── tags
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ## `links`
> 
> ```text
> links
> ├── id
> ├── source_type
> ├── source_id
> ├── target_type
> ├── target_id
> ├── relationship
> └── created_at
> ```
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> Knowledge Item: “Surplus Check Follow-Up Rule”
> linked to:
> ├── bucket: 70_legal
> ├── thread: Surplus Check Recovery
> ├── person/entity: Marion County Clerk
> ├── document: Order Granting Release
> └── action: Call clerk if check not received
> ```
> 
> Now it appears everywhere it matters.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Tags vs links
> 
> Use both, but don’t confuse them.
> 
> ## Links are for known relationships
> 
> Use links when the system knows the exact thing.
> 
> Example:
> 
> - this article is linked to Zai
> - this task came from this QiBit
> - this note belongs to this thread
> - this document supports this legal item
> 
> ## Tags are for loose retrieval
> 
> Use tags for flexible search.
> 
> Example:
> 
> - `gas`
> - `lyft`
> - `surplus-check`
> - `court`
> - `family-ops`
> - `qiserver`
> - `receipt`
> - `waiting-on`
> 
> Blunt truth: **tags alone are too weak**. They become a junk drawer. Links give structure. Tags help retrieval.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Context Dock behavior
> 
> Every major page should ask:
> 
> > “What knowledge is relevant to this thing?”
> 
> It pulls knowledge by:
> 
> 1. Direct links  
> 2. Same thread  
> 3. Same bucket  
> 4. Same person/entity  
> 5. Shared tags  
> 6. AI semantic similarity later  
> 
> So if you open:
> 
> ## Thread: Surplus Check Recovery
> 
> Context Dock shows:
> 
> ```text
> Relevant Knowledge
> ├── Surplus Check Follow-Up Rule
> ├── Marion County Clerk Contact Notes
> ├── Mailing Timeline Notes
> ├── Court Order Summary
> └── Prior Call Script
> ```
> 
> If you open:
> 
> ## Person/Entity: Zai
> 
> Context Dock shows:
> 
> ```text
> Relevant Knowledge
> ├── Zai Lease Terms
> ├── Rent Payment History Notes
> ├── Shared Gas Reimbursement Rule
> └── Contact Preferences
> ```
> 
> That is exactly how helpdesk software works.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Should every module have a docs folder?
> 
> ## For dev docs: yes.
> 
> Each module gets docs.
> 
> ## For app knowledge: no, not as physical folders first.
> 
> Inside the app, knowledge should be records with bucket/module/entity links.
> 
> Later you can export them to folders.
> 
> This avoids duplicate articles like:
> 
> ```text
> finance/gas_rule.md
> lyft/gas_rule.md
> tax/gas_rule.md
> zai/gas_rule.md
> ```
> 
> Nope. One article. Many links.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Export logic later
> 
> When exporting to Markdown/QiNexus, use primary bucket path:
> 
> ```text
> /60_finance/knowledge/gas_categorization_rule.md
> ```
> 
> Inside the markdown frontmatter:
> 
> ```yaml
> bucket: 60_finance
> module: money
> tags:
>   - gas
>   - lyft
>   - reimbursement
> linked_threads:
>   - Lyft Income Sprint
> linked_people:
>   - Cody
> linked_entities: []
> ```
> 
> So the file has one home but many relationships.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Review docs we should create first
> 
> Yes, I’d create a document set like this:
> 
> ```text
> qilife_review_docs/
> ├── 00_qilife_canvas.md
> ├── 01_product_doctrine.md
> ├── 02_qibit_lifecycle.md
> ├── 03_information_architecture.md
> ├── 04_app_flow_and_screens.md
> ├── 05_context_dock_and_knowledge_model.md
> ├── 06_data_model_spine.md
> ├── 07_ai_layer_blueprint.md
> ├── 08_module_map.md
> ├── 09_build_phases.md
> └── 10_codex_build_prompt.md
> ```
> 
> These are review docs, not final code docs yet.
> 
> ---
> 
> # My recommendation
> 
> For QiLife:
> 
> ## Use this doctrine
> 
> **Docs live beside modules in the repo. Knowledge lives centrally in the app and appears beside whatever it is linked to.**
> 
> Clean version:
> 
> ```text
> Build docs = module folders
> Life knowledge = central KB + links + tags + Context Dock
> Exports = bucket-aligned Markdown
> ```
> 
> That gives you:
> 
> - developer clarity
> - navigable KB
> - contextual helpdesk-style knowledge
> - no duplicate articles
> - AI-ready retrieval
> - future Markdown portability
> 
> That’s the right architecture.

### User
> the repo docs should also live in the inapp knowledge for reference do we have to have tehm sepearte or best for the build.

### Assistant
> No, they do **not** have to stay separate forever.
> 
> Best build pattern:
> 
> # Repo docs are the source. In-app knowledge mirrors/indexes them.
> 
> That gives you both:
> 
> 1. **Clean developer docs in the repo**
> 2. **Searchable/contextual knowledge inside QiLife**
> 3. **No duplicate-maintenance nightmare**
> 
> Because if we manually write the same thing in two places, future Cody will want to fight present Cody in the parking lot.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Best architecture
> 
> ## Source of truth
> 
> Repo Markdown files:
> 
> ```text
> qilife/docs/
> ├── 00_overview/
> ├── 10_product/
> ├── 20_architecture/
> ├── 30_data_model/
> ├── 40_ui_flows/
> ├── 50_modules/
> ├── 60_ai_layer/
> ├── 70_deployment/
> └── 90_decisions/
> ```
> 
> These are the canonical dev/build docs.
> 
> ## In-app knowledge
> 
> QiLife imports or indexes those docs as `knowledge_items`.
> 
> So inside the app, you can search and view:
> 
> - QiBit doctrine
> - data model
> - module docs
> - Context Dock design
> - AI behavior notes
> - deployment notes
> - ADRs
> - build rules
> 
> But the app record points back to the source file.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The clean model
> 
> Each in-app knowledge item can have:
> 
> ```text
> title
> body_markdown
> source_type: repo_doc
> source_path: docs/50_modules/qibits/overview.md
> bucket_code: 990_system or 80_tech
> module_key: qibits
> knowledge_type: architecture / procedure / decision / reference
> tags
> last_synced_at
> sync_hash
> ```
> 
> That way QiLife can display it, link it, search it, and show it in the Context Dock.
> 
> But the canonical editable file still lives in Git.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Why repo docs should stay canonical during build
> 
> Because Codex/IDE/tools need file-based docs.
> 
> They can read:
> 
> ```text
> docs/20_architecture/app_shell.md
> docs/30_data_model/qibits.md
> docs/50_modules/money/overview.md
> ```
> 
> That is easier than making Codex query an app database that may not even be built yet.
> 
> So for the build phase:
> 
> **Markdown in repo first. App imports them later.**
> 
> ---
> 
> # How to classify repo docs inside QiLife
> 
> Repo docs should go under:
> 
> ## Bucket
> 
> `990 System`
> 
> or sometimes:
> 
> - `80 Tech` for implementation/deployment
> - `100 Data` for schemas/data model
> - `110 Reference` for durable doctrine
> - `990 System` for app internals
> 
> I’d use this mapping:
> 
> | Repo Doc Type | QiLife Bucket |
> |---|---|
> | Product doctrine | `110 Reference` |
> | App architecture | `990 System` |
> | Module build docs | `990 System` |
> | Data model/schema | `100 Data` |
> | Deployment/server docs | `80 Tech` |
> | ADRs/decisions | `990 System` |
> | User workflows | `110 Reference` |
> 
> ---
> 
> # The practical rule
> 
> ## Dev docs
> 
> Live in:
> 
> ```text
> /qilife/docs/
> ```
> 
> ## App knowledge
> 
> Stores an indexed copy/reference.
> 
> ## QiNexus export
> 
> Later can mirror to:
> 
> ```text
> /990_system/qilife/docs/
> /110_reference/qilife/doctrine/
> /100_data/qilife/schema/
> ```
> 
> But do not start by syncing three places. That’s how we summon the Duplicate Goblin.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The better phrase
> 
> Use this doctrine:
> 
> **Write once in Markdown, index everywhere.**
> 
> That’s the whole thing.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final answer
> 
> For the build, keep docs as repo Markdown.
> 
> Then QiLife gets a **Knowledge Importer** that turns repo docs into in-app knowledge items with source paths.
> 
> So the system becomes:
> 
> ```text
> Repo Markdown Docs
>         ↓
> Knowledge Importer / Indexer
>         ↓
> In-App Knowledge Items
>         ↓
> Context Dock / Search / Ask QiLife
> ```
> 
> That gives us clean build docs **and** the side-by-side in-app knowledge experience without creating duplicate content chaos.

### Assistant
> Yes. That’s the right workflow.
> 
> Use the IDE as the **grunt architect/builder**, then Codex as the **reviewer/validator/fixer**, not the first one holding the steering wheel. Codex is powerful, but if you let it freestyle too early it may “helpfully” rebuild the universe and forget the point.
> 
> # Workflow
> 
> ## Stage 1 — IDE does the grunt work
> 
> Goal: turn the review packet into a proper repo structure and implementation plan.
> 
> The IDE should:
> 
> 1. Read the review docs.
> 2. Create the final `/docs` structure.
> 3. Move the review packet into proper doc folders.
> 4. Create missing module docs.
> 5. Create architecture docs.
> 6. Create data model docs.
> 7. Create a clear build checklist.
> 8. Create a dev prompt handoff for Codex.
> 9. Do **not** start coding the app yet.
> 
> This keeps the project sane.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended repo structure now
> 
> Your current:
> 
> ```text
> _qilife/
> ├── qilife_build_specs_review/
> ├── .gitignore
> └── README.md
> ```
> 
> Should become:
> 
> ```text
> _qilife/
> ├── README.md
> ├── .gitignore
> ├── docs/
> │   ├── 00_overview/
> │   │   ├── 00_qilife_canvas.md
> │   │   ├── 01_product_doctrine.md
> │   │   └── 02_glossary.md
> │   │

> │   │   ├── 01_qibit_lifecycle.md

### User
> start thinking schema and how is the database going to work, what type etc, how do we make it less volitale etc.

### Assistant
> Yes — this is the next serious design layer. I’m going to frame the database as the “life ledger,” not just storage, because volatility comes from weak relationships, sloppy IDs, and unclear source-of-truth rules.

### Assistant
> Yes. Now we need to think like accountants + helpdesk architects + archivists.
> 
> The database cannot be “a bunch of app tables.” It needs to be a **stable life ledger**.
> 
> # Core database decision
> 
> For v1:
> 
> ## Use SQLite first.
> 
> Not because it is tiny. Because it is:
> 
> - local-first
> - easy to back up
> - one file
> - portable
> - fast enough
> - simple to inspect
> - easy to migrate later
> - low maintenance
> - works beautifully for single-user apps
> 
> Then later:
> 
> ## Move to Postgres on QiServer.
> 
> Only after the model proves itself.
> 
> So the path is:
> 
> ```text
> SQLite local dev
> ↓
> SQLite personal production / private server
> ↓
> Postgres when stable or multi-device/server needs increase
> ```
> 
> Do **not** start with a complex distributed sync database. That is where dreams go to get mugged.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Database doctrine
> 
> ## 1. QiBit is the source event
> 
> Everything important either starts as a QiBit or links back to one.
> 
> This prevents orphaned tasks, mystery obligations, random notes, and “why is this here?” syndrome.
> 
> ## 2. Timeline is append-friendly
> 
> The database should preserve history. Do not constantly overwrite reality.
> 
> Prefer:
> 
> ```text
> created
> updated
> resolved
> linked
> logged
> ```
> 
> over silently mutating old meaning.
> 
> ## 3. Use stable IDs
> 
> Every record gets:
> 
> ```text
> id: UUID/ULID
> created_at
> updated_at
> ```
> 
> I’d use **ULIDs** if possible because they sort by time and are cleaner for timeline systems.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> 01JYQ8Z7W4V6K2...
> ```
> 
> Better than random UUID chaos.
> 
> ## 4. Separate facts from interpretation
> 
> This is critical.
> 
> A QiBit should have:
> 
> ```text
> raw_capture = what Cody actually entered
> summary = cleaned version
> meaning = interpretation
> ai_outputs = separate records
> ```
> 
> Do not let AI overwrite the original capture. Ever.
> 
> Original input is evidence. AI is commentary.
> 
> ## 5. Links beat duplicated columns
> 
> Instead of adding `person_id`, `document_id`, `transaction_id`, `note_id`, etc. to every table forever, use a generic `links` table.
> 
> That gives flexibility without schema explosion.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended database type
> 
> ## V1 database
> 
> ```text
> SQLite
> ```
> 
> Use:
> 
> - SQLAlchemy or SQLModel
> - Alembic migrations
> - WAL mode enabled
> - daily backup/export script
> - JSON fields only where appropriate
> - Markdown stored as text
> - files stored on disk, metadata in DB
> 
> ## Later database
> 
> ```text
> Postgres
> ```
> 
> When:
> 
> - QiServer deployment is stable
> - multiple devices matter
> - app grows beyond local desktop use
> - stronger search/indexing needed
> - background jobs/AI indexing become serious
> 
> ---
> 
> # Make it less volatile
> 
> Volatility means:
> 
> - schema changes break everything
> - AI corrupts records
> - tags become junk
> - tasks lose context
> - data cannot export
> - files and DB drift apart
> - app logic becomes spaghetti
> 
> So we protect it with these rules.
> 
> ## Rule 1: Use a small stable core
> 
> Core tables should not change constantly:
> 
> ```text
> qibits
> buckets
> threads
> actions
> action_steps
> people
> transactions
> obligations
> knowledge_items
> documents
> events
> links
> activity_log
> ai_outputs
> ```
> 
> Do not make 80 tables in v1.
> 
> ## Rule 2: Add metadata through extensions, not schema panic
> 
> Use a controlled `metadata_json` field on some records for future extras.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> qibits.metadata_json
> actions.metadata_json
> people.metadata_json
> documents.metadata_json
> ```
> 
> But don’t abuse it. It is a flex pocket, not a junk drawer.
> 
> ## Rule 3: Keep files outside the DB
> 
> Database stores metadata.
> 
> Files live in controlled storage paths.
> 
> ```text
> DB:
> document title, file path, type, hash, linked QiBit
> 
> Disk:
> actual PDF/image/audio/etc.
> ```
> 
> This keeps the DB portable and fast.
> 
> ## Rule 4: Use migrations from day one
> 
> Even with SQLite, use Alembic.
> 
> Do not manually mutate tables like a goblin with a screwdriver.
> 
> Every schema change gets a migration.
> 
> ## Rule 5: Keep append-only logs
> 
> Add:
> 
> ```text
> activity_log
> ```
> 
> Every major change gets logged:
> 
> - created QiBit
> - interpreted QiBit
> - created action
> - linked document
> - resolved obligation
> - completed action
> - added reflection
> - AI suggestion accepted
> 
> This lets you reconstruct “what happened.”
> 
> ## Rule 6: Soft delete, don’t hard delete
> 
> Most records should have:
> 
> ```text
> archived_at
> deleted_at
> ```
> 
> Instead of immediate deletion.
> 
> Because future you will ask:
> 
> > “Where did that thing go?”
> 
> And we do not want the answer to be “the void, babe.”
> 
> ---
> 
> # Schema shape
> 
> ## 1. `qibits`
> 
> The atomic life item.
> 
> ```text
> qibits
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── raw_capture
> ├── summary
> ├── meaning
> ├── qibit_type
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── status
> ├── priority
> ├── importance
> ├── emotional_load
> ├── action_required
> ├── suggested_action
> ├── future_slot
> ├── happened_at
> ├── captured_at
> ├── resolved_at
> ├── retrieval_summary
> ├── reflection
> ├── tags_json
> ├── metadata_json
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> Important:
> 
> `raw_capture` must be sacred. AI does not overwrite it.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. `buckets`
> 
> Your real hierarchy.
> 
> ```text
> buckets
> ├── code
> ├── name
> ├── slug
> ├── folder_path
> ├── sort_order
> ├── description
> ├── is_system
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Seeded:
> 
> ```text
> 00 Inbox
> 10 Workbench
> 20 Timeline
> 30 Life
> 40 People
> 50 Business
> 60 Finance
> 70 Legal
> 80 Tech
> 90 Assets
> 100 Data
> 110 Reference
> 900 Archive
> 990 System
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. `threads`
> 
> Cases/projects/storylines.
> 
> ```text
> threads
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── description
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── status
> ├── priority
> ├── next_action
> ├── due_date
> ├── started_at
> ├── closed_at
> ├── tags_json
> ├── metadata_json
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. `actions`
> 
> Task/work order table.
> 
> ```text
> actions
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── description
> ├── source_qibit_id
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── status
> ├── priority
> ├── energy
> ├── context
> ├── due_date
> ├── scheduled_for
> ├── completed_at
> ├── resolution_note
> ├── tags_json
> ├── metadata_json
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. `action_steps`
> 
> Subtasks/checklist.
> 
> ```text
> action_steps
> ├── id
> ├── action_id
> ├── title
> ├── description
> ├── status
> ├── sort_order
> ├── completed_at
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. `people`
> 
> Lightweight people/entities. Not CRM.
> 
> ```text
> people
> ├── id
> ├── display_name
> ├── legal_name
> ├── type
> ├── relationship
> ├── email
> ├── phone
> ├── address
> ├── notes
> ├── tags_json
> ├── metadata_json
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> Types:
> 
> ```text
> person
> company
> agency
> vendor
> court
> client
> household
> platform
> app_service
> other
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 7. `transactions`
> 
> Money movement.
> 
> ```text
> transactions
> ├── id
> ├── date
> ├── amount_cents
> ├── currency
> ├── direction
> ├── from_label
> ├── to_label
> ├── category
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── status
> ├── notes
> ├── evidence_document_id
> ├── source_qibit_id
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> Use `amount_cents`, not floating decimals. Money stored as floats is how demons get admin access.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 8. `obligations`
> 
> Who owes what.
> 
> ```text
> obligations
> ├── id
> ├── owed_by_label
> ├── owed_to_label
> ├── obligation_type
> ├── amount_cents
> ├── currency
> ├── reason
> ├── status
> ├── due_date
> ├── related_transaction_id
> ├── source_qibit_id
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── resolved_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 9. `knowledge_items`
> 
> Embedded KB articles.
> 
> ```text
> knowledge_items
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── body_markdown
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── module_key
> ├── knowledge_type
> ├── source_type
> ├── source_path
> ├── confidence
> ├── visibility
> ├── tags_json
> ├── metadata_json
> ├── last_synced_at
> ├── sync_hash
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> Repo docs can be imported/indexed here.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 10. `documents`
> 
> File metadata.
> 
> ```text
> documents
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── file_path
> ├── source
> ├── document_type
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── file_hash
> ├── mime_type
> ├── size_bytes
> ├── notes
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> File hash matters for dedupe.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 11. `events`
> 
> Calendar/schedule items.
> 
> ```text
> events
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── description
> ├── start_time
> ├── end_time
> ├── location
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── status
> ├── source_qibit_id
> ├── created_at
> ├── updated_at
> ├── archived_at
> └── deleted_at
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 12. `links`
> 
> The glue.
> 
> ```text
> links
> ├── id
> ├── source_type
> ├── source_id
> ├── target_type
> ├── target_id
> ├── relationship
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Relationships:
> 
> ```text
> created_from
> relates_to
> explains
> supports
> blocks
> resolves
> mentions
> belongs_to
> waiting_on
> caused_by
> evidence_for
> summarizes
> references
> ```
> 
> This is how one QiBit can connect to five things without schema surgery.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 13. `activity_log`
> 
> Append-only history.
> 
> ```text
> activity_log
> ├── id
> ├── occurred_at
> ├── actor
> ├── action
> ├── entity_type
> ├── entity_id
> ├── summary
> ├── before_json
> ├── after_json
> ├── source
> └── created_at
> ```
> 
> This powers:
> 
> > What happened today?
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 14. `ai_outputs`
> 
> AI suggestions/history.
> 
> ```text
> ai_outputs
> ├── id
> ├── source_type
> ├── source_id
> ├── ai_task
> ├── prompt_snapshot
> ├── output_json
> ├── confidence
> ├── accepted
> ├── created_records_json
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> AI output is stored separately so you can accept/reject/compare.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Critical design choice: daily log
> 
> You have two options.
> 
> ## Option A: separate `daily_log`
> 
> Pros:
> 
> - easy daily view
> - clean “what happened today”
> - quick summaries
> 
> Cons:
> 
> - duplicates activity log if done badly
> 
> ## Option B: generate daily log from `activity_log` + timeline QiBits
> 
> Pros:
> 
> - less duplication
> - truer source of record
> 
> Cons:
> 
> - harder to tune daily summaries
> 
> My recommendation:
> 
> ## Use both, but with different jobs.
> 
> ```text
> activity_log = factual audit trail
> daily_summaries = generated/reflected summary
> ```
> 
> So add:
> 
> ```text
> daily_summaries
> ├── id
> ├── date
> ├── summary_markdown
> ├── ai_summary_json
> ├── reviewed
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Do **not** create a massive daily_log table that duplicates everything.
> 
> The “what happened today” page should pull from:
> 
> - QiBits captured today
> - actions completed today
> - transactions today
> - obligations opened/resolved today
> - events today
> - activity_log
> - daily_summaries
> 
> That’s stable.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Less volatile architecture
> 
> ## Use three layers
> 
> ```text
> Raw Layer
> ├── qibits.raw_capture
> ├── documents
> ├── imported repo docs
> └── activity_log
> 
> Structured Layer
> ├── actions
> ├── threads
> ├── people
> ├── transactions
> ├── obligations
> ├── events
> └── links
> 
> Interpretation Layer
> ├── qibits.summary
> ├── qibits.meaning
> ├── knowledge_items
> ├── ai_outputs
> ├── reflections
> └── daily_summaries
> ```
> 
> This prevents AI or later interpretation from corrupting the raw record.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended database engine setup
> 
> ## SQLite settings
> 
> Use:
> 
> ```text
> PRAGMA journal_mode=WAL;
> PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON;
> PRAGMA synchronous=NORMAL;
> ```
> 
> Why:
> 
> - WAL makes it safer and better for concurrent reads/writes.
> - foreign keys prevent broken relationships.
> - synchronous normal is a reasonable durability/performance balance.
> 
> ## Backups
> 
> Have scripts:
> 
> ```text
> scripts/db/backup_db.py
> scripts/db/export_markdown.py
> scripts/db/check_integrity.py
> scripts/db/seed_dev.py
> ```
> 
> Backups should create:
> 
> ```text
> data/backups/qilife_YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM.sqlite
> ```
> 
> Also export human-readable Markdown periodically.
> 
> ---
> 
> # File storage
> 
> Use a predictable storage root:
> 
> ```text
> data/
> ├── db/
> │   └── qilife.sqlite
> ├── files/
> │   ├── documents/
> │   ├── images/
> │   ├── audio/
> │   └── imports/
> ├── exports/
> │   ├── markdown/
> │   └── json/
> └── backups/
> ```
> 
> Later, exports can map to QiNexus buckets.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What I’d add to the docs now
> 
> Create a new doc:
> 
> ```text
> docs/30_data_model/06_database_stability_strategy.md
> ```
> 
> It should define:
> 
> - SQLite first, Postgres later
> - ULIDs
> - raw vs interpreted data
> - links table
> - activity log
> - soft deletes
> - migrations
> - file metadata vs file storage
> - backup/export strategy
> - AI outputs stored separately
> - amount_cents for money
> - daily summaries generated from events/activity
> 
> ---
> 
> # Codex/IDE prompt to add this doc
> 
> ```text
> Create a new QiLife database stability strategy document:
> 
> docs/30_data_model/06_database_stability_strategy.md
> 
> Purpose:
> Explain how the QiLife database should be designed to reduce volatility, protect source data, preserve history, and remain portable.
> 
> Include these decisions:
> 
> 1. Use SQLite for v1 because QiLife is single-user, local-first, portable, and easier to back up.
> 2. Prepare for future Postgres migration on QiServer.
> 3. Use ULID or UUID primary keys, preferably ULID for timeline-friendly sorting.
> 4. Preserve raw captures separately from summaries and AI interpretations.
> 5. Store AI outputs in ai_outputs and require user acceptance before important records are created/updated.
> 6. Use a generic links table for relationships between records.
> 7. Use activity_log as append-only audit history.
> 8. Use daily_summaries for generated/reflected daily summaries instead of duplicating all records into a daily log table.
> 9. Store files on disk and file metadata in documents.
> 10. Store money as amount_cents, not floating decimals.
> 11. Enable SQLite WAL mode and foreign keys.
> 12. Use Alembic migrations from day one.
> 13. Use soft delete fields archived_at and deleted_at for major records.
> 14. Add backup/export scripts.
> 15. Separate data into Raw Layer, Structured Layer, and Interpretation Layer.
> 
> Also add a concise recommended data folder layout:
> 
> data/
>   db/
>   files/
>   exports/
>   backups/
> 
> Do not start coding the app.
> Update docs/30_data_model/00_data_model_spine.md if needed to mention daily_summaries and the database stability document.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # My blunt recommendation
> 
> Do **SQLite + SQLAlchemy + Alembic** first.
> 
> Do not get clever.
> 
> The schema should be stable because:
> 
> - QiBit is the root event
> - links connect everything
> - activity_log preserves history
> - AI suggestions are separate
> - raw capture is preserved
> - files are not trapped in DB
> - exports keep it portable
> - migration history keeps changes sane
> 
> That is the non-chaotic path.

> - Action: Finish 11 Lyft rides
> - Action: Check mail for surplus check
> - QiBit: QiLife needs one central place for tasks, daily log, knowledge, notes, and AI.
> - Knowledge item: QiBit lifecycle doctrine
> 
> Frontend requirements:
> - Dark mode first.
> - Agent-console feel.
> - Left nav.
> - Center workspace.
> - Right Context Dock.
> - Persistent quick capture input labeled "What happened?"
> - Basic cards with readable spacing and subtle depth.
> - Mobile usable enough for testing.
> - Avoid plain ugly white card UI.
> 
> Pages to implement:
> 1. Today
>    - quick capture
>    - today’s QiBits
>    - open actions
>    - waiting items placeholder
>    - AI focus summary placeholder
> 
> 2. Timeline
>    - chronological list of QiBits
>    - filters placeholder
> 
> 3. Inbox
>    - unprocessed/new QiBits
>    - process with AI placeholder button
> 
> 4. Threads
>    - thread list
>    - thread detail basic view
>    - related QiBits/actions placeholder if not fully wired
> 
> 5. Actions
>    - action list grouped by status
>    - action detail
>    - steps checklist
> 
> 6. Ask QiLife
>    - prompt box
>    - mock answer
>    - supporting records placeholder
> 
> 7. Settings/About
>    - explain QiLife purpose
>    - mention Will Be Done as visual planning inspiration
>    - include link: https://github.com/will-be-done/will-be-done
> 
> Backend API endpoints:
> - GET /health
> - GET /api/buckets
> - CRUD /api/qibits
> - CRUD /api/threads
> - CRUD /api/actions
> - CRUD /api/actions/{id}/steps
> - GET /api/timeline
> - GET /api/today
> - POST /api/ai/mock/interpret-qibit
> - POST /api/ai/mock/ask
> 
> Activity logging:
> When a QiBit, Thread, Action, or Step is created/updated/completed, write a simple activity_log row.
> 
> README update:
> Add:
> - setup instructions
> - backend run command
> - frontend run command
> - seed command
> - data/db location
> - current Phase 1 scope
> - not-yet-built list
> 
> Testing:
> Add minimal backend smoke tests if practical:
> - health endpoint
> - bucket seed exists
> - create QiBit
> - list timeline
> 
> Before coding:
> 1. Inspect docs.
> 2. Produce a concise implementation plan.
> 3. Then implement Phase 1.
> 4. Run install/build/test commands if available.
> 5. Report what was built, what was not built, commands used, and next recommended step.
> 
> Be disciplined:
> Build the spine first.
> ```
> 
> ## After Codex finishes
> 
> Do **not** trust it just because it says “done.” We validate.
> 
> Use this review prompt after it codes:
> 
> ```text
> Review the QiLife Phase 1 implementation in:
>

> 8. Does the Today page show useful spine data?

> 10. Do Actions and Steps exist?
> 11. Is Context Dock present?
> 12. Is Ask QiLife mocked, not real AI?
> 13. Are raw captures preserved?

> 17. Are product names consistent?

> 19. Are tests or smoke checks available?
> 20. What is broken or missing?
> 
> Deliver:
> - pass/fail summary

> - exact patch plan
> - do not modify files until approved
> ```
