> That’s the move. Let Codex code the **spine**, then we come behind it with a crowbar and a lint roller.

### User
> I was thinking about the slow of the app, biggest issue is capture and ingestion it must be seamless and automated. So in reality capture looks like this
> 1. Something happens or something I need to save or document.
> 2. I click New “whatever” 
> 3. Text box and or file upload, I type my note or dictate it, or I upload a file or both, then when I click save the text of the note and or the raw text of the file (OCR first if image or PDF) the the ai, using its intelligence auto populates all the other meta data, The Who what where links to the related records or creates new, those are all in draft mode for my final approval or edit, the approvals or edits are logged and used to fine tune the AIs guesses once confidence is 99% they no longer require manual approvals. And since this is a data we don’t need true folders folders are just views right.

### Assistant
> Yes. That’s the actual ingestion model. And you’re right: **folders should become views**, not rigid storage logic.
> 
> This is the correction:
> 
> # QiLife capture is not “create a task”
> 
> It is:
> 
> **Capture raw input → extract text → AI interprets → draft structured records → Cody approves/edits → system learns → records become official.**
> 
> That is the ingestion spine.
> 
> ---
> 
> # New Capture Flow
> 
> ```text
> Something happens
>   ↓
> New QiBit / New Capture
>   ↓
> Text, dictation, file upload, or both
>   ↓
> Save raw input
>   ↓
> Extract text
>   ├── plain text → use directly
>   ├── PDF → extract text / OCR if needed
>   ├── image → OCR
>   ├── audio → transcription later
>   └── file → metadata + extracted text
>   ↓
> AI interpretation
>   ↓
> Draft suggestions
>   ├── title
>   ├── summary
>   ├── meaning
>   ├── bucket/view
>   ├── thread
>   ├── related people/entities
>   ├── action required?
>   ├── suggested actions
>   ├── steps
>   ├── transaction/obligation
>   ├── knowledge item
>   ├── documents
>   ├── timeline slot
>   └── retrieval tags
>   ↓
> Review screen
>   ├── approve
>   ├── edit
>   ├── reject
>   └── split into multiple QiBits
>   ↓
> Official records created/updated
>   ↓
> Approval/edit logged
>   ↓
> AI confidence profile updated
> ```
> 
> That is the correct flow.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The key distinction
> 
> ## Raw capture is permanent
> 
> The original input should be preserved exactly:
> 
> - typed note
> - dictated text
> - uploaded file
> - OCR text
> - extracted file text
> - timestamp
> - source
> - file hash
> 
> This is evidence.
> 
> ## AI interpretation is draft
> 
> AI guesses should not immediately become truth unless confidence/training rules allow it.
> 
> So we need:
> 
> ```text
> raw_capture = sacred
> ai_draft = proposed
> approved_record = official
> ```
> 
> That makes the system safer and less volatile.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Add a Draft Review Layer
> 
> This is the missing schema piece.
> 
> ## `ingestion_items`
> 
> This is the raw intake record.
> 
> ```text
> ingestion_items
> ├── id
> ├── source_type
> ├── raw_text
> ├── original_file_id
> ├── extracted_text
> ├── ocr_status
> ├── processing_status
> ├── captured_at
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Source types:
> 
> ```text
> manual_text
> dictation
> file_upload
> image_upload
> pdf_upload
> audio_upload
> import
> email_later
> ```
> 
> Processing status:
> 
> ```text
> new
> extracting_text
> extracted
> ai_processing
> draft_ready
> approved
> partially_approved
> rejected
> error
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## `ai_drafts`
> 
> AI proposed structured output.
> 
> ```text
> ai_drafts
> ├── id
> ├── ingestion_item_id
> ├── draft_type
> ├── proposed_json
> ├── confidence
> ├── requires_review
> ├── review_status
> ├── reviewed_at
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Draft types:
> 
> ```text
> qibit
> action
> thread
> person
> transaction
> obligation
> knowledge_item
> document
> event
> link
> tag
> ```
> 
> Review status:
> 
> ```text
> pending
> approved
> edited
> rejected
> auto_approved
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## `review_events`
> 
> This is how the AI learns.
> 
> ```text
> review_events
> ├── id
> ├── ai_draft_id
> ├── reviewer
> ├── decision
> ├── original_proposed_json
> ├── final_approved_json
> ├── correction_summary
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Decision:
> 
> ```text
> approved
> edited
> rejected
> split
> merged
> ```
> 
> This gives us a feedback dataset.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Confidence Thresholds
> 
> Your idea is right, but I’d be careful with “99% confidence.”
> 
> Instead of global “AI is 99% confident,” use **per-field and per-action trust rules**.
> 
> Example:
> 
> | AI Guess | Auto-approve? |
> |---|---:|
> | Bucket from obvious text | yes after confidence proven |
> | Tags | yes |
> | Retrieval summary | yes |
> | Title/summary | maybe |
> | Related person | maybe |
> | Create task | review first |
> | Money obligation | review first longer |
> | Legal interpretation | always review |
> | Delete/archive | never auto |
> | Send message/email | never auto |
> 
> So the system learns safely.
> 
> ## Suggested trust levels
> 
> ```text
> review_required
> suggested_auto
> auto_approve_low_risk
> always_manual
> ```
> 
> ## Example
> 
> AI can auto-tag:
> 
> > `lyft`, `gas`, `finance`
> 
> But should not auto-create:
> 
> > “Zai owes Cody $200”
> 
> without your approval until the pattern is proven and risk is low.
> 
> Money/legal/medical = manual review by default. We are not letting the robot freestyle with rent and court stuff, honey.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Folders as Views
> 
> Yes. In the database app:
> 
> ## Buckets are views, not physical folders
> 
> A QiBit belongs to a bucket by metadata:
> 
> ```text
> bucket_code = 60_finance
> ```
> 
> The app shows:
> 
> ```text
> 60 Finance
> ```
> 
> as a view/filter.
> 
> Later, when exporting to QiNexus, that metadata determines the physical path.
> 
> So:
> 
> ```text
> Database = source of truth
> Folders = export/rendered views
> ```
> 
> ## Better doctrine
> 
> **Folders are projections of metadata.**
> 
> That is the line.
> 
> Meaning:
> 
> - In-app, buckets are metadata and filters.
> - In filesystem exports, buckets become folders.
> - No duplicate manual folder sorting.
> - No file chaos.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Revised Data Flow
> 
> ```text
> Capture Layer
> ├── ingestion_items
> ├── uploaded_files
> ├── extracted_text
> └── raw_capture
> 
> Draft Layer
> ├── ai_drafts
> ├── proposed records
> ├── confidence scores
> └── review required flags
> 
> Approval Layer
> ├── review_events
> ├── accepted corrections
> ├── rejected guesses
> └── trust rules
> 
> Official Layer
> ├── qibits
> ├── actions
> ├── threads
> ├── people
> ├── transactions
> ├── obligations
> ├── knowledge_items
> ├── documents
> ├── events
> └── links
> 
> View Layer
> ├── Timeline
> ├── Buckets
> ├── Threads
> ├── Today
> ├── Money
> ├── People
> ├── Knowledge
> └── Context Dock
> 
> Export Layer
> ├── QiNexus folders
> ├── Markdown
> ├── JSON
> ├── backups
> └── evidence packets
> ```
> 
> That’s robust.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Capture UI Should Work Like This
> 
> ## New QiBit screen
> 
> ```text
> New Capture
> ├── What happened?
> │   ├── text box
> │   ├── dictate button placeholder
> │   ├── upload file
> │   └── source/date controls
> │
> ├── Save + Analyze
> │
> └── Draft Review
>     ├── QiBit draft
>     ├── Related people/entities
>     ├── Bucket/view
>     ├── Thread
>     ├── Suggested actions
>     ├── Suggested steps
>     ├── Money/obligation guesses
>     ├── Knowledge suggestions
>     ├── Documents
>     └── Approve / Edit / Reject
> ```
> 
> ## Draft Review should show cards
> 
> ```text
> AI Drafts
> ├── QiBit Card
> │   ├── title
> │   ├── summary
> │   ├── meaning
> │   └── confidence
> │
> ├── Related Records Card
> │   ├── Cody
> │   ├── Zai
> │   ├── Lyft Income Sprint
> │   └── 60 Finance
> │
> ├── Action Card
> │   ├── Collect reimbursement
> │   └── steps
> │
> ├── Money Card
> │   ├── Obligation: Zai owes Cody $40
> │   └── confidence / review required
> │
> └── Knowledge Card
>     ├── gas reimbursement rule
>     └── related notes
> ```
> 
> You approve all, approve selected, or edit.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Schema Additions We Need
> 
> Add these to the docs/build spec:
> 
> ```text
> ingestion_items
> uploaded_files
> text_extractions
> ai_drafts
> review_events
> trust_rules
> ```
> 
> ## `uploaded_files`
> 
> ```text
> uploaded_files
> ├── id
> ├── original_filename
> ├── stored_path
> ├── mime_type
> ├── file_hash
> ├── size_bytes
> ├── upload_status
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ## `text_extractions`
> 
> ```text
> text_extractions
> ├── id
> ├── uploaded_file_id
> ├── extraction_method
> ├── extracted_text
> ├── confidence
> ├── status
> ├── error_message
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Extraction method:
> 
> ```text
> native_pdf_text
> ocr_image
> ocr_pdf
> manual_text
> audio_transcription
> ```
> 
> ## `trust_rules`
> 
> ```text
> trust_rules
> ├── id
> ├── rule_scope
> ├── field_name
> ├── condition_json
> ├── auto_approve_threshold
> ├── risk_level
> ├── enabled
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> field_name: bucket_code
> condition: if confidence >= 0.95 and prior accepted corrections >= 20
> risk_level: low
> enabled: true
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Important: do OCR async-ish
> 
> Even in local app, don’t block the UI too hard.
> 
> On save:
> 
> 1. Save raw file immediately.
> 2. Show capture as “processing.”
> 3. Extract/OCR text.
> 4. Run AI draft.
> 5. Notify/show draft ready.
> 
> For v1, it can be simple synchronous backend processing, but the data model should support statuses.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Update Codex Scope
> 
> Since Codex is about to code, we need to amend the Phase 1 prompt.
> 
> ## Add to Phase 1
> 
> Phase 1 should include:
> 
> - `ingestion_items`
> - `uploaded_files`
> - `ai_drafts`
> - `review_events`
> - basic text/file upload capture
> - AI mock draft generation
> - draft review UI
> - approve draft → creates QiBit/action/thread/etc.
> 
> Do **not** require real OCR yet unless easy.
> 
> For now:
> 
> - plain text extraction from `.txt`/`.md`
> - PDF/image OCR placeholder
> - store file metadata
> - mark OCR status as `pending` or `not_implemented`
> 
> This avoids blocking Phase 1.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Prompt Addendum for Codex
> 
> Give Codex this before it starts or as an updated instruction:
> 
> ```text
> Important update to Phase 1:
> 
> Capture/ingestion is the highest-priority workflow.
> 
> QiLife must not start as manual CRUD screens. It must start with seamless capture:
> 
> 1. User clicks New Capture / New QiBit.
> 2. User enters text, dictation text, uploads a file, or both.
> 3. App saves the raw capture and file metadata first.
> 4. App extracts text if possible.
> 5. App sends raw text + extracted text to AI mock interpretation.
> 6. AI mock creates draft metadata and draft related records.
> 7. Drafts remain pending for user approval/edit.
> 8. On approval, official records are created/updated:
>    - QiBit
>    - Thread
>    - Action
>    - Action Steps
>    - Knowledge Item
>    - Links
>    - future: person/transaction/obligation/document/event
> 9. Approval/edit/rejection is logged in review_events.
> 10. Later, accepted corrections should train trust rules. For v1, implement trust_rules as a table/stub, not real learning.
> 
> Add these models:
> - IngestionItem
> - UploadedFile
> - TextExtraction
> - AIDraft
> - ReviewEvent
> - TrustRule
> 
> Add these API endpoints:
> - POST /api/ingestion/capture
> - GET /api/ingestion/items
> - GET /api/ingestion/items/{id}
> - POST /api/ingestion/items/{id}/mock-analyze
> - GET /api/ai-drafts/pending
> - POST /api/ai-drafts/{id}/approve
> - POST /api/ai-drafts/{id}/reject
> - POST /api/ai-drafts/{id}/edit-approve
> 
> V1 extraction rules:
> - If input is text, use it directly.
> - If uploaded file is .txt or .md, extract text.
> - For PDF/image/audio, store file metadata and create TextExtraction row with status not_implemented or pending.
> - Do not implement heavy OCR in Phase 1 unless already available.
> - Keep OCR-ready architecture.
> 
> Frontend:
> - Prioritize New Capture flow.
> - Add a capture form with text box and file upload.
> - Add Draft Review page/panel.
> - Show AI mock suggestions as editable draft cards.
> - Approving a QiBit draft should create an official QiBit.
> - Approving an Action draft should create an official Action.
> - Approving Step drafts should create ActionSteps.
> - Keep all AI-created records linked back to the source ingestion item and/or QiBit.
> 
> Data doctrine:
> - Raw capture is sacred and must never be overwritten by AI.
> - AI interpretation is draft until approved.
> - Approved records are official.
> - Folders/buckets are metadata views in the app, not physical folders.
> - Physical folders are only export projections later.
> 
> Update docs if needed before coding:
> - docs/30_data_model/00_data_model_spine.md
> - docs/30_data_model/06_database_stability_strategy.md
> - docs/40_ui_flows/00_app_flow_and_screens.md
> - docs/60_ai_layer/00_ai_layer_blueprint.md
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final answer
> 
> Yes. This is the real MVP:
> 
> **Capture → Extract → AI Draft → Review → Approve → Official Record → Learn → Retrieve.**
> 
> Not manual tables.
> 
> And yes:
> 
> **Folders are views. Buckets are metadata. Physical folders are exports.**
> 
> That is the correct architecture.

### User
> Ok so now if we tie this all together what would this app look like and work like based on what we have discussed and what I need and what you know I need.

### Assistant
> Yes. Tied together, this is what QiLife becomes:
> 
> # QiLife: your Personal LifeDesk
> 
> QiLife is not a todo app, not a wiki, not a finance app, and not a CRM.
> 
> It is a **single-agent helpdesk for your life**.
> 
> You are the agent.  
> Your life is the company.  
> Every incoming thing becomes a **QiBit**.  
> The app’s job is to help you capture it, understand it, route it, act on it, document it, resolve it, and retrieve it later with AI.
> 
> That’s the sauce.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What the app looks like
> 
> ## Main layout
> 
> It should look like a clean helpdesk/operator console.
> 
> ```text
> ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
> │ QiLife        Search      + New Capture      Ask QiLife      │
> ├──────────────┬───────────────────────────────┬───────────────┤
> │ Left Nav     │ Main Workspace                │ Context Dock  │
> │              │                               │               │
> │ Today        │ Current page / selected item  │ AI Summary    │
> │ Capture      │                               │ Related Bits  │
> │ Inbox        │                               │ Knowledge     │
> │ Timeline     │                               │ People        │
> │ Threads      │                               │ Actions       │
> │ Actions      │                               │ Documents     │
> │ Calendar     │                               │ Money         │
> │ People       │                               │ Reflection    │
> │ Money        │                               │               │
> │ Knowledge    │                               │               │
> │ Documents    │                               │               │
> │ Ask QiLife   │                               │               │
> └──────────────┴───────────────────────────────┴───────────────┘
> ```
> 
> The **center** is where you work.  
> The **right side** tells you what matters.  
> The **top capture button** is always available.
> 
> No separate wiki. No separate task app. No separate “where did I put that?” nonsense.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The core flow
> 
> Everything starts with:
> 
> # “What happened?”
> 
> You click **New Capture**.
> 
> You can:
> 
> - type a note
> - dictate a note
> - upload a file
> - upload a screenshot
> - upload a PDF
> - attach a receipt
> - paste a text message
> - dump a messy thought
> - add both text and file together
> 
> Then QiLife does this:
> 
> ```text
> Capture raw input
> ↓
> Save original text/file
> ↓
> Extract text from file if possible
> ↓
> AI interprets
> ↓
> AI creates draft suggestions
> ↓
> You approve/edit/reject
> ↓
> Official records are created
> ↓
> Timeline updates
> ↓
> Actions/threads/money/knowledge link together
> ↓
> AI can retrieve it later
> ```
> 
> That is the whole ingestion engine.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Example: messy real-life capture
> 
> You type:
> 
> > Zai owes me $40 for gas from yesterday and I need to ask him before Friday because I’m short for the rental.
> 
> QiLife creates a **draft review**:
> 
> ```text
> QiBit Draft
> Title: Zai gas reimbursement
> Summary: Zai owes Cody $40 for gas from yesterday.
> Meaning: Open reimbursement obligation affecting rental cashflow.
> Bucket: 60 Finance
> Thread: Lyft Income Sprint / Zai Household Money
> People: Zai, Cody
> Action Required: Yes
> 
> Suggested Action:
> Ask Zai for $40 gas reimbursement before Friday.
> 
> Steps:
> 1. Confirm amount.
> 2. Message Zai.
> 3. Mark paid when received.
> 4. Log transaction when paid.
> 
> Obligation:
> Zai owes Cody $40 for gas.
> 
> Future Slot:
> Waiting On / This Week
> 
> Tags:
> gas, Zai, reimbursement, Lyft, rental
> ```
> 
> You approve it.
> 
> Then QiLife creates:
> 
> - QiBit
> - Action
> - Obligation
> - Links to Zai
> - Links to Finance bucket
> - Links to Lyft thread
> - Timeline entry
> - Activity log entry
> 
> Now later you can ask:
> 
> > Who owes me money?
> 
> And it shows up.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The main objects
> 
> ## 1. QiBit
> 
> The atomic unit.
> 
> A QiBit is one captured unit of life data.
> 
> It can be:
> 
> - thought
> - text
> - note
> - receipt
> - task seed
> - problem
> - conversation
> - decision
> - document
> - money event
> - obligation
> - reflection
> - “this matters somehow”
> 
> QiBit is the ticket.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. Timeline
> 
> The spine.
> 
> Everything appears chronologically.
> 
> The timeline answers:
> 
> > What happened?
> 
> Not just “what tasks are due,” but what actually happened across your life.
> 
> It shows:
> 
> - captures
> - tasks created
> - tasks completed
> - files uploaded
> - money logged
> - obligations opened/resolved
> - reflections
> - AI summaries
> - thread updates
> 
> This becomes your memory trail.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Buckets
> 
> Buckets are metadata views, not physical folders.
> 
> They match your real structure:
> 
> ```text
> 00 Inbox
> 10 Workbench
> 20 Timeline
> 30 Life
> 40 People
> 50 Business
> 60 Finance
> 70 Legal
> 80 Tech
> 90 Assets
> 100 Data
> 110 Reference
> 900 Archive
> 990 System
> ```
> 
> Inside the app, buckets are filters/views.
> 
> Later, exports can become real folders.
> 
> So:
> 
> ```text
> Database = source of truth
> Buckets = metadata views
> Folders = export projections
> ```
> 
> That’s the clean model.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. Threads
> 
> Threads are ongoing storylines.
> 
> Not everything is a “project.” Some things are cases, issues, situations, or long-running life messes with a trench coat on.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - Surplus Check Recovery
> - Lyft Income Sprint
> - Zai Lease / Household Money
> - Mom Care Notes
> - QiLife Build
> - QiServer Cleanup
> - Family Hub
> - Jeep / Vehicle
> - Phone Replacement
> 
> A thread page shows:
> 
> - related QiBits
> - actions
> - steps
> - people
> - money
> - documents
> - knowledge
> - timeline
> - AI summary
> - unresolved loops
> 
> Thread answers:
> 
> > What’s the whole situation?
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. Actions
> 
> Actions are tasks/work orders.
> 
> They are not orphaned todo items.
> 
> Every action should ideally link back to:
> 
> - a QiBit
> - a thread
> - a bucket
> - a person/entity
> - possibly money/docs/knowledge
> 
> Action answers:
> 
> > What do I need to do?
> 
> Action fields matter:
> 
> - status
> - priority
> - due date
> - scheduled date
> - energy
> - context: phone, home, computer, errands, car, anywhere
> - steps
> - resolution note
> 
> This is ADHD-friendly because it lets you filter by reality, not fantasy.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. Context Dock
> 
> This is one of the most important parts.
> 
> Every major screen has a right-side **Context Dock**.
> 
> When you open a QiBit, thread, action, person, money item, or document, the Context Dock shows:
> 
> - relevant knowledge
> - related QiBits
> - linked documents
> - related people
> - related money
> - open actions
> - AI summary
> - prior decisions
> - reflection prompts
> 
> This replaces the need for a separate wiki.
> 
> You don’t “go to the knowledge base.”  
> The knowledge comes to the thing you are working on.
> 
> That is the helpdesk-agent model.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 7. Knowledge
> 
> Knowledge still exists centrally, but it is also contextual.
> 
> There is a Knowledge page for browsing/searching, but knowledge items are linked to things.
> 
> Example knowledge items:
> 
> - QiBit lifecycle doctrine
> - Gas categorization rule
> - Family Operating System one-source rule
> - Marion County surplus check follow-up rule
> - QiServer deployment steps
> - Zai lease terms
> - Court filing notes
> - Finance categorization standards
> 
> Each knowledge item can be linked to:
> 
> - bucket
> - thread
> - action
> - QiBit
> - person
> - document
> - money item
> 
> So it works like helpdesk KB articles: centrally searchable, but suggested where relevant.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 8. Money
> 
> Money is not just “budget.”
> 
> Money tracks:
> 
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - who owes me
> - who I owe
> - recurring items later
> - budget categories later
> - evidence/receipts
> - related threads
> 
> Example:
> 
> A transaction is:
> 
> > Cody paid $35 at Circle K for Lyft gas.
> 
> An obligation is:
> 
> > Zai owes Cody $40.
> 
> Those are different things. The app should treat them differently.
> 
> Money answers:
> 
> > What moved, what is owed, and what is unresolved?
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 9. Ask QiLife
> 
> Ask QiLife is not a random chatbot.
> 
> It is wired into:
> 
> - QiBits
> - timeline
> - actions
> - threads
> - people
> - money
> - knowledge
> - documents
> - activity logs
> 
> You can ask:
> 
> - What happened today?
> - What matters right now?
> - Who owes me money?
> - What am I waiting on?
> - What tasks involve Zai?
> - What legal threads are open?
> - What did I capture but not process?
> - What is the next action on the surplus check?
> - What did I spend on gas this week?
> - Turn this rant into QiBits and actions.
> - What is real, what is noise, and what do I do next?
> 
> And it answers with supporting records, not vibes in a trench coat.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What happens when you open the app
> 
> ## Today page
> 
> This is your command center.
> 
> It shows:
> 
> ```text
> Today
> ├── AI Focus Brief
> ├── Scheduled Actions
> ├── Due Actions
> ├── Open Loops
> ├── Waiting On
> ├── New QiBits
> ├── Drafts Needing Approval
> ├── Money Today
> ├── Thread Updates
> └── Reflection Prompt
> ```
> 
> The AI brief should sound like:
> 
> > Today’s real constraints are cashflow, transportation, and caregiving. The top actions are finish Lyft rides, check open money obligations, and process unreviewed captures. Tech cleanup is noise unless it blocks income or care.
> 
> That is what you need. Not a dumb list of 47 overdue tasks judging you from a sidebar.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The most important screen: New Capture
> 
> This is the heart.
> 
> ```text
> New Capture
> ├── What happened?
> │   ├── text box
> │   ├── dictate option
> │   ├── upload file
> │   ├── attach image/PDF
> │   └── happened date/time
> │
> ├── Save + Analyze
> │
> └── Draft Review
>     ├── QiBit Draft
>     ├── Suggested Bucket
>     ├── Suggested Thread
>     ├── Related People
>     ├── Suggested Actions
>     ├── Suggested Steps
>     ├── Suggested Money/Obligation
>     ├── Suggested Knowledge
>     ├── Suggested Tags/Links
>     └── Approve / Edit / Reject
> ```
> 
> This is the flow that matters more than any dashboard.
> 
> Because the app lives or dies by capture.
> 
> If capture is friction, the app is dead. Period.
> 
> ---
> 
> # How AI approval works
> 
> At first, AI suggestions are drafts.
> 
> You approve, edit, or reject.
> 
> QiLife logs that.
> 
> Over time, when the AI repeatedly gets low-risk things right, it can auto-approve some fields.
> 
> But not everything.
> 
> ## Safe to auto-approve eventually
> 
> - tags
> - bucket guesses
> - summaries
> - retrieval summaries
> - obvious thread links
> 
> ## Needs review longer
> 
> - people links
> - task creation
> - due dates
> - money categorization
> 
> ## Always careful/manual
> 
> - legal interpretation
> - medical/care instructions
> - money obligations
> - deleting/archiving
> - sending messages
> - anything with external consequences
> 
> So the app learns without becoming a confident little menace.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What the database does underneath
> 
> The database has layers:
> 
> ```text
> Raw Layer
> ├── ingestion_items
> ├── uploaded_files
> ├── text_extractions
> └── raw QiBit capture
> 
> Draft Layer
> ├── ai_drafts
> ├── confidence scores
> └── proposed records
> 
> Approval Layer
> ├── review_events
> ├── accepted edits
> ├── rejected drafts
> └── trust rules
> 
> Official Layer
> ├── qibits
> ├── threads
> ├── actions
> ├── steps
> ├── people
> ├── transactions
> ├── obligations
> ├── documents
> ├── knowledge_items
> └── events
> 
> History Layer
> ├── activity_log
> └── daily_summaries
> 
> Relationship Layer
> └── links
> ```
> 
> That structure makes the app less volatile because the raw truth, AI guess, and official record are separate.
> 
> AI does not overwrite reality. Good little robot stays in its lane.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What the app feels like
> 
> It should feel like:
> 
> - helpdesk console
> - command center
> - personal operations cockpit
> - timeline memory system
> - AI-assisted intake desk
> - contextual knowledge base
> 
> It should not feel like:
> 
> - Notion
> - Salesforce
> - a spreadsheet
> - a generic todo app
> - a wiki from 2009
> - a calendar with delusions of grandeur
> 
> ---
> 
> # The daily loop
> 
> ## Morning
> 
> Open Today.
> 
> QiLife says:
> 
> - here’s what matters
> - here’s what’s due
> - here’s what’s waiting
> - here are unprocessed captures
> - here’s your realistic focus
> 
> ## During the day
> 
> Something happens.
> 
> You hit New Capture.
> 
> Dump text/file/voice.
> 
> Save + Analyze.
> 
> Approve drafts later or immediately.
> 
> ## While working
> 
> Open an action or thread.
> 
> Context Dock shows:
> 
> - what you know
> - related history
> - documents
> - people
> - money
> - AI next action
> 
> ## End of day
> 
> QiLife summarizes:
> 
> - what happened
> - what got done
> - what moved money-wise
> - who/what is waiting
> - what rolled forward
> - what pattern/reflection matters
> 
> That becomes daily memory.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The final app shape
> 
> ```text
> QiLife
> ├── Capture
> │   ├── ingestion
> │   ├── file upload
> │   ├── text extraction/OCR-ready
> │   ├── AI drafts
> │   └── review/approval
> │
> ├── Timeline
> │   ├── all QiBits
> │   ├── daily activity
> │   ├── resolutions
> │   └── summaries
> │
> ├── Buckets
> │   ├── metadata views
> │   └── folder-aligned exports later
> │
> ├── Threads
> │   ├── cases
> │   ├── projects
> │   ├── storylines
> │   └── ongoing situations
> │
> ├── Actions
> │   ├── tasks
> │   ├── steps
> │   ├── waiting
> │   ├── scheduled
> │   └── resolved
> │
> ├── Context Dock
> │   ├── knowledge
> │   ├── related QiBits
> │   ├── docs
> │   ├── people
> │   ├── money
> │   └── AI summary
> │
> ├── Knowledge
> │   ├── central KB
> │   ├── linked articles
> │   ├── repo docs indexed later
> │   └── contextual surfacing
> │
> ├── Money
> │   ├── transactions
> │   ├── obligations
> │   ├── who owes me
> │   └── who I owe
> │
> ├── People
> │   ├── lightweight entities
> │   ├── history
> │   └── related records
> │
> └── Ask QiLife
>     ├── retrieval
>     ├── triage
>     ├── summaries
>     ├── next actions
>     └── reflection
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # The simplest truth
> 
> QiLife should answer six questions all day:
> 
> 1. **What happened?**
> 2. **What does it mean?**
> 3. **Who/what is related?**
> 4. **What needs to happen?**
> 5. **Where does this belong in time/context?**
> 6. **How do I find/use it later?**
> 
> Everything else is implementation.
> 
> This is the app you need: a **capture-first, AI-assisted, timeline-based Personal LifeDesk** where folders are views, knowledge is contextual, and every life item becomes structured enough to act on without losing the raw truth.

### User
> Oh honey a see one glaring problem with this, do you know what it is. I’ll give you three guesses…

### Assistant
> Oh I already know where you’re probably going, honey.
> 
> My three guesses:
> 
> ## Guess 1 — Capture still assumes you open the app first
> 
> The glaring problem: **when life happens, you may not have the time, energy, or executive function to open QiLife, click New Capture, type, upload, review, approve, etc.**
> 
> So capture cannot only live inside the app.
> 
> It needs **external capture channels**:
> 
> - phone share sheet
> - quick mobile shortcut
> - voice memo
> - text-to-QiLife
> - email-to-QiLife
> - screenshot/import folder watcher
> - browser extension later
> - folder drop zone
> - maybe Telegram/WhatsApp/SMS-style capture later
> 
> Because if capture requires “going into the system,” the system fails exactly when you need it most.
> 
> ## Guess 2 — Approval queue can become another inbox graveyard
> 
> AI drafts are great, but if every capture creates 8 pending cards, congratulations, we built a second job.
> 
> So the review flow must be **tiered**:
> 
> - low-risk metadata auto-applies
> - medium-risk drafts batch-review
> - high-risk money/legal/care items require explicit approval
> - “save now, clean later” mode exists
> - daily review is short and prioritized
> 
> Otherwise the app becomes: “Here are 87 things to approve, enjoy your nervous breakdown.”
> 
> ## Guess 3 — “What happened?” is not always one thing
> 
> One messy capture may contain:
> 
> - 3 tasks
> - 2 people
> - 1 transaction
> - 1 obligation
> - 1 emotional note
> - 1 knowledge update
> - 1 future reminder
> 
> So the system needs **split / merge / bundle logic**.
> 
> The raw capture stays one ingestion item, but AI may propose multiple QiBits or linked records.
> 
> Example:
> 
> > “Mom needs meds, Zai owes gas, and I need to call clerk tomorrow.”
> 
> That is not one QiBit. That is a bundle.
> 
> ---
> 
> My bet? You’re pointing at **Guess 1**:
> 
> **Capture has to happen from wherever you already are, not only inside QiLife.**
> 
> Because that is the real make-or-break. If the intake isn’t frictionless, the whole LifeDesk becomes a beautiful abandoned building.

### Assistant
> Ohhh. Yeah. I see it.
> 
> We designed a **great app**.
> 
> But we’re in the age of **AI agents**.
> 
> And everybody wants/needs a **personal AI assistant that can actually do things**, not another dashboard they have to babysit.
> 
> That’s the glaring problem:
> 
> # QiLife should not be app-first.
> 
> It should be **AI-first / agent-first**, with the app as the control panel.
> 
> The app is not the product.
> 
> The **agent connected to your life data** is the product.
> 
> ## Corrected model
> 
> QiLife should be:
> 
> ```text
> AI Life Agent
> ├── Capture from anywhere
> ├── Understand what happened
> ├── Create/update records
> ├── Ask clarifying questions only when needed
> ├── Retrieve context
> ├── Suggest next actions
> ├── Maintain timeline
> ├── Track obligations
> ├── Summarize days/weeks/threads
> └── Use the app UI as its dashboard/control panel
> ```
> 
> The app is where you review, approve, browse, and manage.  
> But the main interaction should be:
> 
> > “Hey QiLife, this happened. Handle it.”
> 
> Not:
> 
> > “Open app → click module → fill form → assign bucket → link thread → create action → tag person…”
> 
> Absolutely not. That’s just Notion wearing a helpdesk costume.
> 
> ## The real architecture
> 
> # Agent-first, database-backed, UI-assisted
> 
> ```text
> Capture Channels
>     ↓
> AI Agent / Orchestrator
>     ↓
> Draft + Approval Engine
>     ↓
> QiLife Database
>     ↓
> App Console / Context Dock / Timeline
> ```
> 
> The UI is the **agent console**.
> 
> The AI is the **operator**.
> 
> The database is the **memory**.
> 
> ## The app should work like this
> 
> You say:
> 
> > “Zai still owes me forty for gas and I need to ask before Friday.”
> 
> QiLife says:
> 
> > “I drafted an obligation for Zai owing $40, linked it to Finance and Lyft Income Sprint, and created a reminder action for Thursday. Approve?”
> 
> You tap approve.
> 
> Done.
> 
> That’s the future-facing version.
> 
> ## What changes in the blueprint
> 
> We need to add an **Agent Layer** as a first-class core, not “AI page later.”
> 
> ## New spine
> 
> ```text
> QiLife Agent
> ├── Intake
> ├── Interpretation
> ├── Drafting
> ├── Approval
> ├── Record Creation
> ├── Retrieval
> ├── Automation
> ├── Reflection
> └── UI Console
> ```
> 
> ## Add this module
> 
> # Agent Orchestrator
> 
> Responsibilities:
> 
> - receive captures
> - classify intent
> - extract entities
> - draft QiBits/actions/threads/money/knowledge
> - ask clarifying questions
> - route low-risk items automatically
> - queue high-risk items for approval
> - retrieve supporting context
> - execute approved updates
> - log what it did
> 
> ## Add this API concept
> 
> Instead of only CRUD endpoints:
> 
> ```text
> POST /api/agent/capture
> POST /api/agent/ask
> POST /api/agent/review-draft
> POST /api/agent/approve
> POST /api/agent/reject
> POST /api/agent/execute
> ```
> 
> CRUD still exists, but the primary flow is agent commands.
> 
> ## The interface should have two modes
> 
> ### 1. Agent Mode
> 
> Natural language / voice / capture-first.
> 
> ```text
> “What happened?”
> “Ask QiLife”
> “Handle this”
> “Summarize today”
> “What am I missing?”
> ```
> 
> ### 2. Console Mode
> 
> Visual management.
> 
> ```text
> Timeline
> Threads
> Actions
> Money
> People
> Knowledge
> Documents
> ```
> 
> Agent Mode is the front door.  
> Console Mode is the control room.
> 
> ## The real product sentence
> 
> Better version:
> 
> **QiLife is an AI Life Agent with a Personal LifeDesk console, built around QiBits, timeline memory, contextual knowledge, and human approval.**
> 
> That’s sharper.
> 
> ## Why this matters
> 
> Because if we build only the app, you still have to become the clerk.
> 
> But the point is:
> 
> > QiLife should be the clerk.
>

> 
> You should not have to organize your life manually just because the app has nice tables.
>

> You start talking:
> 
> > “Okay, today was a lot. Mom was texting about meds again, Zai still hasn’t paid the gas money, I’m behind on the rental, and I need to get these rides done but I’m exhausted…”
> 
> QiLife should:
> 
> ### 1. Capture the raw conversation
> 
> Preserve transcript.
> 
> ### 2. Extract QiBits
> 
> - Mom medication coordination issue
> - Zai gas obligation still open
> - rental cashflow pressure
> - Lyft income task
> - fatigue/overload signal
> 
> ### 3. Correlate
> 
> Find similar days:
> 
> - days with cashflow + caregiving + transportation pressure
> - days where Lyft income was required
> - days involving Zai obligations
> - days involving medication coordination friction
> 
> ### 4. Interpret
> 
> > “This is not five unrelated issues. It is an overload cluster: cashflow pressure + caregiving interruptions + transportation dependency + unresolved household obligation.”
> 
> ### 5. Draft action plan
> 
> ```text
> Action Plan
> ├── Must Do
> │   ├── Finish minimum profitable Lyft rides
> │   ├── Track gas/rental numbers
> │   └── Confirm mom med status in one source of truth
> │
> ├── Waiting On
> │   └── Zai gas repayment
> │
> ├── Do Not Touch Today
> │   ├── repo refactors
> │   ├── app architecture rabbit holes
> │   └── non-blocking file cleanup
> │
> └── Follow-up
>     ├── Ask Zai for repayment
>     ├── Log actual Lyft net after gas
>     └── Summarize caregiving friction pattern
> ```
> 
> ### 6. Draft records
> 
> - QiBits
> - actions
> - obligation update
> - daily report
> - thread updates
> - reflection/knowledge note
> 
> ### 7. Ask for approval only where needed
> 
> > “I can save the daily report, update the Zai obligation, and create 3 actions. Approve?”
> 
> That is the correct interaction.
> 
> ## New core module: Insight Engine
> 
> We need to add this explicitly.
> 
> ```text
> Insight Engine
> ├── daily pattern comparison
> ├── similar-day retrieval
> ├── unresolved-loop detection
> ├── repeated-person friction
> ├── money pressure detection
> ├── task rollover detection
> ├── thread stagnation detection
> ├── emotional-load clustering
> ├── action-plan drafting
> └── report generation
> ```
> 
> This is where QiLife becomes “you in app form.”
> 
> ## New backend pieces
> 
> Add these to the backend blueprint:
> 
> ```text
> insights
> patterns
> reports
> agent_sessions
> agent_messages
> retrieval_runs
> similarity_matches
> daily_metrics
> ```
> 
> ### `agent_sessions`
> 
> Stores the conversation about your day.
> 
> ```text
> agent_sessions
> ├── id
> ├── session_type
> ├── started_at
> ├── ended_at
> ├── summary
> ├── status
> └── created_at
> ```
> 
> Session types:
> 
> ```text
> daily_checkin
> brain_dump
> thread_review
> money_review
> crisis_triage
> planning
> reflection
> ```
> 
> ### `agent_messages`
> 
> ```text
> agent_messages
> ├── id
> ├── session_id
> ├── role
> ├── content
> ├── created_at
> └── metadata_json
> ```
> 
> ### `insights`
> 
> ```text
> insights
> ├── id
> ├── insight_type
> ├── title
> ├── summary
> ├── evidence_json
> ├── related_records_json
> ├── confidence
> ├── status
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Types:
> 
> ```text
> pattern
> risk
> opportunity
> unresolved_loop
> similar_day
> money_pressure
> task_rollover
> caregiving_load
> relationship_friction
> system_bottleneck
> ```
> 
> ### `reports`
> 
> ```text
> reports
> ├── id
> ├── report_type
> ├── title
> ├── body_markdown
> ├── date_range_start
> ├── date_range_end
> ├── source_records_json
> ├── created_by
> ├── reviewed
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Report types:
> 
> ```text
> daily_report
> weekly_review
> thread_report
> money_report
> care_report
> legal_report
> reflection_report
> ```
> 
> ### `similarity_matches`
> 
> ```text
> similarity_matches
> ├── id
> ├── source_record_type
> ├── source_record_id
> ├── matched_record_type
> ├── matched_record_id
> ├── match_reason
> ├── score
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Eventually this uses embeddings. V1 can mock or use keyword overlap.
> 
> ## Retrieval has to be hybrid
> 
> Do not rely only on embeddings.
> 
> Use:
> 
> ```text
> Retrieval
> ├── exact links
> ├── bucket/thread/person filters
> ├── date/time similarity
> ├── tags
> ├── full-text search
> ├── status/open-loop logic
> ├── money/obligation logic
> ├── embeddings later
> └── AI reasoning over results
> ```
> 
> Embeddings are useful. They are not the whole brain.
> 
> ## The agent should have jobs
> 
> Think of QiLife Agent as multiple internal roles, even if one model handles them:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife Agent
> ├── Intake Clerk
> │   └── captures and extracts
> ├── Triage Agent
> │   └── classifies and routes
> ├── Case Manager
> │   └── connects to threads/actions
> ├── Knowledge Librarian
> │   └── retrieves relevant context
> ├── Pattern Analyst
> │   └── finds similar days/repeated issues
> ├── Planner
> │   └── creates action plans
> ├── Auditor
> │   └── logs and preserves history
> └── Briefer
>     └── explains what matters now
> ```
> 
> The UI can still show one “Ask QiLife,” but the backend should be designed as agent services.
> 
> ## What needs to change in the Codex plan
> 
> Before Codex codes too much, add this amendment:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife is agent-first, not app-first.
> 
> The app console is the cockpit for an AI Life Agent. The primary backend flow is not manual CRUD. It is:
> 
> Capture / Conversation
> → Ingestion
> → Retrieval
> → Correlation
> → AI Drafts
> → Review / Approval
> → Official Records
> → Insights / Reports
> → Next Actions
> 
> Add these modules as first-class backend design targets, even if v1 uses mocks:
> 
> - agent_sessions
> - agent_messages
> - insights
> - reports
> - similarity_matches
> - retrieval_runs
> 
> The Cockpit/Today page should include:
> - Copilot Brief
> - Insight Feed
> - Draft Queue
> - Open Loops
> - Similar Patterns placeholder
> - Today’s Actions
> 
> Ask QiLife should support:
> - daily check-in
> - brain dump
> - thread review
> - money review
> - planning
> - reflection
> 
> V1 can mock retrieval and pattern matching, but the schema and service boundaries must exist.
> ```
> 
> ## The actual MVP now
> 
> Not “create QiBit manually.”
> 
> The MVP is:
> 
> 1. You brain dump.
> 2. QiLife stores the conversation.
> 3. QiLife extracts draft QiBits/actions/obligations.
> 4. QiLife retrieves related records.
> 5. QiLife produces a draft daily brief/action plan.
> 6. You approve/edit.
> 7. It updates the timeline and action ledger.
> 
> That’s the MVP.
> 
> Everything else supports that.
> 
> ## The final product sentence
> 
> **QiLife is an AI Life Copilot with a Personal LifeDesk cockpit: it captures what happens, correlates it with your structured life memory, drafts insights and actions, and keeps your timeline, tasks, knowledge, money, and obligations coherent with minimal intervention.**
> 
> That’s it.
> 
> That is the thing you’ve needed this whole time.

### User
> And the good thing is we have already been dabbling with all these types of ideas and tools now it’s time to bring it all together. So what Indea is needed. Qdrant, Neo4j, Supa, Postgres’s, Reid’s, where do assets go, data? blobs? etc?

### Assistant
> Yes. We’ve already played with all the ingredients. Now we stop hoarding tools and define the actual **QiLife backend stack**.
> 
> Blunt answer: **you do not need all of Qdrant + Neo4j + Supabase + Postgres + Redis on day one.** That would be architecture cosplay. Powerful, yes. Necessary for v1, no.
> 
> You need a stack that supports:
> 
> 1. structured life records  
> 2. raw capture + files  
> 3. AI retrieval  
> 4. similarity/pattern matching  
> 5. timeline/history  
> 6. reports/insights  
> 7. future automation  
> 8. exports/backups  
> 9. low volatility  
> 
> So we layer it.
> 
> ---
> 
> # QiLife backend stack — sane version
> 
> ## Phase 1: Local-first MVP
> 
> Use:
> 
> ```text
> SQLite
> FastAPI
> Local file storage
> Markdown/JSON exports
> Optional local embeddings later
> ```
> 
> This gets the app usable without infrastructure hell.
> 
> ### Why SQLite first?
> 
> Because QiLife is single-user at first.
> 
> SQLite gives you:
> 
> - one database file
> - easy backup
> - easy local dev
> - low maintenance
> - portable data
> - fewer moving parts
> - future migration path to Postgres
> 
> For now:
> 
> ```text
> data/db/qilife.sqlite
> ```
> 
> This is the brainstem.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Phase 2: Server version
> 
> Once the app works, move to:
> 
> ```text
> Postgres
> FastAPI
> Local/server file storage
> Qdrant
> Redis optional
> ```
> 
> This is where QiLife becomes a real private backend on QiServer.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final likely stack
> 
> ## Core database
> 
> ### Postgres
> 
> Use for official structured data.
> 
> Stores:
> 
> - QiBits
> - ingestion items
> - AI drafts
> - review events
> - people
> - threads
> - actions
> - steps
> - transactions
> - obligations
> - knowledge items
> - documents metadata
> - agent sessions
> - reports
> - insights
> - activity log
> - links
> 
> Postgres is the **source of truth** once server-based.
> 
> ### SQLite
> 
> Use for:
> 
> - v1 local dev
> - portable backup
> - offline/local mode
> - prototype testing
> 
> SQLite is the **local first brain**.
> 
> Postgres is the **server brain**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Vector database
> 
> ### Qdrant
> 
> Use Qdrant for semantic memory/search.
> 
> Stores embeddings for:
> 
> - QiBits
> - notes
> - knowledge items
> - document extracted text
> - reports
> - agent sessions
> - daily summaries
> - thread summaries
> - reflections
> 
> Qdrant answers:
> 
> > “What is similar to this?”  
> > “Have I had days like this before?”  
> > “What knowledge is relevant?”  
> > “What old pattern does this resemble?”  
> 
> This is where “similar days” becomes powerful.
> 
> But do **not** start here on day one unless the base records already exist.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Graph database
> 
> ### Neo4j
> 
> Optional later.
> 
> Neo4j is useful for relationship exploration:
> 
> - person → obligation → transaction → thread
> - QiBit → action → document → court case
> - repeated people/entities across patterns
> - relationship maps
> - “show me the network around this issue”
> 
> But here is the truth:
> 
> ## You do not need Neo4j in v1.
> 
> The `links` table in SQLite/Postgres gets you 80% of the graph value.
> 
> Start with:
> 
> ```text
> links table
> ```
> 
> Later, export/sync to Neo4j if graph visualization becomes useful.
> 
> Neo4j is **analysis/visualization layer**, not the first source of truth.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Cache / queues
> 
> ### Redis
> 
> Use later for:
> 
> - background jobs
> - OCR processing queue
> - AI processing queue
> - agent task queue
> - rate limiting
> - temporary session state
> - notifications
> - scheduled jobs
> 
> Do not use Redis as truth storage.
> 
> Redis is the **short-term nervous system**, not the memory.
> 
> For v1, you can skip Redis and use simple background tasks.
> 
> Later:
> 
> ```text
> Redis + RQ / Celery / Dramatiq / FastAPI background workers
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Supabase
> 
> ### Use only if we need hosted Postgres/auth/storage quickly.
> 
> You already have mixed feelings about Supabase and prefer Cloudflare-first for some things.
> 
> For QiLife:
> 
> ## Supabase is not required.
> 
> Possible uses:
> 
> - hosted Postgres
> - auth if you later need multi-device login
> - storage if you want cloud blob storage
> - real-time sync
> 
> But for private QiLife:
> 
> ```text
> QiServer Postgres > Supabase
> ```
> 
> Supabase is helpful if you need quick hosted infrastructure. But if this is your private Life Copilot, keep the source of truth under your control.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Where assets go
> 
> This matters.
> 
> Do not shove files into the database.
> 
> ## Use file storage for blobs/assets
> 
> Actual files live in:
> 
> ```text
> data/files/
> ```
> 
> The database stores metadata.
> 
> Suggested layout:
> 
> ```text
> data/
> ├── db/
> │   └── qilife.sqlite
> │
> ├── files/
> │   ├── uploads/
> │   │   ├── documents/
> │   │   ├── images/
> │   │   ├── audio/
> │   │   ├── video/
> │   │   └── raw/
> │   │
> │   ├── processed/
> │   │   ├── ocr/
> │   │   ├── thumbnails/
> │   │   ├── previews/
> │   │   └── extracted_text/
> │   │
> │   └── attachments/
> │
> ├── exports/
> │   ├── markdown/
> │   ├── json/
> │   ├── csv/
> │   └── evidence_packets/
> │
> ├── backups/
> │   ├── db/
> │   ├── files/
> │   └── full/
> │
> └── indexes/
>     ├── qdrant/
>     └── search/
> ```
> 
> ## Database table: `documents`
> 
> Stores:
> 
> ```text
> documents
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── original_filename
> ├── stored_path
> ├── mime_type
> ├── file_hash
> ├── size_bytes
> ├── document_type
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── source_qibit_id
> ├── extracted_text_path
> ├── ocr_status
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> The file is on disk. The record is in DB. The relationship is through links.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Blob storage later
> 
> When server-based, you have three options.
> 
> ## Option A: local disk on QiServer
> 
> Best for first private deployment.
> 
> ```text
> /srv/qilife/data/files/
> ```
> 
> Pros:
> 
> - simple
> - private
> - fast
> - no cloud dependency
> 
> Cons:
> 
> - you must back it up properly
> 
> ## Option B: S3-compatible storage
> 
> Good later.
> 
> Could be:
> 
> - Cloudflare R2
> - MinIO
> - Backblaze B2
> - Wasabi
> 
> Use this when file volume grows or you want resilient blob storage.
> 
> ## Option C: Google Drive/QiNexus export
> 
> Good for human-readable archive/backbone.
> 
> QiLife database remains truth.  
> QiNexus/Drive is export/archive layer.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Best storage doctrine
> 
> ```text
> Postgres/SQLite = structured truth
> File storage = raw blobs/assets
> Qdrant = semantic memory
> Links table = relationship truth
> Neo4j = optional graph mirror
> Markdown exports = human-readable archive
> Redis = queue/cache, not truth
> ```
> 
> That is the doctrine.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What each thing is for
> 
> ## SQLite
> 
> Use now.
> 
> ```text
> Local app database
> Fast prototyping
> Offline/portable backup
> ```
> 
> ## Postgres
> 
> Use later as server truth.
> 
> ```text
> Main structured database
> Reliable backend
> Good indexing
> Migrations
> Long-term source of truth
> ```
> 
> ## Qdrant
> 
> Use for AI memory.
> 
> ```text
> Embeddings
> Similarity search
> Similar days
> Related notes
> Pattern retrieval
> Context suggestions
> ```
> 
> ## Neo4j
> 
> Use later if graph maps become valuable.
> 
> ```text
> Relationship visualization
> Network analysis
> People/thread/money/document maps
> Pattern exploration
> ```
> 
> ## Redis
> 
> Use later for background work.
> 
> ```text
> OCR queue
> AI processing queue
> notifications
> scheduled tasks
> temporary cache
> ```
> 
> ## Supabase
> 
> Probably not needed for core.
> 
> ```text
> Optional hosted Postgres/auth/storage
> Only if convenience beats control
> ```
> 
> ## Cloudflare R2 / MinIO
> 
> Use later for blobs.
> 
> ```text
> Large file storage
> Durable attachments
> S3-compatible asset storage
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Recommended architecture by phase
> 
> ## Phase 1 — local spine
> 
> ```text
> Frontend: React/Vite
> Backend: FastAPI
> DB: SQLite
> Files: local data/files
> AI: mock services
> Search: SQLite full-text later if easy
> Queue: none
> Vector: none
> Graph: none
> ```
> 
> Goal:
> 
> - capture
> - QiBits
> - drafts
> - approvals
> - timeline
> - actions
> - context dock
> - basic reports
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phase 2 — smarter local AI
> 
> ```text
> DB: SQLite
> Files: local
> Embeddings: local or OpenAI
> Vector: Qdrant local Docker OR SQLite vector extension if simple
> AI: OpenAI/local Ollama hybrid
> ```
> 
> Goal:
> 
> - similar QiBits
> - similar days
> - knowledge retrieval
> - Ask QiLife with real context
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phase 3 — QiServer deployment
> 
> ```text
> DB: Postgres
> Files: /srv/qilife/data/files
> Vector: Qdrant
> Queue: Redis
> Workers: OCR/AI/background jobs
> Backend: FastAPI
> Frontend: deployed web app
> Access: Tailscale/Cloudflare Zero Trust
> ```
> 
> Goal:
> 
> - reliable private copilot backend
> - background ingestion
> - scheduled daily/weekly reports
> - real AI retrieval
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Phase 4 — advanced intelligence
> 
> ```text
> Postgres + Qdrant + Redis
> Optional Neo4j mirror
> Optional R2/MinIO blob storage
> Markdown/QiNexus exports
> ```
> 
> Goal:
> 
> - pattern engine
> - similar day comparisons
> - graph insights
> - recurring loop detection
> - reports
> - evidence packets
> - life analytics
> 
> ---
> 
> # The “glory backend” model
> 
> Here is the real backend map:
> 
> ```text
> Capture Sources
> ├── app text/dictation
> ├── file upload
> ├── watched folder later
> ├── mobile shortcut later
> ├── email import later
> ├── screenshots later
> └── voice notes later
> 
> Ingestion Layer
> ├── ingestion_items
> ├── uploaded_files
> ├── text_extractions
> ├── OCR/transcription jobs
> └── processing status
> 
> Agent Layer
> ├── classify
> ├── interpret
> ├── retrieve context
> ├── correlate similar records
> ├── draft QiBits/actions/money/knowledge
> ├── generate reports
> └── bubble insights
> 
> Review Layer
> ├── ai_drafts
> ├── approval queue
> ├── review_events
> ├── trust_rules
> └── confidence learning
> 
> Official Memory
> ├── qibits
> ├── timeline/activity_log
> ├── threads
> ├── actions
> ├── people
> ├── transactions
> ├── obligations
> ├── documents
> ├── knowledge_items
> ├── reports
> └── insights
> 
> Retrieval Layer
> ├── SQL filters
> ├── full-text search
> ├── links
> ├── tags
> ├── Qdrant embeddings
> └── optional Neo4j graph
> 
> Storage Layer
> ├── SQLite/Postgres
> ├── local files/R2/MinIO
> ├── backups
> └── Markdown exports
> ```
> 
> That is the full machine.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What I’d tell Codex now
> 
> Add this to the docs before overbuilding:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife infrastructure doctrine:
> 
> V1 should use SQLite and local file storage.
> 
> Do not add Qdrant, Neo4j, Redis, Supabase, or object storage in Phase 1.
> 
> Design service boundaries so these can be added later:
> 
> - Postgres as future structured source of truth.
> - Qdrant as future semantic memory/vector store.
> - Redis as future job queue/cache.
> - Neo4j as optional future graph mirror.
> - Cloudflare R2 or MinIO as future blob storage.
> - QiNexus Markdown exports as human-readable archive.
> 
> The app must separate:
> - structured records
> - raw files/blobs
> - extracted text
> - embeddings
> - AI drafts
> - official approved records
> - exports/backups
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # My final recommendation
> 
> ## Start with this:
> 
> ```text
> React/Vite
> FastAPI
> SQLite
> Local files
> Mock AI
> Alembic
> Markdown/JSON exports
> ```
> 
> ## Design for this:
> 
> ```text
> Postgres
> Qdrant
> Redis
> Local/R2 blob storage
> Optional Neo4j
> ```
> 
> ## Do not start with this:
> 
> ```text
> Supabase + Neo4j + Qdrant + Redis + R2 + Postgres all at once
> ```
> 
> That is not architecture. That is summoning a maintenance demon.
> 
> The correct path:
> 
> **SQLite proves the model.  
> Postgres stabilizes the server.  
> Qdrant gives semantic memory.  
> Redis runs background jobs.  
> Blob storage holds assets.  
> Neo4j becomes optional graph analytics.  
> QiNexus exports keep it human-owned.**

### User
> I don’t want us doing mvp1 then 2 then etc it never works. We need the goal and structure from day one but build it in and order that each day we add functionality for dopamine hits and progress without drifting then having to rematch or reorganize the repo because we forgot the end goal.

### Assistant
> Yes. Exactly. “MVP 1, MVP 2, maybe someday the real thing” is how apps become Frankensteined nonsense.
> 
> We need **full-destination architecture from day one**, but build it as **thin vertical slices** that produce daily wins.
> 
> Not:
> 
> > build tiny fake app now, replace it later
> 
> But:
> 
> > build the final app skeleton now, then activate one working artery at a time
> 
> That is the right doctrine.
> 
> # The build philosophy
> 
> ## Full Skeleton, Incremental Organs
> 
> Day one repo should already know the final system shape:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife
> ├── Agent Layer
> ├── Capture Layer
> ├── Ingestion Layer
> ├── Review Layer
> ├── Memory Layer
> ├── Retrieval Layer
> ├── Insight Layer
> ├── Cockpit Layer
> ├── Export Layer
> └── Infrastructure Layer
> ```
> 
> Even if some pieces are stubs, their **folders, interfaces, data contracts, docs, and boundaries exist** from the start.
> 
> That prevents drift.
> 
> Then each day we add one real capability.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The build rule
> 
> ## No throwaway MVPs.
> 
> Instead:
> 
> # North Star Scaffold + Daily Vertical Slices
> 
> A daily slice must touch the real architecture:
> 
> ```text
> UI → API → service → database → activity log → context/retrieval hook
> ```
> 
> Even if it is simple.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ## Bad build
> 
> “Make a temporary task page.”
> 
> No. That becomes trash.
> 
> ## Good build
> 
> “Create Action through the real capture/review path, store it in the real `actions` table, link it to the source QiBit, log the activity, show it in Today.”
> 
> That is progress without future rework.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What Codex needs to hear
> 
> We need to amend the build instructions hard:
> 
> ```text
> Do not build throwaway MVP screens.
> Do not create temporary models that will be replaced.
> Do not build isolated CRUD pages disconnected from the agent/capture architecture.
> Use the final repo structure and final domain model from day one.
> Features may be incomplete, but boundaries must be correct.
> ```
> 
> That’s the line.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final architecture from day one
> 
> The repo should be laid out like the final app, even if some modules are placeholders.
> 
> ```text
> _qilife/
> ├── frontend/
> │   └── src/
> │       ├── app/
> │       ├── shell/
> │       ├── cockpit/
> │       ├── capture/
> │       ├── ingestion/
> │       ├── review/
> │       ├── agent/
> │       ├── qibits/
> │       ├── timeline/
> │       ├── buckets/
> │       ├── threads/
> │       ├── actions/
> │       ├── calendar/
> │       ├── people/
> │       ├── money/
> │       ├── knowledge/
> │       ├── documents/
> │       ├── insights/
> │       ├── reports/
> │       ├── context_dock/
> │       ├── settings/
> │       └── shared/
> │
> ├── backend/
> │   └── app/
> │       ├── main.py
> │       ├── core/
> │       ├── db/
> │       ├── models/
> │       ├── schemas/
> │       ├── api/
> │       ├── services/
> │       │   ├── capture/
> │       │   ├── ingestion/
> │       │   ├── extraction/
> │       │   ├── agent/
> │       │   ├── review/
> │       │   ├── qibits/
> │       │   ├── timeline/
> │       │   ├── actions/
> │       │   ├── retrieval/
> │       │   ├── insights/
> │       │   ├── reports/
> │       │   ├── knowledge/
> │       │   ├── activity/
> │       │   └── exports/
> │       └── workers/
> │
> ├── data/
> │   ├── db/
> │   ├── files/
> │   ├── exports/
> │   ├── backups/
> │   └── indexes/
> │
> ├── docs/
> ├── planning/
> ├── scripts/
> └── tests/
> ```
> 
> This means when we later add Qdrant, Redis, OCR, report generation, or QiNexus exports, the repo already has a home for it. No “where the hell do I put this?” tax.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Database from day one
> 
> Same principle.
> 
> Do not only create today’s tiny tables if we already know the domain.
> 
> Create the **real core schema**, even if some screens are not wired yet.
> 
> ## Core tables from day one
> 
> ```text
> Core Memory
> ├── qibits
> ├── buckets
> ├── threads
> ├── actions
> ├── action_steps
> ├── people
> ├── transactions
> ├── obligations
> ├── knowledge_items
> ├── documents
> ├── events
> ├── links
> ├── activity_log
> └── daily_summaries
> 
> Ingestion / Agent
> ├── ingestion_items
> ├── uploaded_files
> ├── text_extractions
> ├── ai_drafts
> ├── review_events
> ├── trust_rules
> ├── agent_sessions
> ├── agent_messages
> ├── ai_outputs
> └── retrieval_runs
> 
> Insights / Reports
> ├── insights
> ├── reports
> ├── similarity_matches
> └── patterns
> ```
> 
> We do **not** need full UI for all of these immediately.
> 
> But the schema should know the endgame.
> 
> That prevents us from later saying, “Oh no, we forgot ingestion,” or “Oh no, we need agent sessions,” and ripping open the backend.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Daily dopamine build strategy
> 
> Instead of MVP phases, use **daily capability slices**.
> 
> Each day ends with something visible and useful.
> 
> ## Day 1 — App boots + final skeleton exists
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > QiLife opens. It looks like the cockpit. Left nav, center workspace, Context Dock, and “What happened?” capture bar exist.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - repo skeleton
> - frontend shell
> - backend shell
> - SQLite connection
> - buckets seeded
> - health endpoint
> - README run commands
> 
> No fake app. Real skeleton.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 2 — Capture creates real ingestion record
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > You type “Zai owes me $40 for gas,” save it, and it appears in the Capture/Inbox pipeline.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - `ingestion_items`
> - capture endpoint
> - capture UI
> - activity log entry
> - Inbox view
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 3 — Mock AI drafts from capture
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > QiLife analyzes a messy note and produces draft QiBit/action suggestions.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - `ai_drafts`
> - mock agent service
> - draft cards
> - draft review page
> 
> No real AI required yet. The flow matters.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 4 — Approve draft → official QiBit
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > You approve a draft and it becomes a real QiBit on the Timeline.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - qibit creation from approved draft
> - review events
> - links to ingestion item
> - timeline display
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 5 — Action + steps from QiBit
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > The same capture creates an action with steps, visible in Today.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - actions
> - action_steps
> - approve action draft
> - Today action section
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 6 — Threads and buckets become useful
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > Captures start grouping under “Lyft Income Sprint” or “Surplus Check Recovery.”
> 
> Build:
> 
> - threads
> - bucket views
> - thread detail
> - link QiBits/actions to threads
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 7 — Context Dock becomes real
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > Open a QiBit and the side panel shows related thread, actions, knowledge, and activity.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - links retrieval
> - Context Dock data loading
> - related records cards
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 8 — Knowledge items next to work
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > Add a rule/knowledge note and see it beside the relevant thread/action.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - knowledge_items
> - markdown display
> - link knowledge to bucket/thread/QiBit
> - central Knowledge page
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 9 — Agent sessions / daily brain dump
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > You talk/type about your day and QiLife stores it as an agent session, then drafts a report.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - agent_sessions
> - agent_messages
> - mock daily check-in analyzer
> - draft report
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Day 10 — Daily report and open loops
> 
> Dopamine hit:
> 
> > QiLife shows “what happened today” and what is unresolved.
> 
> Build:
> 
> - daily_summaries
> - activity-based report
> - open loops view
> - draft action plan
> 
> ---
> 
> # That is not MVP. That is progressive activation.
> 
> Every day adds functionality without changing the target.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Build doctrine document to add
> 
> Add this to the repo:
> 
> ```text
> docs/10_product/04_build_doctrine.md
> ```
> 
> Content:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife is not built as disposable MVP phases.
> 
> QiLife uses North Star Scaffold + Daily Vertical Slices.
> 
> The full architecture, repo boundaries, data model, and domain language exist from day one.
> 
> Features are activated incrementally through thin vertical slices that touch the real architecture:
> UI → API → service → database → activity log → context/retrieval hook.
> 
> Do not create temporary models, temporary screens, or isolated CRUD workflows that will be replaced later.
> 
> Every feature must preserve:
> - QiBit-first provenance
> - capture/ingestion path
> - timeline visibility
> - activity logging
> - Context Dock readiness
> - future AI/retrieval compatibility
> ```
>

>

> Important build doctrine update:
> 
> Do not build QiLife as throwaway MVP phases.

> Do not add real AI yet.

> Do create the service boundaries for retrieval/insights/reports/agent.
> ```
