> ---
> 
> # The real build order
> 
> Not MVP phases. Use **activation order**:
> 
> ```text
> 0. Final skeleton / repo boundaries
> 1. Capture pipeline
> 2. Draft review pipeline
> 3. QiBit timeline
> 4. Actions + steps
> 5. Threads + buckets
> 6. Context Dock
> 7. Knowledge beside work
> 8. Daily copilot brief
> 9. Agent sessions
> 10. Similarity/retrieval hooks
> 11. Money/obligations
> 12. Documents/extraction
> 13. Insights/reports
> 14. Real AI
> 15. Qdrant/Redis/Postgres server upgrade
> ```
> 
> Each step is a real slice of the final app.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What the app should avoid
> 
> No:
> 
> - temporary todo model
> - isolated note app
> - fake folders that later become metadata
> - manual-only CRUD first
> - separate wiki first
> - “we’ll add AI later” architecture
> - Supabase-first just because it’s easy
> - graph database before we have records
> - embeddings before clean source data
> - “pretty dashboard” before ingestion works
> 
> Because the backend glory is the product.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final answer
> 
> You’re right.
> 
> We need **end-state architecture now**, built in **daily dopamine slices**.
> 
> The app should be scaffolded as the full AI Life Copilot from day one, but each day we activate one real pipeline through the final system.
> 
> The first real pipeline is:
> 
> ```text
> Capture
> → Ingestion
> → Mock Agent Draft
> → Review
> → Approve
> → QiBit
> → Timeline
> → Activity Log
> → Context Dock placeholder
> ```
> 
> That gives immediate progress without architectural debt.
> 
> That’s the way we build this without losing the plot.

### User
> Eventually qilife will replace access, wiki, ollamaUi, firefly, and many more so we should keep that in mind. Now here’s to the elegant in the room. We have hundreds of tables in supabase with valuable data already do we scratch tables, try to migrate or start with a clean project and migrate as needed.

### Assistant
> Yes. Keep the endgame in mind: **QiLife eventually becomes the cockpit that absorbs/replaces QiAccess, wiki, Ollama UI, Firefly-ish money tracking, dashboards, knowledge, and automation control.**
> 
> But the elephant: **you already have hundreds of Supabase tables with valuable data.**
> 
> Blunt answer:
> 
> # Do not migrate everything. Do not scratch everything. Start clean, then harvest.
> 
> The winning move is:
> 
> ## **Clean QiLife core + legacy data bridge + selective migration**
> 
> Not:
> 
> - “reuse all old tables” — that drags chaos forward.
> - “delete everything and start fresh” — that throws away value.
> - “migrate everything now” — that creates a swamp migration before the app even exists.
> 
> The doctrine should be:
> 
> > **QiLife gets a clean canonical schema. Existing Supabase data becomes legacy source material that is inspected, mapped, imported, or archived as needed.**
> 
> ---
> 
> # The correct model
> 
> ```text
> Old Supabase tables
>         ↓
> Legacy Intake / Staging Layer
>         ↓
> Mapping + Deduping + AI Classification
>         ↓
> QiLife Canonical Schema
>         ↓
> Timeline / QiBits / Threads / Actions / Knowledge / Money
> ```
> 
> That protects the new system while still respecting the value of the old data.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Three buckets for existing Supabase data
> 
> Every existing table should fall into one of these categories:
> 
> ## 1. Migrate into QiLife canonical tables
> 
> Only if the data directly maps to QiLife’s core objects:
> 
> - people
> - notes
> - tasks
> - projects
> - transactions
> - documents metadata
> - knowledge records
> - calendar/events
> - logs
> - client/project records worth keeping
> 
> Example:
> 
> Old `contacts`, `clients`, `users`, `people` tables → QiLife `people`.
> 
> Old task tables → QiLife `actions`.
> 
> Old notes/logs → QiLife `qibits`, `notes`, or `knowledge_items`.
> 
> Old finance rows → QiLife `transactions` or `obligations`.
> 
> ## 2. Import as raw legacy QiBits
> 
> If the data is useful but messy, don’t force it into perfect structure.
> 
> Import it as:
> 
> ```text
> QiBit Type: legacy_import
> Bucket: probably 100 Data / 900 Archive / relevant domain
> Thread: Legacy Supabase Import
> Raw Capture: original row JSON/text
> Summary: AI-generated later
> Status: reference / needs_review
> ```
> 
> This keeps it searchable and retrievable without over-normalizing immediately.
> 
> ## 3. Archive untouched
> 
> Some tables should not migrate at all.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - old experiments
> - duplicate schemas
> - abandoned app tables
> - auth/session junk
> - temporary test tables
> - obsolete sync artifacts
> - generated logs you don’t need
> - Supabase internal/platform tables
> 
> Those go into archive/export, not QiLife core.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What not to do
> 
> Do **not** let the existing Supabase schema dictate QiLife’s design.
> 
> That would be backwards.
> 
> QiLife is the future canonical model.
> 
> Supabase is legacy inventory.
> 
> Harsh but true: hundreds of tables usually means **schema drift, experiments, and tool archaeology**. Valuable? Yes. Clean? Probably not, babe.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The canonical QiLife schema stays clean
> 
> QiLife should not inherit table names like:
> 
> ```text
> client_notes_v2
> tasks_backup_old
> finance_test_new
> documents_final_final
> ```
> 
> No.
> 
> QiLife gets:
> 
> ```text
> qibits
> ingestion_items
> ai_drafts
> review_events
> threads
> actions
> action_steps
> people
> transactions
> obligations
> documents
> knowledge_items
> events
> links
> activity_log
> daily_summaries
> agent_sessions
> agent_messages
> insights
> reports
> ```
> 
> Old data maps into that.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Migration strategy
> 
> ## Step 1 — Freeze old Supabase as read-only
> 
> Do not keep actively building on the old schema.
> 
> Treat it as:
> 
> ```text
> legacy_source
> ```
> 
> You can still query/export from it, but stop expanding it.
> 
> ## Step 2 — Create inventory
> 
> Make an inventory of every Supabase table:
> 
> ```text
> table_name
> row_count
> columns
> created/updated fields
> sample rows
> likely purpose
> keep/migrate/archive decision
> target QiLife object
> risk notes
> ```
> 
> This becomes the migration map.
> 
> ## Step 3 — Export legacy data safely
> 
> Before touching anything:
> 
> ```text
> supabase_legacy_export/
> ├── schema.sql
> ├── table_inventory.csv
> ├── tables/
> │   ├── table_a.csv
> │   ├── table_b.csv
> │   └── ...
> └── samples/
> ```
> 
> Also keep JSON exports for messy tables.
> 
> ## Step 4 — Build QiLife import staging
> 
> Add these tables:
> 
> ```text
> legacy_sources
> legacy_tables
> legacy_records
> legacy_mappings
> legacy_import_runs
> ```
> 
> This lets QiLife ingest old data without pretending it is clean yet.
> 
> ## Step 5 — Selective migration
> 
> Migrate only high-value categories first:
> 
> 1. People/entities
> 2. Notes/logs
> 3. Tasks/projects
> 4. Finance/transactions
> 5. Documents metadata
> 6. Knowledge/reference
> 
> Everything else waits.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Add this to the architecture
> 
> ## Legacy staging tables
> 
> ### `legacy_sources`
> 
> ```text
> legacy_sources
> ├── id
> ├── name
> ├── source_type
> ├── connection_label
> ├── exported_at
> ├── notes
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> name: Old Supabase QiApps
> source_type: supabase_export
> ```
> 
> ### `legacy_tables`
> 
> ```text
> legacy_tables
> ├── id
> ├── legacy_source_id
> ├── table_name
> ├── row_count
> ├── column_summary_json
> ├── likely_domain
> ├── migration_decision
> ├── target_model
> ├── notes
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Migration decisions:
> 
> ```text
> migrate
> import_as_qibits
> archive_only
> ignore
> needs_review
> ```
> 
> ### `legacy_records`
> 
> ```text
> legacy_records
> ├── id
> ├── legacy_table_id
> ├── source_primary_key
> ├── raw_json
> ├── extracted_text
> ├── import_status
> ├── target_record_type
> ├── target_record_id
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ### `legacy_mappings`
> 
> ```text
> legacy_mappings
> ├── id
> ├── legacy_table_id
> ├── source_field
> ├── target_model
> ├── target_field
> ├── transform_rule
> ├── confidence
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ### `legacy_import_runs`
> 
> ```text
> legacy_import_runs
> ├── id
> ├── legacy_source_id
> ├── run_status
> ├── started_at
> ├── completed_at
> ├── records_seen
> ├── records_imported
> ├── records_failed
> ├── notes
> └── created_at
> ```
> 
> This gives you a real migration system, not one giant “oops all data” import.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Best path for Supabase specifically
> 
> ## Do not connect QiLife directly to old Supabase tables as live core
> 
> That creates tight coupling.
> 
> Instead:
> 
> ```text
> Supabase export → legacy staging → QiLife import
> ```
> 
> Later, if some Supabase project is still active, we can build a sync connector. But not first.
> 
> ## Use old Supabase as a source, not the source of truth
> 
> This matters.
> 
> QiLife should answer:
> 
> > What does this mean in my current life system?
> 
> Not:
> 
> > How do I preserve old database chaos forever?
> 
> ---
> 
> # Where this fits with replacing other tools
> 
> QiLife eventually replaces tools by absorbing their **capability**, not necessarily their old schema.
> 
> | Old Tool/System | QiLife Replacement |
> |---|---|
> | QiAccess | cockpit/navigation/service launcher inside QiLife |
> | Wiki.js | Knowledge + Context Dock |
> | Ollama UI/OpenWebUI | Ask QiLife / Agent cockpit |
> | Firefly | Money + transactions + obligations + reports |
> | Notion-ish notes | QiBits + Knowledge + Timeline |
> | Task app | Actions + Steps + Threads |
> | Calendar tools | Events + time slotting |
> | Dashboard/homepage | Cockpit + Today + Insights |
> | File chaos | Documents + metadata + exports |
> 
> So yes, QiLife can replace many things — but only if the **canonical model stays clean**.
> 
> ---
> 
> # My recommendation
> 
> ## Start clean
> 
> Create QiLife’s schema from the final architecture.
> 
> ## Preserve old data
> 
> Export old Supabase fully. Do not delete.
> 
> ## Import selectively
> 
> Use a legacy migration layer.
> 
> ## Prioritize high-value records
> 
> Do not migrate hundreds of tables blindly.
> 
> ## Keep old data searchable
> 
> Even messy old rows can become `legacy_import` QiBits or archived JSON.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Decision record to add
> 
> Create:
> 
> ```text
> docs/90_decisions/0006_clean_core_with_legacy_bridge.md
> ```
> 
> Content:
> 
> ```text
> Status: Accepted
> 
> Context:
> QiLife will eventually replace or absorb functionality from QiAccess, Wiki.js, Ollama/OpenWebUI, Firefly-like finance tracking, and other tools. Existing Supabase projects contain hundreds of tables with valuable but inconsistent legacy data.
> 
> Decision:
> QiLife will use a clean canonical schema from day one. Existing Supabase data will not dictate the QiLife schema. Legacy data will be exported, inventoried, staged, mapped, and selectively migrated through a legacy bridge.
> 
> Consequences:
> - QiLife avoids inheriting schema drift.
> - Valuable old data is preserved.
> - Migration can happen gradually.
> - Legacy records can be imported as raw QiBits when structure is unclear.
> - Supabase remains a legacy source, not the new source of truth.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Prompt for IDE/Codex
> 
> Give this to the IDE before coding too far:
> 
> ```text
> Add a legacy data migration doctrine to QiLife.
> 
> Create:
> 
> docs/90_decisions/0006_clean_core_with_legacy_bridge.md
> docs/30_data_model/07_legacy_data_bridge.md
> docs/70_deployment/03_legacy_supabase_export_plan.md
> 
> Doctrine:
> QiLife will use a clean canonical schema from day one. Existing Supabase tables are valuable legacy data, but they must not dictate the QiLife schema.
> 
> Legacy strategy:
> 1. Preserve/export Supabase first.
> 2. Inventory all tables.
> 3. Classify each table as migrate, import_as_qibits, archive_only, ignore, or needs_review.
> 4. Stage legacy rows in legacy_* tables.
> 5. Map high-value data into QiLife canonical tables.
> 6. Keep messy/unclear records as raw legacy QiBits.
> 7. Do not directly couple QiLife runtime to old Supabase tables.
> 
> Add these planned staging tables to the data model docs:
> - legacy_sources
> - legacy_tables
> - legacy_records
> - legacy_mappings
> - legacy_import_runs
> 
> Also update the build doctrine to say:
> QiLife may eventually replace QiAccess, Wiki.js, Ollama/OpenWebUI, Firefly-like finance tracking, dashboards, and other systems, but it must absorb capabilities through the canonical model rather than inheriting old schemas.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final call
> 
> Do **not** scratch old Supabase.
> 
> Do **not** migrate it all.
> 
> Do **not** build QiLife on top of it.
> 
> Build QiLife clean, export Supabase, stage the old data, and migrate only what earns its way into the new system.
> 
> That is how we preserve value without dragging the haunted furniture into the new house.

### User
> Now the rhino in the room, blob storage and local dev. I don’t want to manage that manually I want my app to house in settings or the variables, drive folder, Local Dev Folder, server connection, db sync,

### Assistant
> Yep. That is the **rhino**, and it’s not optional.
> 
> If QiLife is going to become the cockpit for your life, it cannot have “go manually edit `.env` files and move blobs like a peasant” as the operating model.
> 
> The app needs a **Storage + Sync Control Center** from day one.
> 
> # QiLife needs a Settings-backed Infrastructure Registry
> 
> Not random config files. Not hardcoded paths. Not “remember where the Drive folder is.”
> 
> QiLife should have a settings area that knows:
> 
> ```text
> Storage / Sync Settings
> ├── Local Dev Folder
> ├── Local Data Folder
> ├── Local Blob/File Folder
> ├── Drive/QiNexus Folder
> ├── Server Connection
> ├── Database Mode
> ├── Sync Mode
> ├── Backup Mode
> ├── Export Mode
> ├── AI Provider Settings
> ├── Vector/Index Settings
> └── Health Checks
> ```
> 
> This becomes the **control panel for the backend**.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Core doctrine
> 
> ## The app should manage locations
> 
> You should not manage them manually.
> 
> QiLife should store and validate:
> 
> - where local files live
> - where uploads/blobs live
> - where exports go
> - where Drive/QiNexus mirror is
> - where SQLite DB lives
> - where server API lives
> - whether sync is local-only, manual, or server-backed
> - whether backups are current
> - whether folders are reachable
> 
> This should be in-app settings **and** config files for portability.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Best model: Config DB + `.env` + settings UI
> 
> Use three layers.
> 
> ## 1. `.env`
> 
> For bootstrapping only.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> QILIFE_ENV=local
> QILIFE_DATA_ROOT=C:\QiLifeData
> QILIFE_DB_URL=sqlite:///C:/QiLifeData/db/qilife.sqlite
> QILIFE_CONFIG_PATH=C:\QiLifeData\config\qilife.config.json
> ```
> 
> This gets the app started.
> 
> ## 2. `app_settings` table
> 
> For runtime settings.
> 
> ```text
> app_settings
> ├── id
> ├── key
> ├── value_json
> ├── value_type
> ├── scope
> ├── is_secret
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ## 3. Settings UI
> 
> For you.
> 
> Pages:
> 
> ```text
> Settings
> ├── Storage
> ├── Sync
> ├── Server
> ├── Database
> ├── Backups
> ├── AI
> ├── Indexes
> └── Health
> ```
> 
> That’s the clean structure.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Storage locations
> 
> QiLife should know these paths:
> 
> ```text
> Storage Registry
> ├── local_dev_root
> │   └── C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife
> │
> ├── local_data_root
> │   └── C:\QiLifeData
> │
> ├── local_blob_root
> │   └── C:\QiLifeData\files
> │
> ├── local_db_path
> │   └── C:\QiLifeData\db\qilife.sqlite
> │
> ├── drive_root
> │   └── G:\My Drive\QiNexus or configured path
> │
> ├── drive_export_root
> │   └── QiNexus\990_system\qilife or similar
> │
> ├── backup_root
> │   └── C:\QiLifeData\backups
> │
> ├── server_base_url
> │   └── https://qilife.your-private-domain or Tailscale URL
> │
> └── server_blob_root
>     └── /srv/qilife/data/files
> ```
> 
> Do not hardcode these. Store them as settings.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Blob storage model
> 
> Do **not** start with fancy cloud blob storage.
> 
> Start with:
> 
> ```text
> Local Filesystem Blob Store
> ```
> 
> Then design the interface so it can later swap to:
> 
> - QiServer local filesystem
> - Cloudflare R2
> - MinIO
> - Backblaze B2
> - Google Drive export/mirror
> 
> ## Important distinction
> 
> ### Blob store
> 
> Where app files actually live.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - uploads
> - PDFs
> - screenshots
> - images
> - audio
> - processed OCR files
> - thumbnails
> 
> ### Export/mirror
> 
> Where human-readable copies go.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> - Drive/QiNexus Markdown exports
> - evidence packets
> - backups
> - JSON/CSV exports
> 
> Google Drive should probably be an **export/mirror**, not the live blob store at first.
> 
> Why? Drive sync can be weird, slow, and conflict-prone. Great archive. Risky as the live app file engine.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Storage provider abstraction
> 
> Build a storage service interface from day one.
> 
> ```text
> StorageProvider
> ├── local_filesystem
> ├── server_filesystem
> ├── drive_export
> ├── s3_compatible_later
> └── disabled/mock
> ```
> 
> In code, never write files directly from random modules.
> 
> Use:
> 
> ```text
> storage_service.save_file()
> storage_service.get_file()
> storage_service.delete_file()
> storage_service.compute_hash()
> storage_service.get_public_or_private_path()
> ```
> 
> That prevents future chaos.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Suggested local data folder
> 
> Use something outside the repo:
> 
> ```text
> C:\QiLifeData
> ```
> 
> Not inside:
> 
> ```text
> C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife\data
> ```
> 
> Why? Because repo data gets messy with Git, accidental commits, huge files, and rebuilds.
> 
> Better:
> 
> ```text
> C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife        = code repo
> C:\QiLifeData                      = local app data
> G:\My Drive\QiNexus\...            = export/archive/mirror
> /srv/qilife/data                   = future server data
> ```
> 
> Repo should contain only:
> 
> - code
> - docs
> - seed scripts
> - config templates
> 
> Actual private life data should live outside the repo.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Local data folder structure
> 
> ```text
> C:\QiLifeData
> ├── config/
> │   ├── qilife.config.json
> │   └── secrets.local.json
> │
> ├── db/
> │   └── qilife.sqlite
> │
> ├── files/
> │   ├── uploads/
> │   │   ├── documents/
> │   │   ├── images/
> │   │   ├── audio/
> │   │   ├── video/
> │   │   └── raw/
> │   │
> │   ├── processed/
> │   │   ├── extracted_text/
> │   │   ├── ocr/
> │   │   ├── thumbnails/
> │   │   └── previews/
> │   │
> │   └── attachments/
> │
> ├── indexes/
> │   ├── sqlite_fts/
> │   ├── qdrant_later/
> │   └── search_cache/
> │
> ├── exports/
> │   ├── markdown/
> │   ├── json/
> │   ├── csv/
> │   └── evidence_packets/
> │
> ├── backups/
> │   ├── db/
> │   ├── files/
> │   └── full/
> │
> └── logs/
> ```
> 
> That is clean and future-proof.
> 
> ---
>

> 
> # Database tables for this
> 
> Add:
> 
> ## `app_settings`
> 
> ```text
> app_settings
> ├── id
> ├── key
> ├── value_json
> ├── value_type
> ├── scope
> ├── is_secret
> ├── description
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ## `storage_locations`
> 
> ```text
> storage_locations
> ├── id
> ├── key
> ├── label
> ├── provider
> ├── path_or_uri
> ├── purpose
> ├── status
> ├── last_checked_at
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Providers:
> 
> ```text
> local_filesystem
> server_filesystem
> drive_folder
> s3_compatible
> disabled
> ```
> 
> Purposes:
> 
> ```text
> dev_root
> data_root
> db_root
> blob_root
> upload_root
> processed_root
> export_root
> backup_root
> drive_mirror
> server_root
> index_root
> ```
> 
> ## `sync_targets`
> 
> ```text
> sync_targets
> ├── id
> ├── name
> ├── sync_type
> ├── source_location_id
> ├── target_location_id
> ├── mode
> ├── status
> ├── last_run_at
> ├── last_success_at
> ├── config_json
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Sync types:
> 
> ```text
> backup
> export
> mirror
> server_sync
> index_sync
> ```
> 
> ## `sync_runs`
> 
> ```text
> sync_runs
> ├── id
> ├── sync_target_id
> ├── status
> ├── started_at
> ├── completed_at
> ├── files_seen
> ├── files_copied
> ├── records_exported
> ├── errors_json
> └── created_at
> ```
> 
> ## `system_health_checks`
> 
> ```text
> system_health_checks
> ├── id
> ├── check_type
> ├── status
> ├── message
> ├── details_json
> ├── checked_at
> └── created_at
> ```
> 
> This is how the app manages its own infrastructure instead of making you remember everything.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Server future
> 
> When QiLife moves to QiServer:
> 
> ```text
> /srv/qilife
> ├── app/
> ├── data/
> │   ├── db/
> │   ├── files/
> │   ├── exports/
> │   ├── backups/
> │   ├── indexes/
> │   └── logs/
> └── config/
> ```
> 
> For server mode:
> 
> - Postgres becomes DB
> - server filesystem or R2/MinIO becomes blob store
> - Qdrant becomes vector memory
> - Redis becomes queue
> - QiNexus export still exists
> 
> But the app settings should already understand those slots.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What goes in Git vs data storage
> 
> ## Git repo
> 
> ```text
> C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife
> ```
> 
> Contains:
> 
> - source code
> - docs
> - config templates
> - seed scripts
> - migrations
> - tests
> - README
> 
> Does **not** contain:
> 
> - real SQLite DB
> - uploads
> - private files
> - OCR output
> - backups
> - secrets
> - personal exports
> 
> ## Local data
> 
> ```text
> C:\QiLifeData
> ```
> 
> Contains:
> 
> - private database
> - uploaded files
> - processed text
> - exports
> - backups
> - logs
> - indexes
> 
> ## Drive/QiNexus
> 
> Contains:
> 
> - selected exports
> - Markdown knowledge exports
> - evidence packets
> - backup copies
> - human-readable archives
> 
> ---
> 
> # Add to `.gitignore`
> 
> Make sure these are ignored:
> 
> ```text
> .env
> .env.local
> *.sqlite
> *.db
> /data/
> /.local_data/
> /qilife_data/
> C:\QiLifeData
> *.log
> secrets.local.json
> ```
> 
> On Windows `.gitignore` won’t handle absolute paths cleanly, but we can ignore repo-local data folders and make sure actual data is outside repo.
>

> 
> # Build doctrine update
> 
> Add this:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife must manage its own storage and sync configuration through Settings.
> 
> The user should not manually track:
> - local data paths
> - blob storage paths
> - Drive mirror paths
> - server connection settings
> - database mode
> - backup/export/sync status
> 
> The repo is code. The data root is separate. Drive/QiNexus is an export/mirror layer. Server storage is a future provider. Blob storage uses a provider abstraction from day one.
> ```
>

> 
> # Codex prompt addendum
> 
> Give Codex/IDE this:
> 
> ```text
> Add Storage and Sync Control Center doctrine to QiLife.
> 
> Create/update docs:
> 
> docs/20_architecture/05_storage_and_sync_control_center.md
> docs/30_data_model/08_storage_sync_settings.md
> docs/70_deployment/04_local_data_and_blob_storage.md
> docs/90_decisions/0007_app_managed_storage_and_sync.md
> 
> Doctrine:
> QiLife must manage its own storage/sync configuration through Settings. Cody should not manually manage blob paths, Drive mirror paths, local data roots, server URLs, database sync mode, or backup status.
> 
> Decisions:
> 1. Repo code lives at C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife.
> 2. Local private data should live outside the repo, default C:\QiLifeData.
> 3. SQLite DB default path: C:\QiLifeData\db\qilife.sqlite.
> 4. Blob/file storage default root: C:\QiLifeData\files.
> 5. Drive/QiNexus is an export/mirror layer, not the live blob store by default.
> 6. Server storage is a future provider.
> 7. Blob storage must use a storage provider abstraction.
> 8. Settings UI must expose local data root, blob root, Drive mirror folder, server connection, database mode, sync mode, backup/export status, and health checks.
> 9. Use app_settings, storage_locations, sync_targets, sync_runs, and system_health_checks tables.
> 10. Data folders must be created/tested by the app, not manually maintained.
> 11. Actual private data must not be stored in the Git repo.
> 
> Add planned data folders:
> 
> C:\QiLifeData
>   config/
>   db/
>   files/
>   indexes/
>   exports/
>   backups/
>   logs/
> 
> Add planned Settings pages:
> - Storage
> - Sync
> - Server
> - Database
> - Backups
> - AI / Indexes
> - Health
> 
> Also update build doctrine:
> The final architecture scaffold should include services/storage, services/sync, services/health, and settings UI boundaries from day one, even if many providers are placeholders.
> ```
>

> 
> # Final call
> 
> Yes: QiLife must manage this itself.
> 
> You should be able to open Settings and see:
> 
> - where the app data lives
> - where files are stored
> - what Drive folder is linked
> - whether server is connected
> - what database mode is active
> - when last backup/export happened
> - whether indexes are healthy
> - whether sync is working
> 
> That is how this becomes a real operating system instead of another folder mystery.
> 
> **Code repo is not data.  
> Database is structured truth.  
> Blob store holds raw files.  
> Drive is mirror/export.  
> Server is future provider.  
> Settings controls the whole thing.**

### User
> This should eliminate me manually managing files and folders and not knowing what I did or deleting shit I needed

### Assistant
> Yes. That is one of the **main reasons QiLife exists**.
> 
> Not just “organize files better.”
> 
> More like:
> 
> # QiLife becomes the file/folder safety layer
> 
> So you stop having to manually remember:
> 
> - where a file went
> - whether you already saved it
> - what folder it belongs in
> - whether it was imported
> - whether deleting it breaks anything
> - whether it was backed up
> - whether Drive has a copy
> - whether the app knows about it
> - whether the file is evidence, trash, reference, or active work
> 
> Manual folder management is too fragile for your life load. One wrong tired click and boom: mom care folder disappears, legal docs vanish, or financial data gets buried in “misc old stuff.” Absolutely not.
> 
> ## The doctrine
> 
> **Files should be captured by QiLife, tracked by QiLife, stored by QiLife, and exported by QiLife.**
> 
> You should not have to manually sort them into folders first.
> 
> The flow should be:
> 
> ```text
> File arrives
> ↓
> QiLife captures/imports it
> ↓
> QiLife stores it safely
> ↓
> QiLife hashes/dedupes it
> ↓
> QiLife extracts/OCRs text if possible
> ↓
> QiLife links it to QiBits, threads, people, money, legal, etc.
> ↓
> QiLife decides folder/export view later
> ↓
> You can retrieve it by meaning, not by remembering the folder
> ```
> 
> ## The real safety feature
> 
> QiLife needs a **Managed Files Vault**.
> 
> Not a random uploads folder.
> 
> ```text
> Managed Files Vault
> ├── Inbox / Unprocessed
> ├── Active Files
> ├── Linked Evidence
> ├── Processed Text
> ├── Exports
> ├── Backups
> ├── Trash / Quarantine
> └── Integrity Checks
> ```
> 
> But internally, it can store by stable IDs/hashes, not human folder names.
> 
> Example:
> 
> ```text
> C:\QiLifeData\files\objects\
> ├── ab\
> │   └── ab82f...original.pdf
> ├── c4\
> │   └── c4dd3...screenshot.png
> ```
> 
> Then the database knows:
> 
> ```text
> Document:
> title: Order granting release of excess funds
> bucket: 70 Legal
> thread: Surplus Check Recovery
> source_qibit: court order upload
> file_hash: ab82f...
> stored_path: C:\QiLifeData\files\objects\ab\ab82f...pdf
> export_path: 70_legal/surplus_check/documents/order_granting_release.pdf
> status: active_evidence
> ```
> 
> So you don’t depend on folder memory. The database holds the map.
> 
> ## Deleting should be safe
> 
> QiLife should not let files disappear casually.
> 
> Deletion flow should be:
> 
> ```text
> Delete requested
> ↓
> Check links
> ↓
> If linked to records/evidence, warn/block
> ↓
> Move to app trash/quarantine
> ↓
> Keep restore option
> ↓
> Only purge after backup/export or explicit hard-delete
> ```
> 
> Statuses:
> 
> ```text
> active
> unprocessed
> linked
> archived
> quarantined
> deleted_pending_purge
> purged
> ```
> 
> This prevents “I deleted the care folder and now I’m lost” situations.
> 
> ## What Settings should show
> 
> A **Storage Health** page should show:
> 
> ```text
> Storage Health
> ├── Local Data Root: OK
> ├── Database: OK
> ├── File Vault: OK
> ├── Drive Mirror: connected / not connected
> ├── Last Backup: date/time
> ├── Last Export: date/time
> ├── Unprocessed Files: count
> ├── Orphaned DB records: count
> ├── Orphaned files: count
> ├── Duplicate files: count
> ├── Missing linked files: count
> └── Repair / Reindex / Backup Now buttons
> ```
> 
> That gives you confidence instead of folder paranoia.
> 
> ## What this replaces
> 
> This replaces manual habits like:
> 
> - dragging files into folders
> - renaming everything perfectly before saving
> - wondering if a PDF is already uploaded
> - searching Drive manually
> - keeping duplicate “important” copies everywhere
> - deleting things because they “look old”
> - losing context because file names don’t explain why they matter
> 
> QiLife should let you save first, understand second, organize automatically third.
> 
> ## Add this to the build doctrine
> 
> Use this line:
> 
> **QiLife must make manual file/folder management optional, not required. The app owns file intake, tracking, dedupe, linking, backup, export, and safe deletion. Folders are generated views/projections, not the primary source of truth.**
> 
> That is the protective layer.
> 
> ## Tables we need
> 
> Add or strengthen:
> 
> ```text
> documents
> uploaded_files
> file_objects
> file_links
> file_events
> storage_locations
> sync_runs
> system_health_checks
> ```
> 
> ### `file_objects`
> 
> The actual stored blob identity.
> 
> ```text
> file_objects
> ├── id
> ├── file_hash
> ├── original_filename
> ├── stored_filename
> ├── stored_path
> ├── mime_type
> ├── size_bytes
> ├── storage_provider
> ├── storage_location_id
> ├── status
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ### `documents`
> 
> The human/business meaning of the file.
> 
> ```text
> documents
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── document_type
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── source_qibit_id
> ├── file_object_id
> ├── extracted_text_id
> ├── status
> ├── notes
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> One file object can support one or more document records if needed, but usually one-to-one.
> 
> ### `file_events`
> 
> Audit trail.
> 
> ```text
> file_events
> ├── id
> ├── file_object_id
> ├── event_type
> ├── summary
> ├── before_json
> ├── after_json
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Events:
> 
> ```text
> uploaded
> hashed
> deduped
> linked
> renamed_display_title
> exported
> mirrored
> archived
> restore_requested
> deleted_to_trash
> purged
> missing_detected
> repaired
> ```
> 
> ## Final shape
> 
> QiLife should become your **life data intake desk** and **managed file vault**.
> 
> You stop manually managing files as the source of truth.
> 
> Instead:
> 
> ```text
> Capture it
> QiLife stores it
> QiLife understands it
> QiLife links it
> QiLife backs it up
> QiLife exports folder views when needed
> QiLife protects it from accidental deletion
> ```
> 
> That is how we stop the cycle of “I know I had it somewhere” and “did I delete the thing I needed?”
> 
> The app becomes the map, the vault, the assistant, and the safety net.

### User
> So this also effectively replaces paperless so import hashes and such are a must. We are not deduping this thing, it’s dup allergic.

### Assistant
> Exactly. Then we need to stop calling it “document upload” and call it what it really is:
> 
> # QiLife Managed Document Vault
> 
> Yes, this effectively replaces **Paperless** for your personal system over time.
> 
> Not necessarily every advanced Paperless feature on day one, but the core premise:
> 
> - ingest documents
> - hash them
> - OCR/extract text
> - dedupe
> - classify
> - tag/link
> - store safely
> - retrieve by meaning
> - preserve source file
> - prevent accidental loss
> 
> That becomes native QiLife.
> 
> And yes: **dup-allergic** is the correct doctrine.
> 
> Not “we’ll clean duplicates later.”  
> No. The intake system should be allergic at the door.
> 
> ---
> 
> # New doctrine
> 
> **QiLife must treat every incoming file as evidence/data until proven otherwise. It must hash, fingerprint, track, and dedupe before creating duplicate records.**
> 
> A file should not just “upload.”
> 
> It should pass through intake:
> 
> ```text
> File selected
> ↓
> Save to temporary intake
> ↓
> Compute hash
> ↓
> Check existing hashes
> ↓
> If duplicate: link existing file, do not store another blob
> ↓
> If new: store as file_object
> ↓
> Extract/OCR text
> ↓
> Create document draft
> ↓
> AI classifies and links
> ↓
> Cody approves/edit
> ↓
> Document becomes official
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Critical distinction
> 
> ## File Object
> 
> The actual blob.
> 
> Hash-based. Immutable-ish.
> 
> Example:
> 
> `file_objects`
> 
> ```text
> file_hash: ab82f...
> stored_path: C:\QiLifeData\files\objects\ab\ab82f....pdf
> mime_type: application/pdf
> size_bytes: 483920
> ```
> 
> ## Document Record
> 
> The meaning/context of that file.
> 
> Example:
> 
> `documents`
> 
> ```text
> title: Order granting release of excess funds
> bucket: 70 Legal
> thread: Surplus Check Recovery
> document_type: court_order
> file_object_id: ab82f...
> status: active_evidence
> ```
> 
> One physical file object. Multiple possible contextual links. No duplicate blob chaos.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Hashing rules
> 
> Use multiple identifiers:
> 
> ```text
> file_objects
> ├── sha256_hash
> ├── perceptual_hash
> ├── normalized_text_hash
> ├── original_filename
> ├── size_bytes
> ├── mime_type
> └── created_at
> ```
> 
> ## Why multiple hashes?
> 
> ### SHA-256
> 
> Catches exact duplicate file.
> 
> Same PDF/image/file bytes = duplicate.
> 
> ### Normalized text hash
> 
> Catches “same document, different PDF wrapper.”
> 
> Example: scanned PDF re-exported, metadata changed, but text is basically the same.
> 
> ### Perceptual hash
> 
> For images/screenshots.
> 
> Catches visually similar images, resized screenshots, slightly compressed copies.
> 
> This is how it becomes **dup allergic**, not merely “exact file duplicate aware.”
> 
> ---
> 
> # Dedup levels
> 
> QiLife should distinguish:
> 
> ## 1. Exact duplicate
> 
> Same SHA-256.
> 
> Action:
> 
> > Do not store new blob. Link existing file object.
> 
> ## 2. Text duplicate
> 
> Different file, same extracted normalized text.
> 
> Action:
> 
> > Store as possible duplicate or variant, ask user.
> 
> ## 3. Visual duplicate
> 
> Different image bytes, same/similar perceptual hash.
> 
> Action:
> 
> > Flag as likely duplicate.
> 
> ## 4. Near duplicate
> 
> AI/text similarity says “this appears to be the same document.”
> 
> Action:
> 
> > Review required.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Dedup behavior
> 
> When duplicate detected:
> 
> ```text
> Duplicate Found
> ├── Existing file
> ├── Existing document records
> ├── Existing links
> ├── Existing OCR text
> ├── Existing thread/bucket
> └── Options
>     ├── Link to existing
>     ├── Save as new version
>     ├── Save as separate related document
>     └── Ignore duplicate
> ```
> 
> Default should be:
> 
> > **Link existing, don’t duplicate.**
> 
> Unless user says it is a new version.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Add versioning
> 
> This matters.
> 
> Some docs are not duplicates. They are versions.
> 
> Example:
> 
> - lease draft
> - final signed lease
> - revised medical summary
> - updated court order
> - bank statement corrected copy
> 
> So add:
> 
> ```text
> document_versions
> ├── id
> ├── document_id
> ├── file_object_id
> ├── version_label
> ├── version_number
> ├── change_note
> ├── is_current
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Then QiLife can say:
> 
> > “This looks similar to an existing document. Is this a duplicate or a new version?”
> 
> That is safe.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Paperless replacement capability map
> 
> | Paperless-ish Need | QiLife Native Equivalent |
> |---|---|
> | document intake | ingestion_items + uploaded_files |
> | file storage | file_objects |
> | OCR | text_extractions |
> | dedupe | hashes + duplicate detection |
> | correspondents | people/entities |
> | tags | tags + links |
> | document types | document_type |
> | custom fields | metadata_json |
> | archive serial/location | bucket/thread/context |
> | full text search | extracted text + FTS + future vectors |
> | workflows | AI drafts + review events |
> | audit/history | file_events + activity_log |
> | storage path templates | export projections |
> 
> The difference is QiLife links docs directly to life context, not just a document inbox.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Required tables
> 
> Add these to the schema:
> 
> ```text
> file_objects
> document_versions
> file_events
> duplicate_candidates
> ```
> 
> ## `file_objects`
> 
> ```text
> file_objects
> ├── id
> ├── sha256_hash
> ├── perceptual_hash
> ├── normalized_text_hash
> ├── original_filename
> ├── stored_filename
> ├── stored_path
> ├── mime_type
> ├── size_bytes
> ├── storage_provider
> ├── storage_location_id
> ├── status
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ## `documents`
> 
> ```text
> documents
> ├── id
> ├── title
> ├── document_type
> ├── bucket_code
> ├── thread_id
> ├── source_qibit_id
> ├── current_file_object_id
> ├── extracted_text_id
> ├── status
> ├── notes
> ├── tags_json
> ├── metadata_json
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ## `document_versions`
> 
> ```text
> document_versions
> ├── id
> ├── document_id
> ├── file_object_id
> ├── version_number
> ├── version_label
> ├── change_note
> ├── is_current
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ## `duplicate_candidates`
> 
> ```text
> duplicate_candidates
> ├── id
> ├── incoming_file_object_id
> ├── existing_file_object_id
> ├── duplicate_type
> ├── confidence
> ├── status
> ├── review_note
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Duplicate types:
> 
> ```text
> exact_hash
> text_hash
> perceptual_hash
> semantic_match
> manual_match
> ```
> 
> Statuses:
> 
> ```text
> pending_review
> confirmed_duplicate
> confirmed_version
> confirmed_distinct
> ignored
> ```
> 
> ## `file_events`
> 
> ```text
> file_events
> ├── id
> ├── file_object_id
> ├── event_type
> ├── summary
> ├── before_json
> ├── after_json
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Intake rules
> 
> ## File intake should always do this
> 
> ```text
> 1. Store original file safely.
> 2. Compute SHA-256.
> 3. Check exact duplicate.
> 4. If duplicate exists, avoid storing duplicate blob.
> 5. Extract text if possible.
> 6. Compute normalized text hash.
> 7. Compute perceptual hash for images.
> 8. Create duplicate candidate if needed.
> 9. Create document draft.
> 10. AI classifies document.
> 11. User approves/link/version decision.
> ```
> 
> For v1, full OCR can be placeholder, but the table and statuses must exist.
> 
> ---
> 
> # File statuses
> 
> ```text
> intake_pending
> hashing
> duplicate_detected
> stored
> text_extraction_pending
> text_extracted
> ocr_pending
> ocr_failed
> linked
> archived
> quarantined
> deleted_pending_purge
> purged
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Search/retrieval requirement
> 
> Document retrieval should use:
> 
> ```text
> metadata
> file hash
> OCR/extracted text
> document title
> thread links
> bucket
> people/entities
> tags
> QiBits
> AI summary
> future embeddings
> ```
> 
> That way you don’t need to remember filenames.
> 
> You can ask:
> 
> > “Find the court order about excess funds.”
> 
> Or:
> 
> > “Show the medical PDF from the May visit.”
> 
> Or:
> 
> > “What documents are linked to Mom’s care thread?”
> 
> That is the point.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Add to Codex/IDE prompt
> 
> Give it this doctrine:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife should eventually replace Paperless-style document intake for Cody.
> 
> Add Managed Document Vault doctrine:
> - files must be hashed on intake
> - duplicate prevention is required
> - folders are not the source of truth
> - physical folders are export projections
> - the database stores metadata and relationships
> - file blobs are stored through a storage provider
> - documents link to QiBits, threads, people, money, actions, and knowledge
> - exact duplicates should not create duplicate blobs
> - near duplicates should create duplicate_candidates for review
> - document versions should be supported
> 
> Add planned tables:
> - file_objects
> - document_versions
> - file_events
> - duplicate_candidates
> 
> Update:
> - docs/30_data_model/00_data_model_spine.md
> - docs/30_data_model/08_storage_sync_settings.md
> - docs/20_architecture/05_storage_and_sync_control_center.md
> - docs/90_decisions/0007_app_managed_storage_and_sync.md
> 
> Add new decision record:
> docs/90_decisions/0008_managed_document_vault_dup_allergic.md
> 
> Decision:
> QiLife will be dup-allergic. File intake must hash, track, dedupe, and link files before creating duplicate blobs. QiLife replaces manual folder management and eventually replaces Paperless-style document intake by making documents part of the QiBit/timeline/thread/knowledge system.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final call
> 
> Yes: **QiLife replaces Paperless eventually.**
> 
> But better, because Paperless stores documents.
> 
> QiLife stores documents **inside your life context**.
> 
> A PDF is not just a PDF.
> 
> It is:
> 
> - what happened
> - why it matters
> - who it involves
> - what thread it belongs to
> - what action it triggers
> - what evidence it supports
> - what knowledge it updates
> - how to retrieve it later
> 
> And the file layer must be **dup-allergic by design**.

### User
> So what’s the final verdict

### Assistant
> Final verdict:
> 
> # Build QiLife clean, agent-first, with the full end-state skeleton from day one.
> 
> Do **not** build a tiny throwaway MVP.  
> Do **not** migrate old Supabase wholesale.  
> Do **not** make folders the source of truth.  
> Do **not** make this “just a task app with AI.”
> 
> QiLife is:
> 
> ## **An AI Life Copilot with a Personal LifeDesk cockpit**
> 
> Its job:
> 
> > Capture what happens, structure it, connect it, retrieve context, draft actions/reports/insights, protect files, prevent duplicates, and keep Cody oriented with minimal manual organizing.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The final architecture doctrine
> 
> ## 1. Agent-first, app-second
> 
> The app is the cockpit.
> 
> The **agent** is the real product.
> 
> You should be able to brain dump:
> 
> > “Today was chaos. Mom needed meds, Zai still owes gas money, I’m short for the rental, and I need to drive.”
> 
> And QiLife should correlate it, extract QiBits, find similar days, draft actions, update obligations, generate a brief, and ask for approval where needed.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. QiBit is the atomic unit
> 
> Everything starts as or links back to a **QiBit**.
> 
> A QiBit is one captured unit of life data:
> 
> - note
> - task seed
> - document
> - receipt
> - text
> - problem
> - obligation
> - decision
> - event
> - reflection
> - file
> - conversation
> - insight
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Timeline is the spine
> 
> Timeline answers:
> 
> > What happened?
> 
> Everything goes onto the timeline:
> 
> - captures
> - actions
> - approvals
> - files
> - money
> - reports
> - insights
> - resolutions
> - reflections
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. Capture is the highest-priority workflow
> 
> This app lives or dies by ingestion.
> 
> Flow:
> 
> ```text
> Something happens
> → New Capture
> → text / dictation / file upload
> → save raw input
> → extract/OCR text
> → AI drafts metadata + records
> → Cody approves/edits/rejects
> → official records created
> → timeline/activity updated
> → future retrieval works
> ```
> 
> Raw capture is sacred. AI interpretation is draft until trusted/approved.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. Build the full scaffold now, activate daily slices
> 
> No “MVP 1, 2, 3” nonsense.
> 
> Use:
> 
> # North Star Scaffold + Daily Vertical Slices
> 
> The repo should know the final shape from day one:
> 
> ```text
> capture
> ingestion
> review
> agent
> qibits
> timeline
> buckets
> threads
> actions
> calendar
> people
> money
> knowledge
> documents
> insights
> reports
> retrieval
> context_dock
> storage
> sync
> exports
> settings
> ```
> 
> Then each day we activate one real pipeline.
> 
> First real slice:
> 
> ```text
> Capture
> → Ingestion
> → Mock AI Draft
> → Review
> → Approve
> → QiBit
> → Timeline
> → Activity Log
> → Context Dock placeholder
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. Database: SQLite now, Postgres later
> 
> Use **SQLite first** because this is single-user, local-first, portable, and low-friction.
> 
> But design cleanly for future Postgres.
> 
> Use:
> 
> - stable IDs, preferably ULID
> - migrations from day one
> - raw vs interpreted data separation
> - links table
> - activity log
> - daily summaries
> - AI outputs separate
> - review events
> - trust rules
> - soft deletion
> - amount_cents for money
> - file metadata in DB, blobs on disk
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 7. Old Supabase data: preserve, don’t inherit
> 
> Do **not** build QiLife on top of old Supabase tables.
> 
> Do **not** migrate hundreds of tables blindly.
> 
> Correct approach:
> 
> ```text
> Clean QiLife canonical schema
> + legacy Supabase export
> + inventory
> + staging tables
> + selective migration
> + import messy rows as legacy QiBits when useful
> ```
> 
> Old Supabase is a **legacy source**, not the source of truth.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 8. Files: QiLife becomes the managed vault
> 
> This replaces manual folder management and eventually Paperless-style document intake.
> 
> File flow:
> 
> ```text
> Upload/import file
> → hash it
> → dedupe it
> → extract/OCR text
> → classify it
> → link it
> → store safely
> → prevent accidental deletion
> → export folder views later
> ```
> 
> QiLife must be **dup-allergic**.
> 
> Add:
> 
> - `file_objects`
> - `documents`
> - `document_versions`
> - `duplicate_candidates`
> - `file_events`
> - `text_extractions`
> 
> Exact duplicates should not create duplicate blobs. Near duplicates should be flagged for review.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 9. Folders are views
> 
> Inside QiLife:
> 
> > Buckets are metadata.
> 
> Physical folders are only export projections.
> 
> So:
> 
> ```text
> Database = source of truth
> Blob store = actual files
> Buckets = views
> QiNexus folders = exports/mirrors
> ```
> 
> No more manually dragging files around and accidentally deleting important stuff.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 10. Settings must manage infrastructure
> 
> QiLife needs a **Storage + Sync Control Center**.
> 
> The app should manage:
> 
> - local data folder
> - blob/file root
> - SQLite DB path
> - Drive/QiNexus mirror folder
> - server URL
> - database mode
> - backup status
> - sync status
> - storage health
> - AI/index settings
> 
> Default:
> 
> ```text
> Code repo: C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife
> Private data: C:\QiLifeData
> SQLite DB: C:\QiLifeData\db\qilife.sqlite
> Files: C:\QiLifeData\files
> Exports/backups: C:\QiLifeData\exports and backups
> Drive/QiNexus: mirror/export, not live blob store
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Stack verdict
> 
> ## Start with
> 
> ```text
> React + Vite + TypeScript
> FastAPI
> SQLite
> Local file storage
> Mock AI service
> Markdown rendering
> Alembic migrations
> ```
> 
> ## Design for later
> 
> ```text
> Postgres = server source of truth
> Qdrant = semantic memory / similar days
> Redis = queues/background jobs
> R2 or MinIO = blob storage later
> Neo4j = optional graph mirror
> QiNexus = Markdown/export/archive layer
> ```
> 
> ## Do not start with
> 
> ```text
> Supabase + Qdrant + Neo4j + Redis + R2 + Postgres all at once
> ```
> 
> That’s not architecture. That’s a maintenance demon with a login screen.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What QiLife eventually replaces
> 
> Over time, QiLife can absorb the capabilities of:
> 
> - QiAccess
> - Wiki.js
> - Paperless
> - Ollama/OpenWebUI-style chat UI
> - Firefly-style money tracking
> - task apps
> - scattered notes
> - document folders
> - daily logs
> - dashboards
> 
> But it should absorb them through the **QiLife canonical model**, not by inheriting every old schema.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final build instruction
> 
> Tell Codex/IDE:
> 
> > Build the final scaffold now. Activate the capture-to-QiBit pipeline first. Do not build throwaway screens. Do not drift into CRUD-first app design. QiLife is agent-first, capture-first, timeline-backed, dup-allergic, storage-managed, and built around structured retrieval.
> 
> That’s the verdict.
> 
> **QiLife is not another app. It is the operating cockpit for your life data.**

### User
> how do i make this part of qlife but be able to give access to my mom too without access to all my stuff.

### Assistant
> Yes — this becomes **QiLife with a shared-access layer**, not a separate app.
> 
> The clean answer:
> 
> # QiLife stays private. Mom gets a scoped portal.
> 
> You do **not** give your mom access to “QiLife.”  
> You give her access to a **limited Care Space** inside QiLife.
> 
> Think:
> 
> ```text
> QiLife Core
> ├── Cody Private Cockpit
> ├── Personal LifeDesk
> ├── Full QiBit Timeline
> ├── Money / Legal / Tech / Private Notes
> └── Shared Spaces
>     └── Mom Care Space
> ```
> 
> Mom only sees what is explicitly inside or shared to **Mom Care Space**.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The model: Spaces + Permissions
> 
> Add a top-level concept:
> 
> ## Space
> 
> A **Space** is a scoped area of access.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> ```text
> Spaces
> ├── Cody Private
> ├── Mom Care
> ├── Household
> ├── Client / One-Off Work
> └── Public / Shared Export later
> ```
> 
> Every QiBit, note, task, document, knowledge item, or calendar item has:
> 
> ```text
> space_id
> visibility
> access_policy
> ```
> 
> Default should be:
> 
> ```text
> space = Cody Private
> visibility = private
> ```
> 
> Nothing is shared unless you intentionally share it.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Mom gets access to this
> 
> Her portal should be lightweight, based on her actual note habits: small buckets, simple date/time notes, medicine/treatment/grocery/info/prayer/etc., not a medical-charting monster. The uploaded note-transcript summary specifically points to buckets like Cody, dates, glucose level, medicine/pills, grocery list, immunizations, Tylenol, breathing treatments, doctor excuses, prayer, care notes, and info, and warns not to overbuild this into an EMR-style system. fileciteturn0file0
> 
> So Mom Care Space can include:
> 
> ```text
> Mom Care Space
> ├── Dashboard
> ├── Care Notes
> ├── Grocery / Supplies
> ├── Med / Treatment Notes
> ├── Appointments
> ├── Documents shared with Mom
> ├── Simple Tasks
> ├── Announcements
> └── Prayer / Personal Notes if she wants
> ```
> 
> Not:
> 
> ```text
> Cody Legal
> Cody Finance
> QiLife build notes
> Zai obligations unless shared
> Private daily logs
> Raw emotional brain dumps
> Sensitive documents
> Full AI memory
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Permission levels
> 
> Keep this simple.
> 
> ```text
> Access Roles
> ├── Owner
> │   └── Cody: everything
> ├── Contributor
> │   └── can add/edit within assigned space
> ├── Viewer
> │   └── can view assigned space
> └── Guest
>     └── very limited/shared links later
> ```
> 
> For Mom:
> 
> ```text
> Mom = Contributor in Mom Care Space
> ```
> 
> Optional safer version:
> 
> ```text
> Mom = Contributor for Care Notes + Grocery
> Mom = Viewer for Appointments/Documents
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # The key safety rule
> 
> ## Sharing is explicit.
> 
> A record can be shared in three ways:
> 
> ```text
> Share Modes
> ├── private
> ├── shared_to_space
> ├── shared_to_person
> └── public_link later
> ```
> 
> Default:
> 
> ```text
> private
> ```
> 
> So if you create a QiBit about Mom but it contains your private frustration, the system should not automatically show it to her.
> 
> Instead, the AI can suggest:
> 
> > “This relates to Mom Care. Share a cleaned care note version?”
> 
> That is the right move.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Very important: private vs shared versions
> 
> Sometimes you need two records:
> 
> ## Private QiBit
> 
> Raw reality:
> 
> > “Mom texted again and I’m overwhelmed.”
> 
> ## Shared Care Note
> 
> Clean operational version:
> 
> > “Medication question needs review. Confirm pickup/status.”
> 
> Same situation, different audience.
> 
> So QiLife needs:
> 
> ```text
> private_source_qibit_id
> shared_summary_id
> ```
> 
> This lets the system preserve your raw truth while creating a safe, useful shared version.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Database additions
> 
> Add these tables/concepts:
> 
> ```text
> spaces
> space_members
> record_visibility
> share_events
> ```
> 
> ## `spaces`
> 
> ```text
> spaces
> ├── id
> ├── name
> ├── space_type
> ├── description
> ├── owner_person_id
> ├── default_visibility
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Types:
> 
> ```text
> private
> care
> household
> client
> public_export
> system
> ```
> 
> ## `space_members`
> 
> ```text
> space_members
> ├── id
> ├── space_id
> ├── person_id
> ├── role
> ├── status
> ├── invited_at
> ├── accepted_at
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> Roles:
> 
> ```text
> owner
> contributor
> viewer
> guest
> ```
> 
> ## Add to core records
> 
> For shared-aware records:
> 
> ```text
> space_id
> visibility
> created_by_person_id
> ```
> 
> Visibility:
> 
> ```text
> private
> space_visible
> restricted
> archived
> ```
> 
> ## `share_events`
> 
> ```text
> share_events
> ├── id
> ├── record_type
> ├── record_id
> ├── shared_from_space_id
> ├── shared_to_space_id
> ├── shared_to_person_id
> ├── shared_by_person_id
> ├── share_mode
> ├── summary
> ├── created_at
> └── updated_at
> ```
> 
> This gives you an audit trail.
> 
> ---
> 
> # UI structure
> 
> ## Cody view
> 
> Full cockpit:
> 
> ```text
> Cody QiLife
> ├── Cockpit
> ├── Capture
> ├── Timeline
> ├── Draft Queue
> ├── Threads
> ├── Actions
> ├── People
> ├── Money
> ├── Knowledge
> ├── Documents
> ├── Spaces
> └── Settings
> ```
> 
> ## Mom view
> 
> Simple portal:
> 
> ```text
> Mom Care Space
> ├── Today
> ├── Add Note
> ├── Care Notes
> ├── Grocery / Supplies
> ├── Appointments
> ├── Documents
> └── Settings / Help
> ```
> 
> No overwhelming left nav. No full timeline. No private context dock.
> 
> ---
> 
> # How capture works with Mom access
> 
> When you capture something, QiLife asks/suggests:
> 
> ```text
> Where should this go?
> ├── Cody Private
> ├── Mom Care
> ├── Household
> └── Other
> ```
> 
> But default is **Cody Private**.
> 
> If AI detects it is care-related, it can draft:
> 
> ```text
> Private QiBit:
> Raw capture preserved privately.
> 
> Shared Care Note:
> Clean version for Mom Care Space.
> 
> Suggested Action:
> Add task/check item.
> ```
> 
> You approve before sharing.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Feature toggles still matter
> 
> For Mom, use adoption presets:
> 
> ```text
> Simple Mode
> ├── Dashboard
> ├── Tasks
> ├── Grocery/Supplies
> └── Announcements
> 
> Care Mode
> ├── People
> ├── Care Notes
> ├── Appointments
> └── Documents
> 
> Full Mode
> ├── Calendar
> ├── Meals
> ├── Budget
> ├── Advanced Care Notes
> └── Transcript Import
> ```
> 
> The uploaded transcript-derived design note explicitly recommends feature toggles and adoption modes so the household can adopt gradually, with Care Notes starting off lightweight and optional. fileciteturn0file0
> 
> ---
> 
> # Authentication without overbuilding
> 
> Eventually you need login. Keep it simple:
> 
> ## For now/local dev
> 
> ```text
> single-user Cody
> mock Mom account / demo switcher
> ```
> 
> ## Later/private server
> 
> Use one of:
> 
> ```text
> Email magic link
> Passcode invite
> Cloudflare Zero Trust
> Tailscale-only access
> ```
> 
> For Mom, I’d avoid complicated account setup. Use:
> 
> ```text
> Mom portal link + simple passcode
> ```
> 
> or Cloudflare Access if she can handle it.
> 
> But the internal model should already support:
> 
> ```text
> person
> space
> role
> visibility
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # The blunt architecture answer
> 
> Do **not** split this into a separate Family Hub database.
> 
> Make **Family Hub / Mom Care** a **Space inside QiLife**.
> 
> But keep the UI separate and simple.
> 
> ```text
> Same backend
> Same canonical records
> Different access scope
> Different interface
> Different permissions
> ```
> 
> That means:
> 
> - you maintain one system
> - Mom doesn’t see your private stuff
> - shared care notes live in the same life model
> - documents/tasks/appointments can be linked without duplication
> - AI can help create clean shared summaries
> - you can revoke/hide access later
> 
> ---
> 
> # Codex/IDE addendum
> 
> Give this to Codex before it locks the schema:
> 
> ```text
> Add multi-space scoped access design to QiLife.
> 
> QiLife is private-first, but must support limited shared spaces such as Mom Care without exposing Cody’s full data.
> 
> Doctrine:
> - Cody Private is the default space.
> - Nothing is shared by default.
> - Shared access happens through Spaces.
> - Mom Care is a scoped space/portal, not a separate app.
> - The same backend can power Cody’s full cockpit and Mom’s simplified portal.
> - Mom should only see records explicitly assigned/shared to Mom Care.
> - Private raw QiBits can generate cleaned shared notes, but raw private content must remain private unless Cody approves sharing.
> 
> Add planned tables:
> - spaces
> - space_members
> - share_events
> 
> Add fields to major records:
> - space_id
> - visibility
> - created_by_person_id
> 
> Visibility values:
> - private
> - space_visible
> - restricted
> - archived
> 
> Roles:
> - owner
> - contributor
> - viewer
> - guest
> 
> Create default spaces:
> - Cody Private
> - Mom Care
> - Household
> 
> UI:
> - Cody sees full QiLife cockpit.
> - Mom Care portal shows simple Dashboard, Add Note, Care Notes, Grocery/Supplies, Appointments, Documents, and Announcements.
> - Do not expose Cody Money, Legal, Tech, private Timeline, raw brain dumps, or full Ask QiLife memory to Mom.
> 
> Add sharing flow:
> - Private QiBit may create a cleaned Shared Care Note draft.
> - Cody approves before sharing.
> - Log share_events.
> 
> Do not build full auth yet.
> For local dev, allow a mock user/space switcher.
> Future auth can use magic link, passcode invite, Cloudflare Access, or Tailscale.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Final verdict
> 
> QiLife stays your private AI cockpit.
> 
> Mom gets a **scoped Mom Care Space** with a simpler interface.
> 
> Same backend. Same canonical model. Different visibility.
> 
> That gives you the shared care functionality without handing anyone the keys to your entire nervous system.

### User
> qilife also what do i tell the ide to update about our approach and all. after what we discusseda bout the focus of the app ingestion ect.

### Assistant
> Yes. Tell the IDE we’ve had a **major architecture correction**:
> 
> QiLife is not app-first. It is **agent-first, ingestion-first, storage-managed, and space-scoped**.
> 
> Here’s the exact IDE prompt.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## IDE Prompt — Update QiLife Doctrine After Architecture Correction
> 
> Paste this into the IDE:
> 
> ```text
> You are working in:
> 
> C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife
> 
> Goal:
> Update the QiLife docs and build approach based on the latest architecture decisions.
> 
> Do not start coding yet unless explicitly instructed after this doc update.
> This is a doctrine/spec correction pass.
> 
> Major correction:
> QiLife is not primarily a manual app with AI features. QiLife is an AI Life Copilot with a Personal LifeDesk cockpit.
> 
> The app UI is the cockpit/control panel.
> The backend/agent is the real product.
> The highest-priority workflow is seamless capture, ingestion, AI drafting, review, approval, structured memory, retrieval, and insight generation.
> 
> Core product sentence:
> QiLife is an AI Life Copilot with a Personal LifeDesk cockpit. It captures what happens, correlates it with structured life memory, drafts insights/actions/reports, protects files, prevents duplicates, and keeps Cody oriented with minimal manual organizing.
> 
> Update the documentation to reflect these doctrines:
> 
> 1. Agent-first, not app-first
> - QiLife should behave like Cody’s AI copilot inside an app.
> - The user should be able to talk/type/brain-dump to QiLife and have it extract QiBits, actions, obligations, reports, insights, and relevant context.
> - Manual CRUD screens are secondary control surfaces, not the primary workflow.
> - The main interaction is: “What happened?” / “Talk to QiLife” / “Handle this.”
> 
> 2. Capture and ingestion are the highest priority
> The first real working pipeline should be:
> 
> Capture
> → Ingestion Item
> → File/Text Extraction
> → Mock AI Draft
> → Draft Review
> → Approval/Edit/Reject
> → Official QiBit/Action/Thread/etc.
> → Timeline
> → Activity Log
> → Context Dock / Retrieval hooks
> 
> Add/update docs to make clear:
> - Raw capture is sacred.
> - AI interpretation is draft until approved or trusted.
> - Approval/edit/rejection must be logged.
> - Future trust rules can auto-approve low-risk guesses.
> - High-risk areas like money, legal, medical/care, deletion, and external messaging require review.
> 
> 3. QiBit remains the atomic unit
> A QiBit is one captured unit of life data.
> Everything important starts as or links back to a QiBit.
> 
> 4. Timeline remains the spine
> Timeline answers “what happened?”
> Every capture, approval, action, file, document, report, insight, and resolution should be timeline-visible.
> 
> 5. Build the full North Star scaffold from day one
> Do not build throwaway MVPs.
> Do not build temporary isolated CRUD pages.
> Do not build manual-only screens that will later need to be replaced.
> 
> Use the doctrine:
> North Star Scaffold + Daily Vertical Slices
> 
> The final repo/module boundaries should exist from day one, even if some are stubs.
> 
> Required module boundaries:
> - capture
> - ingestion
> - extraction
> - review
> - agent
> - qibits
> - timeline
> - buckets
> - threads
> - actions
> - calendar
> - people
> - money
> - knowledge
> - documents
> - insights
> - reports
> - retrieval
> - context_dock
> - storage
> - sync
> - settings
> - exports
> - spaces/access
> 
> Every implemented feature should be a vertical slice through the real architecture:
> UI → API → service → database → activity_log → retrieval/context hook
> 
> 6. Database approach
> Use SQLite for local-first development now, but design for future Postgres on QiServer.
> 
> Use:
> - stable IDs, preferably ULID if straightforward
> - migrations from day one
> - raw vs interpreted data separation
> - activity_log as append-only history
> - daily_summaries for generated/reflected daily summaries
> - links table for relationships
> - ai_outputs, ai_drafts, review_events, trust_rules
> - soft delete/archive fields
> - amount_cents for money
> - file metadata in DB, blobs on disk
> 
> Do not add Qdrant, Redis, Neo4j, Supabase, R2, or MinIO in first code pass.
> Design service boundaries for them later:
> - Postgres = future structured source of truth
> - Qdrant = future semantic memory/similar days
> - Redis = future background jobs
> - Neo4j = optional future graph mirror
> - R2/MinIO = future blob provider
> 
> 7. Supabase legacy doctrine
> QiLife should not inherit old Supabase schema chaos.
> 
> Add/update doctrine:
> - QiLife uses a clean canonical schema.
> - Existing Supabase tables are legacy sources.
> - Preserve/export Supabase data.
> - Inventory tables.
> - Stage legacy rows.
> - Selectively migrate useful records.
> - Import messy useful rows as legacy QiBits.
> - Supabase is not the runtime source of truth.
> 
> Planned legacy bridge tables:
> - legacy_sources
> - legacy_tables
> - legacy_records
> - legacy_mappings
> - legacy_import_runs
> 
> 8. Storage and blob doctrine
> QiLife must eliminate manual file/folder management.
> 
> The app should manage:
> - local data root
> - blob/file root
> - Drive/QiNexus mirror folder
> - server connection
> - database mode
> - sync mode
> - backup/export status
> - storage health
> 
> Default locations:
> - Repo/code: C:\QiLabs\60_QiApps\_qilife
> - Private data: C:\QiLifeData
> - SQLite DB: C:\QiLifeData\db\qilife.sqlite
> - File vault: C:\QiLifeData\files
> - Exports/backups: C:\QiLifeData\exports and C:\QiLifeData\backups
> - Drive/QiNexus: export/mirror layer, not live blob store by default
> 
> Add/update doctrine:
> - Code repo is not data.
> - Database is structured truth.
> - Blob store holds raw files.
> - Drive/QiNexus is mirror/export/archive.
> - Folders are projections of metadata, not the source of truth.
> - Buckets are metadata/views inside QiLife.
> 
> Add planned tables:
> - app_settings
> - storage_locations
> - sync_targets
> - sync_runs
> - system_health_checks
> 
> 9. Managed Document Vault / Paperless replacement doctrine
> QiLife eventually replaces Paperless-style intake.
> 
> Add/update doctrine:
> - QiLife is dup-allergic.
> - Every incoming file must be hashed.
> - Exact duplicates should not create duplicate blobs.
> - Near duplicates should be flagged for review.
> - Files should be stored as managed file objects.
> - Documents are meaning/context records linked to file objects.
> - Support document versions.
> - File deletion should be safe, logged, and restorable before purge.
> 
> Add planned tables:
> - file_objects
> - documents
> - document_versions
> - duplicate_candidates
> - file_events
> - text_extractions
> 
> File intake flow:
> File upload
> → temporary intake
> → hash
> → duplicate check
> → store or link existing file_object
> → extract/OCR text if possible
> → AI document draft
> → approval/link/version decision
> → official document record
> → timeline/activity log
> 
> 10. Spaces / access doctrine
> QiLife is Cody-private by default but must support scoped shared spaces.
> 
> Add/update doctrine:
> - Cody Private is the default space.
> - Nothing is shared by default.
> - Mom Care is a scoped shared space/portal, not a separate app.
> - Same backend, different access scope and UI.
> - Mom should only see records explicitly assigned/shared to Mom Care.
> - Private raw QiBits can generate cleaned shared Care Notes, but Cody must approve sharing.
> 
> Add planned tables:
> - spaces
> - space_members
> - share_events
> 
> Add planned fields to major records:
> - space_id
> - visibility
> - created_by_person_id
> 
> Default spaces:
> - Cody Private
> - Mom Care
> - Household
> 
> Visibility values:
> - private
> - space_visible
> - restricted
> - archived
> 
> Roles:
> - owner
> - contributor
> - viewer
> - guest
> 
> For local dev:
> - use mock user/space switcher
> - no full auth yet
> 
> 11. Mom Care / Care Notes doctrine
> Mom Care is a lightweight add-on/space, not a clinical EMR.
> 
> Use mom’s actual note-taking pattern: simple atomic buckets, date/time notes, quick capture, optional archive/delete, gradual adoption.
> 
> Care Notes should support buckets/nodes like:
> - Cody
> - dates
> - glucose level
> - medicine / pills today
> - charts
> - grocery list
> - immunizations
> - Jeep
> - Tylenol
> - breathing treatments
> - doctor excuses
> - prayer
> - care notes
> - info
> 
> Do not design Care Notes as medical charting software.
> Design it as household operational notes.
> 
> This direction is based on the transcript-derived Care Notes summary already in the project context. It emphasizes small note buckets, date/time entries, optional archive/delete, lightweight adoption, and avoiding EMR-style overbuilding.
> 
> 12. Feature toggles/adoption modes
> QiLife should support feature toggles through a central feature registry, not random conditionals.
> 
> Add planned feature registry:
> frontend/src/config/features.ts
> 
> Each feature should define:
> - id
> - label
> - description
> - defaultEnabled
> - navGroup
> - adoptionPreset
> - route
> - icon key if used
> 
> Adoption presets:
> - Simple Mode
> - Care Mode
> - Full Mode
> 
> Toggling a feature off hides it from navigation but does not delete its data.
> 
> 13. Cockpit home screen
> The main home screen should be Cockpit / Today.
> 
> It should eventually include:
> - Copilot Brief
> - Insight Feed
> - Draft Queue
> - Open Loops
> - Similar Patterns placeholder
> - Today’s Actions
> - Waiting On
> - Storage/Sync health warnings if needed
>
